# Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide Ointment 에코나졸질산염·트리암시놀론아세토니드연고  

Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide Ointment contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amounts of econazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{18}H_{15}C_{13}N_{2}O}\cdot\mathrm{HNO_{3}}\,:\,444.70)$ and triamcinolone acetonide $\mathrm{(C_{24}H_{31}F O_{6}:434.49)}$ ).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Ointments, with Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide.  

Identification Weigh an amount of Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide Ointment, equivalent to 10 mg of econazole nitrate ( $\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~}~m g~}$ of triamcinolone acetonide), dissolve in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, use a $0.1\%$ methanol solution of econazole nitrate and a $0.01\%$ methanol solution of triamcinolone acetonide as the standard solutions. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $1~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution onto a thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of toluene, ethanol, ethyl acetate and $85\%$ formic acid $(50:20:20:5)$ ) as the developing solvent, and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (principal wavelength: $254~\mathrm{nm}$ ) or spray evenly with platinic acid iodide-potassium iodide TS; the colors and $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Assay (1) Econazole nitrate —Weigh accurately an amount of Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide Ointment equivalent to about $40~\mathrm{mg}$ of econazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{18}H_{15}C_{13}N_{20}{\cdot}H N O_{3})}$ according to the labeled amount, add a mixture of methanol and water $(40:60)$ to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $40~\mathrm{mg}$ of econazole nitrate RS, add a mixture of methanol and water $(40:60)$ to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the econazole nitrate standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas of econazole nitrate, $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , for each solution.  

Amount (mg) of econazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{18}H_{15}C_{13}N_{20}{\cdot}H N O_{3})}$ $=$ Amount (mg) of econazole nitrate $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}$  

Operating conditions   
Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $10~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $3~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $35\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  
Mobile phase: Control the mixing ratio of mobile phase A and mobile phase B stepwise or via the gradient elution as follows.   
Mobile phase A: Dissolve $0.77\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of ammonium acetate in water to make $1000~\mathrm{{mL}}$ . Add $200~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol to $800\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution.  

Mobile phase B: A mixture of acetonitrile and methanol $(60:40)$ .  

![](images/491ae876a24370199fb4162a538cc08feabb9a9aa573751a40154f654d7e086e.jpg)  

Flow rate: $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the symmetry factor is NMT 1.5.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 5 times with $10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak areas of Piroxicam is NMT $0.73\%$ .  

(2) Triamcinolone acetonide —Weigh accurately an amount of Econazole Nitrate and Triamcinolone Acetonide Ointment equivalent to about $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of triamcinolone acetonide $\left({\bf C}_{24}\mathrm{H}_{31}\mathrm{FO}_{6}\right)$ according to the labeled amount, add methanol to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{~mg}$ of triamcinolone acetonide RS and add methanol to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Take $10.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add methanol to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following operating conditions, and determine the peak areas of triamcinolone acetonide, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , for each solution.  

Amount (mg) of triamcinolone acetonide $\left({\bf C}_{24}{\bf H}_{31}{\bf F}{\bf O}_{6}\right)$ $=$ Amount (mg) of triamcinolone acetonide $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\frac{1}{10}$  

decylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (3 to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).   
Mobile phase: A mixture of water, acetonitrile and acetic acid(100) $(59:40:1)$ .  
Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream 에코나졸질산염·트리암시놀론아세토니드·겐타마이신황산염크림  

Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amounts of econazole nitrate $\mathrm{(C_{18}H_{15}C l_{3}N_{2}O}$ $\cdot\mathrm{HNO}_{3}:444.70\rangle$ ) and triamcinolone acetonide $({\bf C}_{24}{\mathrm{H}}_{31}{\mathrm{FO}}_{6}:434.50)$ ), and NMT $90.0\%$ and NLT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of gentamicin sulfate.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Creams, with Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate.  

Identification (1) Econazole nitrate and triamcinolone acetonide —Weigh an amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream equivalent to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of econazole nitrate, dissolve in 10 mL of methanol, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, use a $0.1\%$ methanol solution of econazole nitrate RS and a $0.01\%$ methanol solution of triamcinolone acetonide RS as the standard solutions. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solutions onto a thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of toluene, ethanol, ethyl acetate and $85\%$ formic acid $(55:20:20:5)$ ) as the developing solvent, and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly hexachloroplatinic (IV) acid-potassium iodide TS on the plate and examine under ultraviolet light; the $R_{f}$ values and the colors of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

(2) Gentamicin sulfate —(1) Dissolve $5~\mathrm{g}$ of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, then add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of $\mathfrak{a}$ -naphtholethanol solution (1 in 500). Gently superimpose the solution onto $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of sulfuric acid; a purplish blue color develops at the boundary layer.  

(3) Weigh an amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream equivalent to $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of gentamicin sulfate, add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ of phosphate buffer solution $\ensuremath{\left(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0\right)}$ to make $100~\mathrm{{mL}}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of gentamicin sulfate RS, add $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\ensuremath{\left(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0\right)}$ to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution onto a thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Develop with a mixture of chloroform, methanol and strong ammonia water $(2:1:1)$ as the developing solvent, and air-dry the plate. Place the plate in an appropriate container containing between $2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ and $4\textrm{g}$ of iodine crystals, close the lid, and let stand for 3 to 5 minutes; the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution have the same $R_{f}$ value and color.  

Assay (1) Econazole nitrate —Weigh accurately an amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream equivalent to about $40~\mathrm{mg}$ of econazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{18}H_{15}C_{13}N_{20}{\cdot}H N O_{3})}$ according to the labeled amount, add a mixture of methanol and water $(40:60)$ to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $40\;\mathrm{mg}$ of econazole nitrate RS, add a mixture of methanol and water $(40:60)$ to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas of econazole nitrate from each solution, $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , respectively.  

Amount (mg) of econazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{18}H_{15}C_{13}N_{20}{\cdot}H N O_{3})}$ $=$ Amount (mg) of econazole nitrate $\begin{array}{r}{\mathrm{RS}\!\times\!\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\end{array}$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $10~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $3~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $35\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Control the mixing ratio of mobile phase A and mobile phase B stepwise or via the gradient elution as follows.  

Mobile phase A: Dissolve $0.77\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of ammonium acetate in water to make $1000~\mathrm{{mL}}$ . Add $200~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol to $800\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution.  

Mobile phase B: A mixture of acetonitrile and methanol $(60:40)$ .  

![](images/4c34ecbbc92dd1c49a78e1f7cb988396d54cd9c10614e6ecb329fc959ce85195.jpg)  

Flow rate: $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the symmetry factor is NMT 1.5.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 5 times with $10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak areas of Piroxicam is NMT $0.73\%$ .  

(2) Triamcinolone acetonide —Weigh accurately an amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream equivalent to about $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of triamcinolone acetonide $\left({\bf C}_{24}{\bf H}_{31}{\bf F}{\bf O}_{6}\right)$ , add methanol to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of triamcinolone acetonide RS and add methanol to make 100 mL. Take $10.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add methanol to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas of triamcinolone acetonide, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , in each solution.  

Amount (mg) of triamcinolone acetonide $\left({\bf C}_{24}\mathrm{H}_{31}\mathrm{FO}_{6}\right)$ $=$ Amount $\mathrm{(mg)}$ of triamcinolone acetonide $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\frac{1}{10}$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.0\ \mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $30~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (3 to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of water, acetonitrile and acetic acid(100) $(59:40:1)$ .  

Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

(3) Gentamicin sulfate —(1) (A) Cylinder plate method $\textcircled{1}$ Medium (a) Medium for seed and base layer Peptone $6.0\;\mathrm{g}$ Glucose $1.0\;\mathrm{g}$ Yeast extract $3.0~\mathrm{g}$ Sodium chloride $10.0~\mathrm{g}$ Meat extract 1.5 g Agar $13.0\sim20.0\mathrm{\,g}$ Weigh the above ingredients, add purified water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ after sterilization of the solution so that it will be 7.8 to 8.0.  

(b) Agar medium for transferring test organism: Use the medium in $(\mathrm{A})\mathrm{\rightarrow}\mathcal{\emptyset}$ (b) (ⅱ) $\circledcirc$ under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics.  

$\circled{2}$ Test organism: Use Staphylococcus epidermidi sATCC 12228 as the test organism. $\circled{3}$ Standard solution: Weigh an appropriate amount of gentamicin RS, dry for 3 hours at $110\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ under vacuum (NMT $0.67\ \mathrm{kPa})$ ), then weigh accurately an amount equivalent to $5~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) and dissolve in $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0)$ to prepare a standard stock solution containing $1~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL. Pipet an appropriate amount of this standard stock solution, dilute with the above buffer solution to contain $4.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and $1.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the standard solutions.  

$\circledast$ Test solution: Weigh accurately an amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream equivalent to about $25~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency), dissolve in $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\mathrm{(pH}$ 8.0) to prepare a solution containing $1~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL; pipet an appropriate amount of this solution and dilute with the above buffer solution to contain $4.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and $1.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the test solutions.  

(B) Standard curve method $\textcircled{1}$ Medium: Prepare according to (A) $\textcircled{1}$ under the Microbial assays for antiobiotics.  

$\circled{2}$ Test organism: Follow (A) $\circled{2}$ under Microbial assays for antiobiotics.  

$\circled{3}$ Standard solution: Pipet an appropriate amount of the standard stock solution of (A) $\circled{3}$ under Microbial Assays for Antibiotics, dilute to contain $0.064~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency), $0.080~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency), $0.100~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency), $0.125~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) and $0.156~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\ensuremath{\left(\mathrm{pH\8.0}\right)}$ , and use these solutions as the standard solutions. Prepare a solution containing $0.100~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL and use this as the standard intermediate diluent.  

$\circledast$ Test solution: Pipet an appropriate amount of the solution from (A) $\circled{4}$ under Microbial Assays for Antibiotics, and dilute to contain $0.10~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL with $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\left(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0\right)$ , and use this solution as the test solution.  

(2) Content of gentamicin C1, etc. (liquid chromatography) Weigh an appropriate amount of Econazole Nitrate, Triamcinolone Acetonide and Gentamicin Sulfate Cream and gentamicin RS and dissolve in water to prepare solutions containing $0.65~\mathrm{mg}$ per mL; take $10.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the solution, add $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of isopropanol and $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of $o$ -phthaldehyde, shake to mix, add isopropanol to make 25 mL, warm for 15 minutes on a steam bath at $60\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , cool, and use as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. Using the test solution and the standard solution, perform the test as directed under the Liquid Chromatography under the following conditions, and measure the peak areas of gentamicin $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ ,and $A_{S}$ for each solution (Gentamicin $C_{1};\,25$ to $50\%$ , Gentamicin $\mathrm{{C}_{1a}}$ : 10 to $35\%$ , Gentamicin ${\mathbf{C}}_{2}$ and $\mathrm{C}_{2\mathrm{a}}$ : 25 to $55\%$ ).  

Respective content $(\%)$ of Gentamicin $C_{1}$ , Gentamicin $\mathrm{C_{1a}}$ , Gentamicin $\mathrm{C}_{2\mathrm{a}}$ and Gentamicin ${\mathbf{C}}_{2}$  

$$
=\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times100
$$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $330\,\mathrm{nm})$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $5\,\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $10~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized porous silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 to $10\,\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: Add $250~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100) to $700\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of methanol, shake to mix, and dissolve $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of sodium 1-heptanesulfonate in this solution.  

Flow rate: About $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: K as determined from the Gentamicin ${\bf C}_{1}$ peak is 2 to 7, the number of theoretical plates determined from the Gentamicin ${\bf C}_{2}$ peak is NLT 1200, and the resolution R between the two peaks is NLT 1.25. Test according to the above conditions; Gentamicin ${\mathrm{C}}_{1}$ , Gentamicin $\mathrm{{C_{1a}}}$ , Gentamicin $\mathrm{{C}}_{2\mathrm{{a}}}$ and Gentamicin ${\bf C}_{2}$ are eluted in this order.  

System repeatability: The relative standard deviation for repeatability is NMT 2.0.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Edrophonium Chloride 에드로포늄염화물  

![](images/9e7326b37a8152bb3c7143dd0bec7a709cb3c76f112a08009f8fbb1d81cc82b6.jpg)  

Edrophonium Chloride $\mathrm{C_{10}H_{16}C l N O:201.69}$ $N\!\cdot$ -Ethyl-3-hydroxyN,N -dimethylbenzenaminium chloride [ 116-38-1 ]  

Edrophonium Chloride, when dried, contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of edrophonium chloride (${\mathrm{C}}_{10}{\mathrm{H}}_{16}$ ClN).  

Description Edrophonium Chloride occurs as white crystals or a crystalline powder and is odorless.   
It is very soluble in water, freely soluble in ethanol(99.5) or acetic acid(100), and practically insoluble in acetic anhydride or ether.   
It is hygroscopic.   
It is gradually colored by light.  

Identification (1) To $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of an aqueous solution of Edrophonium Chloride (1 in 100), add one drop of iron(III) chloride TS; the solution exhibits a pale purple color.  

(2) Determine the absorption spectra of the solutions of Edrophonium Chloride and edrophonium chloride RS in $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid (1 in 20000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(3) An aqueous solution of Edrophonium Chloride (1 in 50) responds to the Qualitative Analysis for chloride.  

Melting point Between 166 and $171\ {}^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition).  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $1.0\;\mathrm{g}$ of Edrophonium Chloride in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 3.5 and 5.0.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution —Dissolve $1.0\;\mathrm{g}$ of Edrophonium Chloride in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the solution is clear and colorless.  

(2) Heavy metals— Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Edrophonium Chloride according to Method 1 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 20 ppm).  

(3) Arsenic— Proceed with $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Edrophonium Chloride according to Method 1 and perform the test $(\mathrm{NMT}\ 2\ \mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(4) Related substances —Dissolve about $0.50\mathrm{~g~}$ of Edrophonium Chloride in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethanol(95) and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, and add ethanol(95) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ Pipet $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add ethanol(95) to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thinlayer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of methanol, chloroform and ammonia water(28) $(16:4:1)$ to a distance of about $10~\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Observe the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ); the spots other than the principal spot obtained from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution.  

Loss on drying NMT $0.2\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$ , in vacuum, phosphorus pentoxide, 3 hours).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.2\mathrm{~g~}$ of Edrophonium Chloride, previously dried, dissolve in $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of acetic anhydride and acetic acid(100) $(7:3)$ , and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

![](images/bae5828b6539a7f54f2803017b348b62cd2a26892a3cb19b74f74e99710ad0c2.jpg)  
His Lys Leu Gln Thr Tyr Pro Arg Thr Asp Val Gly Ala Gly Thr Pro NH 2  

Elcatonin $\mathrm{C_{148}H_{244}N_{42}O_{47}}$ : 3363.77 N-{[(3 S,6 S,9 S,12 S)-3-Amino-6-(2-amino-2-   
oxoethyl)-15-[(1 R)-1-hydroxyethyl]-12-   
(hydroxymethyl)-9-isobutyl-4,7,10,13,16,24-   
hexaoxo-1-oxa-5,8,11,14,17-pentaazacyclotetra  
cosan-18-yl]carbonyl}-L-valyl-L-le ucylglycyl-L-lysylL-leucyl-L-seryl-L-glutaminyl-L-α-   
glutamyl-L-leucyl-L-histidyl-L-lysyl-L-leucyl-L  
glutaminyl-L-threonyl-L-tyrosyl-L-prolyl-L-arginyl-Lthreonyl-L-α-aspartyl-L-valylglycyl-L-alanylglycyl-Lthreonyl-L-prolinamide [ 60731-46-6 ]  
Elcatonin contains NLT 5000 and not more 7000 of elcatonin units per mg of peptide, calculated on the anhydrous basis. Description Elcatonin occurs as a white powder.   
It is very soluble in water, freely soluble in ethanol(95), and practically insoluble in acetonitrile.   
It is hygroscopic.   
The $\mathrm{pH}$ of aqueous solution of Elcatonin (1 in 500) is between 4.5 and 7.0.  

Identification Determine the absorption spectra of the solutions of $5~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Elcatonin and elcatonin RS in 5 mL of water, respectively, as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

Constituent amino acids Put about $1~\mathrm{mg}$ of Elcatonin into a test tube for hydrolysis, dissolve in phenolic acid TS, replace the air inside with nitrogen, seal the tube in vacuum, and heat at $110{\pm}2\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 24 hours. After cooling, open the tube, evaporate the hydrolysate to dryness in vacuum, dissolve the residue in about $1\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of 0.02 mol/L hydrochloric acid TS, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately weigh exactly $1.33\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of Laspartic acid, $1.19\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of L-threonine, $1.05\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of Lserine, $1.47~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-glutamic acid, $1.15~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-proline, $0.75~\mathrm{mg}$ of glycine, $0.89~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{L}$ -alanine, $1.17~\mathrm{mg}$ of Lvaline, $1.89~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-2-aminosuberic acid, $1.31~\mathrm{mg}$ of Lleucine, $1.81~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-tyrosine, $1.83~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-lysine hydrochloride, $2.10~\mathrm{mg}$ of L-histidine hydrochloride monohydrate and $2.11\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of L-arginine hydrochloride, dissolve them in $0.02\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions; 14 peaks of amino acids obtained from the test solution appear. Molar ratios of respective constituent amino acids to alanine are as follows: between 1.7 and 2.2 for aspartic acid, between 3.5 and 4.2 for threonine, between 2.4 to 3.0 for serine, between 2.7 and 3.2 for glutamic acid, between 1.7 and 2.2 for proline, between 2.7 and 3.2 for glycine, between 1.6 and 2.2 for valine, between 0.8 and 1.2 for 2-aminosuberic acid, between 4.5 and 5.2 for leucine, between 0.7 and 1.2 for tyrosine, between 1.7 and 2.2 for lysine, between 0.8 and 1.2 for histidine, and between 0.7 and 1.2 for arginine.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: Visible spectrophotometer (wavelengths: $440\;\mathrm{nm}$ and $570\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4\,\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $8~\mathrm{{cm}}$ in length, packed with strongly acidic ion exchange resin for liquid chromatography composed of a sulfonated styrene-divinylbenzene copolymer ( $\ensuremath{3\,\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: Varied between 50 and $65\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .Chemical reaction vessel temperature: A constant temperature of about $130\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .Color developing time: About 1 minute. Mobile phase: Buffer solutions A, B, C and D, with sodium ion concentrations of $0.10\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ ,$0.135\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ $1.26~\mathrm{mol/L}$ and $0.20\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ , respectively; provided that the ion concentration is varied stepwise from $0.10\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ to $1.26\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ with the buffer solutions A, B, C and D.  

![](images/ec81b5faeca8d36bfdf2d3aa0f361a1f0631c4e9fbb5f25789b26d89b3e675be.jpg)  

Reaction reagent: Mix $407\ \mathrm{g}$ of lithium acetate dihydrate, $245\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of acetic acid(100) and $801\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of 1- methoxy-2-propanol, add water to make $2000~\mathrm{mL}$ , stir for about 20 minutes to mix while passing nitrogen, and use this solution as the solution A. Separately, add $77\,\mathrm{\textrm{g}}$ of ninhydrin and $0.134\:\mathrm{g}$ of sodium borohydride to $1957~\mathrm{mL}$ of 1-methoxy-2-propanol, stir for 20 minutes to mix while passing nitrogen, and use this solution as the solution B. Mix the solution A and solution B before use.  

Flow rate of mobile phase: Adjust so that the retention time of arginine is about 75 minutes.  

Flow rate of reaction reagent: About $0.2\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ .Selection of column: Proceed with $10\,\mathrm{\upmuL}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; use a column from which aspartic acid, threonine, serine, glutamic acid, proline, glycine, alanine, valine, 2- aminosuberic acid, leucine, tyrosine, lysine, histidine and arginine are eluted in this order with complete separation of each peak.  

Purity (1) Acetic acid —Weigh accurately about $3~\mathrm{mg}$ to $6~\mathrm{mg}$ of Elcatonin quickly under conditions of $25{\pm}2\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and $50{\pm}5\%$ relative humidity, add exactly $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution to mix, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $0.5\;\mathrm{g}$ of acetic acid(100), and add the internal standard solution to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the resulting solution, add the internal standard solution to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and calculate the peak area ratios, $Q_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $Q_{S}$ , of acetic acid to that of the internal standard; the amount of acetic acid is NMT $7.0\%$ .  

$$
=\frac{Q_{\mathrm{T}}}{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\frac{W_{S T}}{W_{\mathrm{SA}}}\times50
$$  

Internal standard solution —An aqueous solution of citric acid monohydrate (1 in 4000).  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $210\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.0\ \mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $6\;\mathrm{{cm}}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $5\;{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $25~^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $13.2\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of monobasic ammonium phosphate in $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 2.5 with phosphoric acid, and add water to make 1000 Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of acetic acid is about 4 minutes.  

System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; acetic acid and citric acid are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 2.0.  

(2) Related substances —Dissolve $1.0\ \mathrm{~mg~}$ of Elcatonin in $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of trichloroacetic acid and acetonitrile $(2:1)$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $0.3\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the resulting solution, add a mixture of trichloroacetic acid and acetonitrile $(2:1)$ to make 10 mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine each peak area as directed in the automatic integration method; the sum of the peak areas other than elcatonin in the test solution is not greater than the peak area of elcatonin in the standard solution, and each peak area other than elcatonin in the test solution is not greater than one-third of the peak area of elcatonin in the standard solution.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4\,\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of trifluoroacetic acid TS and acetonitrile (change the ratio from $85:15$ to $55:45$ in 30 minutes).  

Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of elcatonin is about 25 minutes.  

# System suitability  

Detection sensitivity: Adjust the detection sensitivity so that the peak height of elcatonin obtained from $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution is between $50\;\mathrm{mm}$ and 200 System performance: Dissolve $2~\mathrm{mg}$ of Elcatonin in $200~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of trypsin TS for test of elcatonin. Warm this solution at $37\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour, and add one drop of acetic acid(100), and heat at $95~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 minute. To $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution, add $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the test solution, and mix it. Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above operating conditions; the resolution between the peak of elcatonin and the peak which is eluted immediately before the peak of elcatonin is NLT 2.0, and the retention time of elcatonin is about 25 minutes.  

Time span of measurement: A range in which the gradient elution appearing on the chromatogram is regularly changing after the solvent peak.  

Water Weigh accurately about 1 to $3~\mathrm{mg}$ of Elcatonin quickly and perform the test as directed under the coulometric titration under the Water; it is NMT $8.0\%$ . It should be weighed under conditions of $25{\pm}2~\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and $50{\pm}5\%$ relative humidity.  

Nitrogen content Weigh accurately 15 to $20\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of Elcatonin quickly under the conditions of $25{\pm}2~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and $50{\pm}5\%$ relative humidity, and perform the test as directed under the Nitrogen Determination; the amount of nitrogen (N: 14.01) is NLT $16.1\%$ and NMT $18.7\%$ , calculated on the anhydrous and residual acetic acid-free basis. Assay (i) Animals: Select healthy male Sprague-Dawley rats each weighing between $90~\mathrm{g}$ and $110~\mathrm{g}$ . Keep the rats for NLT 3 days before use, providing an appropriate uniform diet and water.  

(ii) Solution for elcatonin: Dissolve $2.72{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of sodium acetate trihydrate in water to make $200\;\mathrm{mL}$ , add $0.2\;\mathrm{g}$ of bovine serum albumin, and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 6.0 with acetic acid(100). Prepare before use.  

(iii) Standard solution: Dissolve elcatonin RS in the solution for elcatonin to make two standard solutions: the high-dose standard solution, $S_{\mathrm{H}}$ , containing exactly 0.075 unit in each mL, and the low-dose standard solution, $S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ ,containing exactly 0.0375 unit in each mL.  

(iv) Test solution: Weigh accurately 0.5 to $2.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of Elcatonin quickly under conditions of $25{\pm}2\;\mathrm{~}^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and $50{\pm}5\%$ relative humidity, and dissolve in the solution for elcatonin to make two test solutions: the high-dose test solution, $T_{\mathrm{H}}$ , containing the units per mL equivalent to $S_{\mathrm{H}}$ and the low-dose test solution, $T_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ , containing the units per mL equivalent to $S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ .  

(v) Deproteinizing solution for elcatonin: Dissolve $160\;\mathrm{g}$ of trichloroacetic acid and $30.6~\mathrm{g}$ of strontium chloride in water to make $3600\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

(vi) Procedure: Divide the animals into 4 equal groups of NLT 10 animals each. Withhold all food for 18 to 24 hours before the injections, and also withhold water during the assay until the final blood sample is taken. Handle the animals with care in order to avoid undue excitement.  

Inject exactly $0.2\ \mathrm{mL}$ each of the standard solution and the test solution into the tail vein of each animal as indicated in the following regimen:  

First Group $\mathrm{S_{H}}$ Third Group THSecond Group $\S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ Fourth Group  T LAt 1 hour after the injection, take a sufficient blood sample to perform the test from the carotid vein of each animal under ether anesthesia, centrifuge the blood samples to separate serum, and determine the serum calcium according to the following (G).

Separately, pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of calcium standard solution for the Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy, and add a solution of sodium chloride (17 in 2000) to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . # Elcatonin Injection 엘카토닌주사액  

Elcatonin Injection is an aqueous injection and contains NLT $80.0\%$ and NMT $125.0\%$ of the labeled amount of elcatonin units.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Injections, with Elcatonin.  

Description Elcatonin Injection occurs as a clear, colorless liquid.  

Identification (1) Take $12\ \mathrm{mL}$ of Elcatonin Injection, evaporate to dryness on a steam bath, dissolve in $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of water, and use this solution as the test solution. Add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of alkaline copper TS to the test solution, shake to mix, and allow to stand for 10 minutes.  To this solution, add $0.2~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted Folin TS (1 in 2) and heat on a steam bath for 3 minutes; the solution exhibits a pale blue color. (2) Perform the test with Elcatonin Injection as directed under Assay; the test group exhibits NLT $20\%$ serum calcium reduction compared to the control group. The test animals are divided into 2 groups with 5 animals, respectively: the test group and control group. For the test group, Prepare the test solution by pipetting $0.5\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of Elcatonin Injection and diluting in solution for elcatonin to obtain a solution having known a concentration of 0.1 elcatonin unit per mL. Use a solution for elcatonin vehicle as a control solution. Inject $0.2\ \mathrm{mL}$ of each of these solutions into the tail vein.  

pH Between 5.0 and 6.5. Sterility Meets the requirements. Pyrogen Meets the requirements. The amount tested is $2.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ per kg of the body weight of a test animal.  

Particulate contamination: Visible particles Meets the requirements.  

Insoluble particulate matter in injections Meets the requirements.  

Extractable volume of injections Meets the requirements.  

Assay (1) Animals— Select healthy male SpragueDawley rats each weighing 90 to $110~\mathrm{g}$ . Keep the rats for NLT 3 days before use, providing an appropriate uniform diet and water.  

(2) Solution for elcatonin— Dissolve $2.72{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of sodium acetate trihydrate in water to make $200\;\mathrm{mL}$ , add 0.2 g of bovine serum albumin, and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 6.0 with acetic acid(100). Prepare before use.  

(3) Standard solution— Dissolve elcatonin RS in the solution for elcatonin to prepare solutions containing exactly 0.075 units and 0.0375 units per mL, respectively. Use these solutions as the high-concentration standard solution $S_{\mathrm{H}}$ and the low-concentration standard solution $S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ , respectively.  

(4) Test solution —Pipet $0.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of Elcatonin Injection, add the solution for elcatonin to obtain solutions having known concentration of units equivalent to the high-concentration standard solution $\mathrm{S_{H}}$ and the lowconcentration standard solution $\S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ , and use these solutions as the high-concentration test solution $\mathrm{T_{H}}$ and the low-concentration test solution $\mathrm{T_{L}}$ , respectively.  

(5) Procedure— Divide the test animals into 4 groups of NLT 10 animals each (the same number of animals). Withhold all food for 18 to 24 hours before the injections, and also withhold water during the assay until the final blood sample is taken. Handle the animals with care in order to avoid undue excitement.  

Inject exactly $0.2\ \mathrm{mL}$ each of the standard solutions and the test solutions into the tail vein of each animal as indicated in the following regimen:  

![](images/a2b7401615821d4698d2efae266d04bc44809cb5e3b1ff45629f0e21be04e1c9.jpg)  

At 1 hour after the injection, take a sufficient blood sample to perform the test from the carotid artery and vein of each animal under ether anesthesia, centrifuge the blood samples to separate serum, and determine the serum calcium according to the following (G).  

(6) Serum calcium assay— Pipet $0.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of serum, add the deproteinizing solution for elcatonin to make exactly $5~\mathrm{mL}$ , shake to mix well, centrifuge, and use the clear supernatant as the test solution for calcium assay. Separately, pipet $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of calcium standard solution for atomic absorption spectrophotometry, and add sodium chloride solution (0.85 in 100) to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add deproteinizing solution for elcatonin to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution for calcium assay. Separately, take $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, proceed in the same manner as in preparation of standard solution for calcium assay, and use this solution as the blank test solution. Determine the absorbances, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of the test solution, standard solution and the blank test solution as directed under the Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy according to the following conditions.  

Gas: Air–acetylen   
Lamp: Calcium hollow cathode lamp   
Wavelength: $422.7\;\mathrm{nm}$  

$$
\begin{array}{r}{=0.01\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}-A_{0}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}-A_{0}}\times10\times100}\end{array}
$$  

Deproteinizing solution for elcatonin —Dissolve $160~\mathrm{~g~}$ of trichloroacetic acid and $30.6\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of strontium chloride in water to make $3600~\mathrm{mL}$ .  

(7) Calculation— The amounts of calcium in 100 mL of serum obtained from $\mathrm{S_{H}}$ ,$\S_{\mathrm{{L}}}$ ,$\mathrm{T_{H}}$ and $\mathrm{T_{L}}$ in the serum calcium Assay shall be ${\bf y}_{1},\,{\bf y}_{2},\,{\bf y}_{3}$ and ${\mathrm{y}}_{4}$ , respectively. For each group, add ${\bf y}_{1},\,{\bf y}_{2},\,{\bf y}_{3}$ and ${\mathrm{y}}_{4}$ to make ${\sf Y}_{1}$ ,$\mathbf{Y}_{2}$ ,$\Upsilon_{3}$ and $\mathrm{Y}_{4}$ , respectively.  

Number of elcatonin units per mL of Elcatonin Injection $=$ antilog $M\times$ [Number of elcatonin units in $1\;\mathrm{mL}$ of  the high − concentration standard solution] × $\times\,{\frac{b}{a}}$  

$$
\begin{array}{c}{\mathbf{M}=0.3010\times\frac{\mathbf{Y}_{\mathbf{a}}}{\mathbf{Y}_{\mathbf{b}}}}\\ {\mathbf{Y}_{\mathbf{a}}=\mathbf{\Omega}-\mathbf{\Omega}\mathbf{Y}_{1}\ -\ \mathbf{Y}_{2}+\mathbf{Y}_{3}+\mathbf{Y}_{4}}\\ {\mathbf{Y}_{\mathbf{b}}=\mathbf{Y}_{1}\ -\ \mathbf{Y}_{2}+\mathbf{Y}_{3}\ -\ \mathbf{Y}_{4}}\end{array}
$$  

a: Amount (mL) of sample taken b: Total amount (mL) when elcatonin vehicle is added to the sample to prepare the high-concentration test solution  

$\mathrm{F^{\prime}}$ calculated according to the following equation is less than the $\boldsymbol{\mathrm F}$ in the table for n when $S^{2}$ is calculated. Also, when L $(\mathbf{P}=0.95)$ is calculated according to the following equation, $\mathrm{L}$ is NMT 0.2. If $\boldsymbol{\mathrm{F}}^{\prime}$ exceeds F, or if $\mathrm{L}$ exceeds 0.2, repeat the test, increasing the number of animals or arranging the assay conditions so that $\boldsymbol{\mathrm{F}}^{\prime}$ is NMT F and $\mathrm{L}$ is NMT 0.20.  

$$
\mathrm{F^{\prime}=\frac{(-Y_{1}+Y_{2}+Y_{3}-Y_{4})^{2}}{4f S^{2}}}
$$  

$\operatorname{f}=$ Number of test animals in each group  

$$
S^{2}=\frac{\sum\Upsilon^{2}-\Upsilon/\mathrm{f}}{\mathrm{n}}
$$  

$\Sigma\mathbf{y}^{2}=$ The sum of the squares of ${\mathrm{y}}_{1},{\mathrm{y}}_{2},{\mathrm{y}}_{3}$ and ${\mathrm{y}}_{4}$ of each  

$$
\mathrm{Y}={\mathrm{Y}_{1}}^{2}+{\mathrm{Y}_{2}}^{2}+{\mathrm{Y}_{3}}^{2}+{\mathrm{Y}_{4}}^{2}
$$  

$$
\mathtt{n}=4(f\ -\ 1)
$$  

$$
\begin{array}{c}{{\mathrm{L}=2\sqrt{(C-1)(C M^{2}+0.09062)}}}\\ {{{}}}\\ {{C={\frac{\mathrm{Y}_{\mathrm{b}}^{2}}{\mathrm{Y}_{\mathrm{b}}^{2}-4\mathrm{fs}^{2}\mathrm{t}^{2}}}}}\end{array}
$$  

$\mathrm{t}^{2}$ : The table corresponding to $\mathbf{n}$ in the following table when $\mathrm{s}^{2}$ is calculated.   

![](images/513912c741cd2744f067541a632d25e2be13b857ffd3aac442035222f37d175e.jpg)  

Packaging and storage Preserve in hermetic containers.  

# Enalapril Maleate 에날라프릴말레산염  

![](images/a2784eb14cf5e3ecd8198a8427b6a6bc5ef2718fc136f2de92931c39a49cce1a.jpg)  

$\mathrm{C_{20}H_{28}N_{2}O_{5}{\cdot}C_{4}H_{4}O_{4}:492.52}$ (2S)-1-[(2S)-2-{[(2S)-1-Ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl]pyrrolidine-2-  

carboxylic acid $(Z)$ -but-2-enedioate [ 76095-16-4 ]Enalapril Maleate contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $102.0\%$ of enalapril maleate $\mathrm{(C_{20}H_{28}N_{2}O_{5}{\cdot}C_{4}H_{4}O_{4})}$ , calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Enalapril Maleate occurs as white crystals or a crystalline powder. It is freely soluble in methanol, sparingly soluble in water or ethanol(99.5), and slightly soluble in acetonitrile.  

Melting point —About $145\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition). Identification (1) To $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Enalapril Maleate, add 1 mol/L hydrochloric acid TS, shake, add $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of ether, and shake for 5 minutes. Take $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the upper layer, distill the ether on a steam bath, and add $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water to the residue while shaking. Add 1 drop of potassium permanganate TS; the red color of the solution disappears immediately.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Enalapril Maleate and enalapril maleate RS as directed in the paste method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) The retention times of the major peaks obtained from the test solution and the standard solution in the Assay are the same.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{25}$ : Between $-41.0^{\circ}$ and $-43.5^{\circ}$ (0.1 g after drying, methanol, $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ ,$100\;\mathrm{mm}$ ).  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Proceed with $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Enalapril Maleate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(2) Related substances —Weigh accurately about 30 mg of Enalapril Maleate, dissolve in a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.5$ , and acetonitrile $(95:5)$ to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $30~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of enalapril maleate RS, dissolve in a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.5$ and acetonitrile $(95:5)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet accurately $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\ 2.5$ and acetonitrile $(95:5)$ to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution Perform the test with 50 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas of each solution by the automatic integration method, and calculate the content of each related substance; a peak among two peaks other than the major peak is NMT $1.0\%$ , another peak is NMT $0.3\%$ , and the total content of the related substances is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Content $(\%)$ of each related substance $=\ 100\times\left({\frac{C_{\mathrm{S}}}{C_{\mathrm{i}}}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\right)$  

$C_{\mathrm{{S}}}$ : Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ of the standard solution $C_{\mathrm{i}}$ : Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ ) of Enalapril Maleate in the test solution $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of each related substance in the test solution  

$A_{S}$ : Peak area of each related substance in the standard solution  

Operating conditions  

For the detector, column, column temperature, mobile phase and flow rate, proceed as directed in the operating conditions under the Assay.  

Loss on drying NMT $1.0\%$ (NMT 0.67 kPa, $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}_{!}$ , 2 hours).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.2\%$ ($\,[\,{\bf\rho}_{1}\,{\bf g})$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $30~\mathrm{mg}$ of Enalapril Maleate, dissolve in a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.5$ , and acetonitrile $(95:5)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve about $30~\mathrm{mg}$ , accurately weighed, of enalapril maleate RS in a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}$ 2.5, and acetonitrile $(95:5)$ to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and calculate the major peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , from each solution.  

Amount (mg) of enalapril maleate $\mathrm{(C_{20}H_{28}N_{2}O_{5}{\cdot}C_{4}H_{4}O_{4})}$ $\equiv.$ Amount (mg) of enalapril maleate $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.1~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with styrene-divinylbenzene copolymer for liquid chromatography ( $5\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: $70\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ Flow rate: $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$  

Mobile phase: Control the mixing ratio of mobile phase A and mobile phase $\mathbf{B}$ in stages or gradient elution  

as follows.  

Mobile phase A: A mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,6.8$ and acetonitrile $(19:1)$ .  

Mobile phase B: A mixture of acetonitrile and phosphate buffer solution, pH 6.8 $(33:17)$ .  

![](images/f91b602efdd460ef21d61a4aed55faa7fc4c468343bc5df4553512dcd03a0e87.jpg)  

System suitability  

System performance: Mix $1\mod$ of enalapril diketopiperazine solution and $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution. Proceed with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above operating conditions; enalapril and enalapril diketopiperazine are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 3.5.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the operating conditions under the Assay; the relative standard deviation of the peak areas is NMT $1.0\%$ .  

$p H\,6.8$ phosphate buffer solution —Dissolve $2.8~\mathrm{g}$ of sodium dihydrogen phosphate dihydrate in about $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of water. Adjust with $9\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ of sodium hydroxide TS to a $\mathrm{pH}$ of 6.8, dilute with water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

$p H\,2.5$ phosphate buffer solution —Dissolve $2.8~\mathrm{g}$ of sodium dihydrogen phosphate dihydrate in about $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of water. Adjust with phosphoric acid to a $\mathrm{pH}$ of 2.5, dilute with water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Enalapril diketopiperazine solution —Place about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate RS in a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ beaker to form a mound on the bottom of the beaker, and place the beaker on a hotplate stirrer. Heat up to a temperature not to cause pyrolysis for about 5 to 10 minutes until the solid is melted. Immediately allow to cool, add $50\,\mathrm{\ml}$ of acetonitrile, and sonicate for a few minutes. The solution typically contains, in each mL, between $0.2~\mathrm{mg}$ and 0.4 mg of enalapril diketopiperazine.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

# Enalapril Maleate Tablets 에날라프릴말레산염정  

Enalapril Maleate Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount of enalapril maleate $\mathrm{(C_{20}H_{28}N_{2}O_{5}{\cdot}C_{4}H_{4}O_{4}}$ : 492.52).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Enalapril Maleate.  

Identification (1) Weigh an amount of previously powdered Enalapril Maleate Tablets equivalent to $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of Enalapril Maleate according to the labeled amount, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and shake well. Centrifuge this solution, take the clear supernatant, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $25~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate RS in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of water, acetone, 1-butanol and acetic acid(100) $\lfloor1:1:$ $1:1)$ ) as the developing solvent to a distance of about 10 cm, and air-dry the plate. Examine under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254~\mathrm{nm}$ ); the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the 2 spots obtained from the test solution and 2 spots obtained from the standard solution are the same.  

(2) The retention times of the major peaks obtained from the test solution and the standard solution in the Assay are the same.  

Purity Related substances —Use the test solution and the standard solution prepared as directed under the Assay, the $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ phosphate buffer solution, and the enalapril diketopiperazine solution prepared as directed under the Assay of Enalapril Maleate. Take $1.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of the standard solution, add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ ,to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the related substance standard solution. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution, the standard solution, the related substance standard solution and the buffer solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the conditions of the Assay, determine the peak area of each solution by the automatic integration method, and calculate the content of related substances. Determine the peak areas of all peaks with peak areas NLT $0.1\%$ of the enalapril peak area except for peaks appearing in the buffer solution in the chromatogram of the test solution.  

$$
=\frac{492.53}{348.39}\times\frac{C V}{N}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\frac{100}{L}
$$  

492.53: Molecular weight of enalapril maleate  

348.39: Molecular weight of anhydrous enalaprilate   
C: Concentration $(\upmu\mathrm{g/mL)}$ of enalaprilate in the   
standard solution   
$V$ : Volume (mL) of the test solution   
N: Number of tablets taken for the test   
$L$ : Labeled amount $\mathrm{(mg)}$ of enalapril maleate for   
tablets   
$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of enalaprilate in the test solution  

$$
={\frac{492.53}{358.44}}\times{\frac{C^{\prime}V}{N}}\times{\frac{\phantom{4}A_{\mathrm{T}}}{1.25A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\times{\frac{100}{L}}
$$  

492.53: Molecular weight of enalapril maleate  

358.44: Molecular weight of enalapril diketopiperazine   
$C^{\prime}$ : Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ ) of enalapril maleate RS in related substance standard solution  

V: Volume (mL) of the test solution N: Number of tablets taken for the test 1.25: Peak area of enalapril diketopiperazine to enalapril  

$L$ : Labeled amount (mg) of enalapril maleate for tablets  

$$
={\frac{C^{\prime}V}{N}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\times{\frac{100}{L}}
$$  

The total amount of related substances, including enalaprilate and enalapril diketopiperazine, is NMT $5.0\%$ .  

Enalaprilate standard solution —Weigh accurately an appropriate amount of enalaprilate RS, and dissolve in water to make a solution containing $0.4~\mathrm{mg}$ per mL.  

Standard solution —Weigh accurately about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate RS, add $0.5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of enalaprilate RS, add $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of buffer solution, dissolve by mixing well, and add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Related substance standard solution —Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution accurately, and add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Enalapril Maleate Tablet at 50 revolutions per minute according to Method 2 under the Dissolution, using $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,6.8$ , as the dissolution medium. After 30 minutes from starting the dissolution test, take $20\;\mathrm{~mL}$ of the dissolved solution, and filter through a membrane filter with a pore size NMT $0.8\ \upmu\mathrm{m}$ . Discard the first $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, and use the subsequent filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately 10 mg of enalapril maleate RS, dissolve in phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\ 6.8$ , to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test according to the operating conditions under the Assay of Enalapril Maleate.  

It meets the requirements if the dissolution rate of Enalapril Maleate Tablets for 30 minutes is NLT $80\%$ .  

Uniformity of dosage units It meets the requirements of the Content Uniformity Test when the test is performed according to the following method. Take 1 tablet of Enalapril Maleate Tablet, add $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , sonicate for 15 minutes if necessary, shake for 30 minutes, add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Take a certain amount of this solution, and dilute exactly with the buffer solution to the concentration of $0.1~\mathrm{mg}$ per mL. Separately, weigh accurately $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate RS, dissolve in phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test as directed under the Assay of Enalapril Maleate.  

Amount (mg) of enalapril maleate $\left({\bf C}_{20}\mathrm{H}_{28}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{5}{\cdot}{\bf C}_{4}\mathrm{H}_{4}\mathrm{O}_{4}\right)$  

$$
\dot{\mathbf{\eta}}=T\times\frac{C}{D}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}
$$  

$T:$ Labeled amount $\mathrm{(mg)}$ of enalapril maleate in 1 tablet $C$ : Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ of the standard solution $D$ : Concentration $\mathrm{(mg/mL)}$ of enalapril maleate in the test solution $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of enalapril maleate in the test solution $A_{S}$ : Peak area of enalapril maleate in the standard solution $p H~2.2$ phosphate buffer solution —Dissolve $1.38\mathrm{~g~}$ of sodium dihydrogen phosphate dihydrate in about 800 mL of water, add phosphoric acid to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 2.2, and add water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Assay Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 tablets of Enalapril Maleate Tablets, and powder. Weigh accurately a portion of this powder, equivalent to about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate $\left({\bf C}_{20}\mathrm{H}_{28}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{5}{\cdot}\mathrm{C}_{4}\mathrm{H}_{4}\mathrm{O}_{4}\right)$ ), add $50\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , from the Uniformity of dosage units, sonicate for 15 minutes, and shake for 30 minutes. Then, add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , sonicate for 15 minutes, filter through a membrane filter, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of enalapril maleate RS, add $0.5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of enalaprilate RS, dissolve in 50 mL of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , and sonicate if necessary. Then, add phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\ 2.2$ ,to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following operating conditions, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of each solution.  

Amount (mg) of enalapril maleate $\left({\bf C}_{20}{\mathrm{H}}_{28}{\mathrm{N}}_{2}{\mathrm{O}}_{5}{\cdot}{\mathrm{C}}_{4}{\mathrm{H}}_{4}{\mathrm{O}}_{4}\right)$ $=$ Amount (mg) of enalapril maleate $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $215\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25\ \mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with hydroxy propylsilyl silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: $50\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$  

Mobile phase: A mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,2.2$ , and acetonitrile $(75:25)$ .  

Flow rate: $2\ \mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Take $0.5\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of enalapril diketopiperazine solution, and add the standard solution to make $25~\mathrm{mL}$ . Proceed with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; maleic acid, enalaprilate, enalapril and enalapril diketopiperazine are eluted in this order with the resolutions between maleic acid and enalaprilate, enalaprilate and enalapril, and enalapril and enalapril diketopiperazine being NLT 2.0, respectively.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $50\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak areas of enalapril is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

![](images/955f969494cf68df4f5634ebc345cb70ba10d5cfb8135b1a4059eacae8a0578b.jpg)  
Enflurane $\mathrm{C}_{3}\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{ClF}_{5}\mathrm{O}:184.49$ 2-Chloro-1-(difluoromethoxy)-1,1,2-trifluoroethane [13838-16-9 ]  

Description Enflurane occurs as a clear, colorless fluid.   
It is slightly soluble in water.   
It is miscible with ethanol(95) or ether.   
It is a volatile, and not inflammable.   
It shows no optical rotation.   
Boiling point —Between 54 and $57^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Identification (1) Take $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of Enflurane, and prepare the test solution as directed under the Oxygen Flask Combustion using $40~\mathrm{mL}$ of water as the absorbent. The test solution responds to the Qualitative Analysis for chloride and fluoride.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Enflurane and enflurane RS as directed under the liquid film method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Refractive index $n_{D}^{20}$ : Between 1.302 and 1.304. Purity (1) Acidity or alkalinity —To $60\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of Enflurane, add $60\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of freshly boiled and cooled water, shake for 3 minutes to mix, take the water layer, and use this solution as the test solution. To $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of the test solution, add 1 drop of bromocresol purple TS and 0.10 mL of $0.01\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide solution; a violet color develops. To $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, add 1 drop of bromocresol purple TS and $60~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid; a yellow color is produced.  

(2) Chloride —Weigh $20~\mathrm{g}$ of Enflurane, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, shake well to mix, and separate the water layer. Take $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the water layer, and add $6~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute nitric acid and water to make $50~\mathrm{{mL}}$ . Perform the test using this solution as the test solution. Prepare the control solution with $0.30~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid (NMT $0.001\%$ ).  

(3) Related substances —Perform the test with $5\;\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of Enflurane as directed under the Gas Chromatography according to the following conditions. Introduce the sample, immediately determine each peak area other than the peak of air as directed in the automatic integration method, and calculate the amount of each peak by the percentage peak area method; the amount of the substances other than enflurane is NMT $0.10\%$ .  

Operating conditions Detector: A thermal conductivity detector Column: A stainless steel about $3\ \mathrm{mm}$ in inside diameter and about $3\,\textrm{m}$ in length, packed with diatomaceous earth for gas chromatography, 180 to $250~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter, coated with diethylene glycol succinate ester for gas chromatography at the ratio of $20\%$ .  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $80\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Carrier gas: Helium  

Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of enflurane is about 3 minutes.  

# System suitability  

Test for required detectability: Take $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of Enflurane, and add 2-propanol to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add 2-propanol to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the system suitability solution. Take 1.0 mL of this solution and add 2-propanol to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ . Confirm that the peak area of enflurane obtained from $5\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution is equivalent to 7 to $13\%$ of the peak area of enflurane from the system suitability solution.  

System performance: Mix $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of Enflurane with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of 2-propanol. Proceed with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above operating conditions, enflurane and 2-propanol are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 2.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the system suitability solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the ratios of the peak area of enflurane is NMT Time span of measurement: About 3 times the retention time of enflurane.  

(4) Evaporation residue —Pipet $65\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of Enflurane, evaporate to dryness on a steam bath, and dry the residue at $105~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour; the mass of the residue is NMT $1.0\;\mathrm{mg}$ .  

Water NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~10~g~}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers and store at below $30\,^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .

Enoxacin $\mathrm{C_{15}H_{17}F N_{4}O_{3}{\cdot}1\%H_{2}O}:347.34$ 1-Ethyl-6-fluoro-4-oxo-7-(piperazin-1-yl)-1,4-dihydro1,8-naphthyridine-3-carboxylic acid sesquihydrate [84294-96-2 ]  

Enoxacin Hydrate, when dried, contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of enoxacin $(\mathrm{C}_{15}\mathrm{H}_{17}\mathrm{FN}_{4}\mathrm{O}_{3}:320.32)$ .Description Enoxacin Hydrate occurs as white to pale yellowish brown crystals or a crystalline powder. It is freely soluble in acetic acid(100), slightly soluble in methanol, very slightly soluble in chloroform, and practically insoluble as water, ethanol(95) or ether. It dissolves in dilute sodium hydroxide TS. It is gradually colored by light.  

Identification (1) Put $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate and $30~\mathrm{mg}$ of sodium metal in a test tube, and heat gently with caution until glowing red. After cooling, add $0.5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol and $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and heat to boiling. Add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute acetic acid and filter; the filtrate responds to the Qualitative Analysis (2) for fluoride.  

(2) Dissolve $50~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Enoxacin Hydrate and enoxacin hydrate RS in dilute sodium hydroxide TS to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ each of these solutions and add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . With these solutions, determine the absorption spectra as directed under the Ultravioletvisible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(3) Determine the infrared spectra of Enoxacin Hydrate and enoxacin hydrate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of ab  

# Melting point Between 225 and $229\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (after drying).  

Purity (1) Sulfate —Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sodium hydroxide TS, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid, shake to mix, and centrifuge. Filter the clear supernatant, take $30\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, and add water to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution and perform the test. Prepare the control solution by adding $0.50~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.005~\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid, $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sodium hydroxide TS, $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid and water to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ (NMT $0.048\%$ ).  

(2) Heavy metals— Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 20 ppm).  

(3) Arsenic —Proceed with $1.0\mathrm{~g~}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate according to Method 3 and perform the test (NMT 2 ppm).  

(4) Related substances —Dissolve $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of methanol and chloroform $(7:3)$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add a mixture of methanol and chloroform $(7:3)$ to make $200\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $5\,\textrm{\scriptsize\sharp L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of 1-butanol, water and acetic acid(100) $(3:1:1)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10\;\mathrm{cm}$ , and airdry the plate. Observe the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ); the spots other than the principal spot obtained from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution.  

Loss on drying Between $7.0\%$ and $9.0\%$ ($\mathrm{~\,~1~g,~105~^{o}C.}$ , 3 hours).  

Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($1\;\mathrm{g}$ , platinum crucible). Assay Weigh accurately about $0.3\mathrm{~g~}$ of Enoxacin Hydrate, previously dried, dissolve in $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and titrate with $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=32.03~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C}_{15}\mathrm{H}_{17}\mathrm{FN}_{4}\mathrm{O}_{3}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Eperisone Hydrochloride 에페리손염산염  

![](images/a7317a8e80e5283a62ee0d39f7e853255bf4ad4c232dea9ed3b9ea2afe677585.jpg)  

1-(4-Ethylphenyl)-2-methyl-3-(piperidin-1-yl)   
propan-1-one hydrochloride [ 56839-43-1 ]  
Eperisone Hydrochloride contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of eperisone hydrochloride $(\mathrm{C_{17}H_{25}N O{\cdot}H C l})$ .Description Eperisone Hydrochloride occurs as a white crystalline powder.   
It is freely soluble in water, methanol or acetic acid(100), and soluble in ethanol(99.5).  

Melting point— About $167\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition) A solution of Eperisone Hydrochloride in methanol (1 in 100) shows no optical rotation.  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of solutions of Eperisone Hydrochloride and eperisone hydrochloride RS in methanol (1 in 100000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Eperisone Hydrochloride and eperisone hydrochloride RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Midinfrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) An aqueous solution of Eperisone Hydrochloride (1 in 50) responds to the Qualitative Analysis for chloride.  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Eperisone Hydrochloride as directed under Method 1 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $20\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

(2) Piperidine hydrochloride —Weigh $1.0\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Eperisone Hydrochloride and dissolve in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2), $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of copper(II) sulfate pentahydrate solution (1 in 20) and $1.5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia water(28), and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, to $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of piperidine hydrochloride solution (1 in 1000), add $18~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, 2.0 mL of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2), $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of copper(II) sulfate pentahydrate solution (1 in 20) and $1.5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia water(28), and use this solution as the standard solution. To each of the test solution and the standard solution, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of isopropyl ether and carbon disulfide $(3:1)$ , mix well for 30 seconds, allow them to stand for 2 minutes, and compare the color of two supernatants; the color obtained from the test solution is not more intense than that obtained from the standard solution.  

(3) Related substances —Weigh $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of Eperisone Hydrochloride, dissolve it in $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the mobile phase, and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly 100 mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with exactly $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine each peak area as directed in the automatic integration method; the total area of the peaks other than eperisone obtained from the test solution is not greater than 1/5 times the peak area of eperisone from the standard solution.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $30\,^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of methanol, $0.0375\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium 1-decanesulfonate solution and perchloric acid $(600:400:1)$ ).  

Flow rate: Adjust so that the retention time of eperisone is about 17 minutes.  

# System suitability  

Test for required detectability: Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution and add the mobile phase to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ . Confirm that the peak area of eperisone obtained from $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution is equivalent to 7 to $13\%$ of that from the standard solution.  

System performance: Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the number of theoretical plates and symmetry factor of the peak of eperisone are NLT 4000 and NMT 2.0, respectively.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of eperisone is NMT $3.0\%$ .  

Time span of measurement: About 2 times the retention time of eperisone.  

Sodium $^{\,l}$ -decanesulfonate solution, 0.0375 mol/L —Dissolve $3.665\ \mathrm{g}$ of sodium 1-decanesulfonate in $400\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water.  

Water NMT $0.2\%$ $\mathrm{[0.1~g}$ , coulometric titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.2\%$ ($\,[\,{\bf\rho}_{1}\,{\bf g})$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.6\ \mathrm{g}$ of Eperisone Hydrochloride, dissolve in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), add $80\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of acetic anhydride, and titrate with $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=29.59\ \mathrm{mg}$ of C 17 H25 NO∙HCl  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.
