# Erythromycin 에리트로마이신  

![](images/2e964c6fe5cd30183110df35eb04adcac7d416c110965e5dc57783d7983ea63a.jpg)  

Erythromycin $\mathrm{C}_{37}\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93 (3 R,4 S,5 S,6 R,7 R,9 R,11 R,12 R,13 S,14 R)-6-[(2 S,3 R,4 S,6 R)- 4-(Dimethylamino)-3-hydroxy-6-methyloxan-2-yl]oxy14-ethyl-7,12,13-trihydroxy-4-[(2 R,4 R,5 S,6 S)-5-hydroxy4-methoxy-4,6-dimethyloxan-2-yl]oxy-3,5,7,9,11,13- hexamethyl-oxacyclo-tetradecane-2,10-dione [ 114-07-8 ]Erythromycin is a macrolide substance having antifungal activity produced by the growth of Saccharopolyspora erythraea .  

Erythromycin contains NLT $930~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and NMT 1020 μg (potency) of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{N}\mathbf{O}_{13})$ ) per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Erythromycin occurs as a white to pale yellowish white powder.  

It is very soluble in $N,N\!\cdot$ -dimethylformamide, freely soluble in methanol or ethanol(95), and slightly soluble in water.  

Identification (1) Determine the infrared spectra of Erythromycin and erythromycin RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(2) Dissolve $10~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Erythromycin and erythromycin RS in $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thinlayer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thinlayer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of methanol and ammonia water(28) $(50:1)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10~\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly 4-methoxybenzaldehydesulfuric acid TS on the plate, and heat at $100~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 15 minutes; the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution show a dark purple color and the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values are the same.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ : Between $-71^{\circ}$ and $-78^{\circ}$ (1g, calculated on the anhydrous basis, ethanol(95), $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , 100 mm).  

pH Dissolve $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin in $150~\mathrm{mL}$ of water;   
the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 8.0 and 10.5.  

Purity (1) Thiocyanate —Weigh accurately about $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin, transfer into a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ brown volumetric flask, dissolve by adding $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of iron(III) chloride TS and methanol to make to $50~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately potassium thiocyanate, previously dried at $105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour and cooled, transfer into two $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flasks, and add methanol to make $50\,\mathrm{\mL}$ .Take accurately $5.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ each of these solutions, add methanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , then take exactly $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ each of the resulting solutions, transfer into $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ brown volumetric flasks, add exactly $1.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of iron(III) chloride TS to each solution, add methanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use these solutions as the standard solutions. Separately, transfer $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the iron(III) chloride TS into a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ brown volumetric flask, dissolve in methanol to make 50 mL, and use this solution as the standard test solution. Use the test solution, the standard solutions and the standard test solution within 30 minutes after the preparation. Perform the test with the test and standard solutions as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy using the blank test solution as the control solution, determine the absorbance at $492\;\mathrm{nm}$ , and calculate the amount of thiocyanate by the following formula; it is NMT $0.3\%$ .  

$$
={\frac{58.08}{97.18}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{W_{T}}}\times0.5\times\left[{\frac{W_{1}}{A_{1}}}+{\frac{W_{2}}{A_{2}}}\right]
$$  

$A_{\mathrm{{T}}}$ :Absorbance of the test solution $W_{\mathrm{T}}$ :Amount (mg) of sample taken $A_{1},A_{2}$ : Absorbance of each standard solution $W_{1}$ ,$W_{2}$ : Amount (mg) of potassium thiocyanate taken from each standard solution 58.08: Molecular weight of thiocyanate 97.18: Molecular weight of potassium thiocyanate System suitability :Determine the absorption spectrum of each standard solution, and calculate suitability factor (S) by the following formula; it is between 0.985 and 1.015.  

$$
S={\frac{A_{1}}{W_{1}}}\!+\!{\frac{W_{2}}{A_{2}}}
$$  

$A_{1},A_{2}$ : Absorbance of each standard solution $W_{1}$ ,$W_{2}$ : Amount (mg) of potassium thiocyanate taken from each standard solution  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Ceftazidime Hydrate according to Method 4 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $20\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

(3) Arsenic —Proceed with $1.0\textbf{g}$ of Erythromycin according to Method 5 and perform the test with hydrochloric acid instead of dilute hydrochloric acid (1 in 2) $(\mathrm{NMT}\ 2\ \mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(4) Related substances —Dissolve $40~\mathrm{mg}$ of Erythromycin in $2\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\nobreakspace7.0\$ and methanol $(15:1)$ to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $16~\mathrm{mg}$ of erythromycin RS in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,7.0$ and methanol $(15:1)$ to make exactly $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard stock solution. Dissolve $5~\mathrm{mg}$ each of erythromycin $\mathbf{B}$ and erythromycin C in 2 mL of methanol, add exactly $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard stock solution, add a mixture of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}$ 7.0 and methanol $(15:1)$ to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Take exactly each $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the test solution and the standard solution, perform the test as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak area of each solution by the automatic integration method; the peak areas of erythromycin B and erythromycin C from the test solution are not greater than the peak areas of erythromycin B and erythromycin C in the standard solution. In addition, the peak areas other than erythromycin, erythromycin B and erythromycin C are not greater than the peak area of erythromycin from the standard solution.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $215\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 ${\upmu\mathrm{m}}\textrm{-}10~\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $70\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $3.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of dibasic potassium phosphate in water to make $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , adjust $\mathrm{pH}$ to 9.0 with diluted phosphoric acid (1 in 10). To $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $190~\mathrm{mL}$ of $t$ -butyl alcohol, $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile and water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of erythromycin is about 20 minutes.  

# System suitability  

System performance: Dissolve $2~\mathrm{~mg}$ of Ndemethylerythromycin in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution. Proceed with $100\,\mathrm{\upmuL}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; N-demethylerythromycin, erythromycin C, erythromycin and erythromycin B are eluted in this order with the resolution between Ndemethylerythromycin and erythromycin C being NLT 0.8, and the resolution between N-demethylerythromycin and erythromycin being NLT 5.5.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 3 times with $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solutions according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of erythromycin is NMT $3.0\%$ .  

Time span of measurement: About 4 times the retention time of erythromycin after the solvent peak. Water NMT $10.0\%$ ($_{0.2\mathrm{~g~}}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.2\%$ ($\mathrm{~\ensuremath~{~1~}~}\mathrm{g})$  

Sterility It meets the requirements when used in the manufacturing of sterile preparations. However, it is exempt from the requirements when there is a terminal sterilization process in the manufacturing process of sterile preparations.  

Pyrogen It meets the requirements when used in the manufacturing of sterile preparations. Proceed with an appropriate amount of Erythromycin to prepare a solution containing $1.0~\mathrm{mg}$ per mL, use $50\ \mathrm{ml}$ of this solution as the test solution. However, inject the test solution to a rabbit by $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ per $\mathrm{kg}$ of the rabbit weight.  

Assay Weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) each of Erythromycin and erythromycin RS, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following operating conditions, and determine the peak areas, $\mathrm{Ar}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ of erythromycin.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $210\;\mathrm{nm})$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $15\ \mathrm{cm}$ to $30\ \mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $5\;{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of methanol and 0.067 $\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate $(3:2)$ .  

System suitability  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $20\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solutions according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of erythromycin is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

# Erythromycin Delayed-Release Capsules 에리트로마이신장용캡슐  

Erythromycin Delayed-Release Capsules contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $(\mathrm{C}_{37}\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}:733.93)$  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Capsules, with Erythromycin.  

Identification Perform the test as directed under the Identification of Erythromycin Delayed-Release Tablets. Water NMT $7.5\%$ $\left(0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}\right.$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 capsule of Erythromycin Delayed-Release Capsules at 50 revolutions per minute  for 60 minutes according to Method 1 under the Dissolution, using $900\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of $0.06\mathrm{\mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid as the dissolution medium. Immediately wash the remaining contents and the basket with water to remove hydrochloric acid, and perform the test for 60 minutes under the conditions described in the above test method, using $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.2\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, pH 6.8, as the dissolution medium. Take $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the dissolved solution 60 minutes after starting the second dissolution test, and use the filtrate as the test solution.  

Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements. Assay Proceed as directed under the Assay under Erythromycin. Take NLT 20 capsules of Erythromycin Delayed-Release Capsules, weigh accurately the mass of the contents equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) according to the labeled potency, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Gel 에리트로마이신겔  

Erythromycin Gel contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $\mathrm{\bfC}_{37}\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Gels, with Erythromycin.  

Identification Perform the test under the Identification (2) of Erythromycin Tropical Solution. However, weigh accurately an appropriate amount of Erythromycin Gel and erythromycin RS, and dissolve in methanol to make a solution containing $2.5~\mathrm{{mg}}$ (potency) per mL; use this solution as the test solution and standard solution, respectively.

However, weigh accurately an amount of Erythromycin Gel equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) according to the labeled potency, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use the mobile phase to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ ; use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Topical Solution 에리트로마이신외용액  

Erythromycin Topical Solution contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin ( $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93), when quantified as a topical solution.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under the Liquids, with Erythromycin.  

Identification (1) Take $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of Erythromycin Topical Solution, add acetone to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ then add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the solution exhibits amber to a reddish purple color.  

(2) Take $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of Erythromycin Topical Solution, add $7~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $26~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin RS in methanol to make $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Develop the plate with a mixture of methanol and chloroform $(85:15)$ as the developing solvent, dry the plate at room temperature, spray evenly a mixture of ethanol(95), $p$ -methoxybenzaldehyde and sulfuric acid $(90:5:5)$ , and heat at $100~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values are the same when comparing the spots of the test solution and the standard solution.  

Water (1) When using only ethanol as a solvent in the prescription: (1) NMT $8.0\%$ , when $20~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL, (2) NMT $5.0\%$ , when $15~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL.   
(2) When using ethanol and acetone as a solvent in the prescription: NMT $2.0\%$ .  
(3) When using neither ethanol as a solvent nor stabilizer in the prescription: no criteria to apply.   
However, use a mixture of pyridine and methanol for water determination $(1:1)$ , instead of methanol for water determination.  

Assay Perform the test as directed under the Assay of Erythromycin. Weigh accurately an amount of Erythromycin Gel equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) according to the labeled potency, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Enteric-Coated Tablets 에리트로마이신장용정  

Erythromycin Enteric-Coated Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin ( $\mathrm{\bf~\left(C_{37}H_{67}N O_{13}\right.}$ : 733.93). Erythromycin EntericCoated Tablets are delayed-release preparations.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Erythromycin.  

Identification Perform the test as directed under the Identification (2) of Erythromycin. Weigh an amount of powdered Erythromycin Enteric-Coated Tablets, equivalent to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin according to the labeled amount, add $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of methanol, shake to mix, filter, and use this solution as the test solution.  

Loss on drying NMT $10.0\%$ $\mathrm{0.2\g,\,0.67\kPa}$ ,$60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 3 hours).  

Disintegration Meets the requirements. Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements. Assay Perform the test as directed under the Assay of Erythromycin. Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 tablets of Erythromycin Enteric-Coated Tablets, powder, weigh accurately an amount of this powder, equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of eythromycin according to the labeled potency, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Estolate 에리트로마이신에스톨산염  

![](images/702276f1340ec7062fe04a6e7538a5a0fd60ed1c1fc913c5f03ef6fe26697a41.jpg)  

Erythromycin Estolate  

$\mathrm{C_{40}H_{71}N O_{14}{}\cdot C_{12}H_{25}O S O_{3}H:1056.39}$ [(2 S,3 R,4 S,6 R)-4-(Dimethylamino)-2- [[(3 R,4 S,5 S,6 R,7 R,9 R,11 R,12 R, 13 S,14 R)-14-ethyl  

7,12,13-trihydroxy-4-[(2R,4R,5S,6S)-5-hydroxy-4- methoxy-4,6-dimethyloxan-2-yl]oxy-3,5,7,9,11,13- hexamethyl-2,10-dioxo-oxacyclotetradec-6-yl]oxy]-6- methyloxan-3-yl] propanoate dodecyl hydrogen sulfate [3521-62-8 ]  

Erythromycin Estolate, when dried, contains NLT $600~\mathrm{~\mug~}$ (potency) of Erythromycin (C37H67NO13: 733.93) per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Erythromycin Estolate occurs as a white crystalline powder or a powder. It is odorless and has a bitter taste.  

It is sparingly soluble in methanol or ethanol(95) and very slightly insoluble in water or benzene.  

Identification Determine the infrared spectra of Erythromycin Estolate and erythromycin estolate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

pH Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Estolate in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 4.5 and 7.0.  

Purity Free erythromycin ―Dissolve $0.250\mathrm{g}$ of this drug, weighed accurately, in $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the mobile phase and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $75.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of erythromycin RS and dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take exactly $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add acetonitrile to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions; the peak area obtained from the test solution is not larger than the major peak area obtained from the standard solution (NMT $6.0\%$ ).  

Buffer solution ―Dissolve $3.4~\mathrm{g}$ of potassium dihydrogen phosphate and $2.75~\mathrm{mL}$ of Triethylamine in water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

# Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $195\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column $4.6\;\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\ensuremath{\,\mathrm{\upmum}}\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $30\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ of a mixture of acetonitrile and buffer solution (35:65) to 3.0 by adding dilute phosphoric acid.  

Flow rate: $1\ \mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $25~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution and the test solution according to the above conditions; the retention time of the first major peak in the test solution and erythromycin in the standard solution is about 5 minutes and about 10 minutes.  

Time span of measurement: About twice the retention time of the erythromycin peak for the standard solution, and about 4.5 times the first peak retention time of erythromycin propionate for the test solution.  

Water NMT $4.0\%$ $(0.2\ \mathrm{g},\,20\ \mathrm{mL}$ of methanol containing $10\%$ imidazole, volumetric titration, direct titration).  

Assay Proceed as directed under the Assay under Erythromycin. However, weigh accurately an appropriate amount of Erythromycin Estolate, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution (pH 8.0) to contain $1.0~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL, and then warm this solution on a steam bath at $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 2 hours, or allow to stand at room temperature of 16 to 18 hours. Use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Estolate Capsules 에리트로마이신에스톨산염캡슐  

Erythromycin Estolate Capsules contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}:733.93)$ .  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Capsules, with Erythromycin Estolate.  

Identification Weigh the appropriate amount of each Erythromycin Estolate Capsules and erythromycin estolate RS, dissolve in a small amount of methanol, add water to make a solution containing $500~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per $\mathrm{mL}$ , respectively, and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of methanol and 2- propanol $(85:15)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10\;\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Apply iodine vapor on the thin-layer chromatographic plate or evenly spray $10\%$ sulfuric acid solution; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Loss on drying NMT $5.0\%$ $\mathrm{[0.1~g.}$ , in vacuum, $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 3 hours).  

romycin. Take NLT 20 capsules of Erythromycin Estolate Capsules, weigh accurately the mass of the contents, and weigh accurately an amount equivalent to about 50 mg (potency) according to the labeled potency, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ , to contain $1.0\;\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL. Then warm this solution in a $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ water bath for 2 hours or allow it to stand at room temperature for 16 to 18 hours, and use this solution as the test solution.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate 에리트로마이신에틸숙시네이트  

![](images/2903fdf7a13772cdc67f202694330f890df437edd81c935f7954183d34df4f94.jpg)  
$\mathrm{C_{43}H_{75}N O_{16}:862.05}$  

4- O-[(2 S,3 R,4 S,6 R)-4-(Dimethylamino)-2- [[(3 R,4 S,5 S,6 R,7 R,9 R,11 R,12 R,13 S,14 R)-14-ethyl7,12,13-trihydroxy-4-[(2 R,4 R,5 S,6 S)-5-hydroxy-4- methoxy-4,6-dimethyloxan-2-yl]oxy-3,5,7,9,11,13- hexamethyl-2,10-dioxo-oxacyclotetradec-6-yl]oxy]-6- methyloxan-3-yl] 1-O-ethyl-butanedioate [ 1264-62-6 ]Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate is a derivative of erythromycin.  

Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate contains NLT $780~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and NMT $900~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) of erythromycin $(\mathrm{C}_{37}\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}:733.93)$ ) per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate occurs as a white powder.  

It is freely soluble in methanol, soluble in ethanol(95) and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Dissolve $3~\mathrm{~mg}$ of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone and add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the solution exhibits an orange color and immediately changes into red to dark purple.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate and erythromycin ethylsuccinate RS, previously dried in a desiccator (in vacuum, silica gel) for 24 hours, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both exhibits similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers. $\mathbf{pH}$ The pH of a solution obtained by suspending $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate in $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water is between 6.0 and 8.5.  

Purity (1) Free erythromycin ―Weigh accurately 0.250 g of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate, dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $75.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of the erythromycin RS and dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add acetonitrile to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions; the peak area obtained from the test solution is not larger than the area of the major peak obtained from the standard solution (NMT $6.0\%$ ).  

Operating conditions  

Proceed as directed under the operating conditions for free erythromycin under the Purity of Erythromycin Estolate.  

# System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $25~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution and the test solution under the above conditions; the peak retention times of erythromycin in the standard solution and erythromycin ethylsuccinate in the test solution are about $8\ \mathrm{min}$ and about 24 min, respectively.  

Time span of measurement: About 2 times the peak retention time of erythromycin for the standard solution, and about 2 times the peak retention time of erythromycin ethylsuccinate for the test solution.  

(2) Related substances ―Weigh accurately about $0.115~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate, put it into a 50- mL Erlenmeyer flask, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of hydrolysis TS to mix. Allow to stand at room temperature for about 12 hours, add the hydrolysis TS to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of erythromycin, dissolve it in $12.5\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of methanol, add hydrolysis TS to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (1). Separately, weigh accurately about $5~\mathrm{mg}$ each of erythromycin B and erythromycin C, dissolve them in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add 2.5 mL of standard solution (1), and then add hydrolysis solution to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the standard solution (2). Perform the test with $200~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution (2) as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions and calculate the amount of individual related substances other than erythromycin A, erythromycin B, erythromycin C, erythromycin A enolether and erythromycin $N_{}$ -ethylsuccinate and the amount of erythromycin A enolether and erythromycin N-ethylsuccinate according to the following formula; each is NMT $3.0\%$ . However, the relative retention time of erythromycin $N\!\cdot$ -ethylsuccinate to the retention time of erythromycin A is about 1.3, and the peak areas of erythromycin A enolether and erythromycin $N_{}$ -ethylsuccinate are calculated by multiplying the area obtained by the automatic integration method by the sensitivity coefficients for erythromycin A of 0.09 and 0.14, respectively.  

$$
=\;50\times{\frac{C\times P}{W}}\times{\frac{A_{T}}{A_{S}}}
$$  

C: Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ of erythromycin in the standard solution (2)  

P: Content $(\%)$ of erythromycin A in erythromycin RS  

# W: Amount (mg) of sample taken  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak areas of each related substance, other than erythromycin A, erythromycin B, erythromycin C, erythromycin A enol ether and erythromycin $N\!\cdot$ -ethylsuccinate obtained from the test solution, and erythromycin A enol ether and erythromycin $N_{}$ -ethylsuccinate  

AS: Peak area of erythromycin A obtained from the standard solution (2)  

Hydrolysis TS ―A solution prepared by dissolving 2 $\mathrm{g}$ of dibasic potassium phosphate in water to make 100 mL and adjust the pH to 8.0 with phosphoric acid.  

# Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $215\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with spherical styrene-divinylbenzene copolymer for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\{5\,\upmu\mathrm{m}\right.}}$ to $10\,\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $70\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Add $400~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, $175~\mathrm{mL}$ of $t^{\star}$ -butyl alcohol and $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile to $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ , and add water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Flow rate: $2\ \mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $200~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the system suitability solution (1) under the above conditions; $N\!\cdot$ -demethylerythromycin, erythromycin C, erythromycin A and erythromycin B are eluted in this order with the resolution of $N\!\cdot$ -demethylerythromycin and erythromycin C being $\mathrm{NLT}\ 0.8$ and the resolution of $N\cdot$ demethylerythromycin and erythromycin A being NLT 5.5. Additionally, proceed with $100\,\mathrm{\upmuL}$ of the system suitability solution (2) under the above conditions; the relative retention time of erythromycin A enol ether to the retention time of erythromycin A is about 4.3 to 4.7. System repeatability: Repeat the test 5 times with $200\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ each of standard solution (1) under the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of erythromycin is NMT $1.0\%$ .  

System suitability solution $(I)$ ―Dissolve about 2 mg of $N\cdot$ -demethylerythromycin in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard  

solution (2).  

System suitability solution (2) ―Dissolve about 10 mg of erythromycin in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, then add 10 mL of buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,3.5$ , and allow to stand for 30 min. Keep refrigerated until use and discard after 8 hours after preparation.  

Buffer solution, $p H\ \&.O{\mathrm{-}}{\mathrm{A}}$ solution obtained by dissolving $2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of dibasic potassium phosphate in water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ and adjusting the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 8.0 with phosphoric acid. Buffer solution, $p H\ 3.5{\mathrm{-}}{\mathrm{A}}$ solution obtained by adjusting $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of the buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\;8.0$ to ${\mathrm{pH}}\,3.5$ with phosphoric acid.  

Water NMT $5.0\%$ ($\mathrm{~\ensuremath~{~0.5~\mathrm{~g~}~}~}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $1.0\%$ (1 g).  

Sterility It meets the requirements when used in the manufacturing of a sterile preparation. However, it is excluded in cases where there is a terminal sterilization process in the manufacturing of a sterile preparation.  

Pyrogen It meets the requirements when used in a sterile preparation. However, weigh an appropriate amount of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate to make an aqueous suspension containing $50~\mathrm{mg}$ per mL, use this solution as the test solution, and inject $0.1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution into the lower extremity muscle. However, the test solution injected to a rabbit shall be $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ per $\mathrm{kg}$ of the rabbit weight.  

Assay Cylindrical plate method (1) Medium Agar medium for seed and base layer: Use the medium in (A) (2) (a) $\textcircled{2}\textcircled{6}$ under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics. However, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 7.8 to 8.0.  

(2) Test organism: Use Staphylococcus aureus ATCC $6538\;\mathrm{P}$ as the test organism. (3) Weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{~mg}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Ethylsuccinate, dissolve in $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\mathrm{(pH}$ 8.0) to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Take exactly an appropriate amount of this solution, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0)$ to contain 20.0 and $5.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high concentration and low-concentration test solutions, respectively. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of the erythromycin RS, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add again $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\mathrm{(pH}$ 8.0) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard stock solution. Store the standard stock solution at below $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and use it within 7 days. Take exactly an appropriate amount of this standard stock solution, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\left(\mathrm{pH}\right.8.0\right)$ to contain 20.0 and $5.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high-concentration standard solution and the low-concentration standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test according to (A) (8) under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics.  

# Erythromycin and Tretinoin Topical Gel 에리트로마이신·트레티노인외용겔  

Erythromycin and Tretinoin Topical Gel contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93); NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $130.0\%$ of the labeled amount of tretinoin ($\mathrm{\bfC}_{20}\mathrm{H}_{28}\mathrm{O}_{2}$ : 300.44).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Gels, with Erythromycin and Tretinoin.  

Identification (1) Erythromycin —(i) Dissolve Erythromycin and Tretinoin Topical Gel and erythromycin RS in methanol to make a solution containing $2.5~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL, and use this solution as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography, develop the plate with a mixture of methanol and chloroform ( $\leftmoon\rightmoon\leftmoon$ 15) as the developing solvent, and take it out to dry at room temperature. Spray evenly a mixture of ethanol, $p_{-}$ -methoxybenzaldehyde and sulfuric acid $(90:5:5)$ , and warm at $100\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes; when comparing the black-purple spots of the test solution and the standard solution, the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of them are the same.  

(ii) Dissolve Erythromycin and Tretinoin Topical Gel in methanol to make a solution containing $2.5~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) per mL. Take $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add acetone to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the resulting solution turns from orange to reddish purple. (2) Tretinoin —The retention times of the major peaks obtained from the test solution and the standard solution under the Assay are the same.  

# Assay (1) Erythromycin  

(i) Microbial Assays for Antibiotics (i) Cylindrical plate method  

⑴ Medium: Agar medium for seed and base layer Microbial Assays for Antibiotics: Use the medium in (i) ⑵ (a) $\textcircled{2}\textcircled{6}$ . However, adjust the pH to 7.8 to 8.0. ⑵ Test organism: Use Staphylococcus aureus ATCC 6538P as the test organism.  

⑶ Common standard solution: Weigh accurately an amount equivalent to about $40~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin RS, dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0$ , to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and shake well to mix. Use this solution as the common standard stock solution. Store the common standard stock solution at below $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and use within 7 days. Pipet an appropriate amount of the common standard stock solution, dilute with the above buffer solution to contain 20.0 and $5.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use this solution as the common standard solution.  

⑷ Test solution: Weigh accurately an amount of Erythromycin and Tretinoin Topical Gel, equivalent to about $40~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency), dissolve in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathsf{p H}\ 8.0$ , to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution.

# Erythromycin Lactobionate 에리트로마이신락토비온산염  

![](images/79b7c215a213a5669bd8711bfaaf9ea93b0a451c57b1a67e71446057d233ad3e.jpg)  

C37 H67 NO 1 ·C 12 H22 O12 : 1092.22 (3 R,4 S,5 S,6 R,7 R,9 R,11 R,12 R,13 S,14 R)-6-[(2 S,3 R,4 S,6 R)- 4-(Dimethylamino)-3-hydroxy-6-methyloxan-2-yl]oxy  

14-ethyl-7,12,13-trihydroxy-4-[(2 R,4 R,5 S,6 S)-5-hydroxy4-methoxy-4,6-dimethyloxan-2-yl]oxy-3,5,7,9,11,13- hexamethyl-oxacyclo-tetradecane-2,10-   
dione(2 R,3 R,4 R,5 R)-2,3,5,6-tetrahydroxy-4-   
[(2 S,3 R,4 S,5 R,6 R)-3,4,5-trihydroxy-6-   
(hydroxymethyl)oxan-2-yl]oxyhexanoate [ 3847-29-8 ]Erythromycin Lactobionate is the lactobionate of erythromycin.   
Erythromycin Lactobionate contains NLT $590\ \upmu\mathrm{g}$ and NMT 700 μg (potency) of erythromycin $\left({37\mathrm{H}_{67}\mathrm{NO}_{13}}\right)$ per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis. Description Erythromycin Lactobionate occurs as a white powder.   
It is freely soluble in water, methanol or ethanol(99.5) and slightly soluble in acetone.  

Identification (1) To the $3~\mathrm{mg}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the resulting solution exhibits an orange color and immediately turns red to dark violet.  

(2) To $0.3\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate, add 15 mL of ammonia TS and $15~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform, shake to mix, and take the separated aqueous layer. Wash this solution with three $15\,\mathrm{\mL}$ portions of chloroform, and evaporate to dryness on a steam bath. Dissolve the residue in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of methanol and water $(3:2)$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $0.10~\mathrm{g}$ of lactobionic acid in a mixture of methanol and water $(3:2)$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of water, 1-butanol and acetic acid(100) $(3:3:$ 1) as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10\;\mathrm{cm}$ ,and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly dilute sulfuric acid on the plate, and heat at $105\;^{\circ}\!C$ for 20 minutes; the principal spot obtained from the test solution exhibits a dark brown color and has the same $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ value as the spot obtained from the standard solution.  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $0.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate in 10 mL of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 5.0 and 7.5.  

Purity Heavy metals —Proceed with $0.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 50 ppm).  

Water NMT $5.0\%$ $\left(0.5\,\mathrm{~g~}\right.$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

Residue on ignition NMT $2.0\%$ (1 g). However, moisten the charred residue with $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of nitric acid and 5 drops of sulfuric acid.  

Sterility It meets the requirements when used in the manufacturing of sterile preparations. However, it is exempt from the requirements there is a terminal sterilization process in the manufacturing process of sterile preparations.  

Bacterial endotoxins Less than 1.0 EU per mg (potency) of erythromycin when used in the manufacturing of sterile preparations.  

Assay Cylinder-plate method —(1) Medium: Agar media for seed and base layer  Use the medium in (A) (2) (a) $\textcircled{2}$ $\circledcirc$ under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics. However, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 7.8 to 8.0.   
(2) Test organism: Use Staphylococcus aureus ATCC 6538P as the test organism.   
(3) Weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{~mg}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Lactobionate, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . Take exactly an appropriate amount of this solution, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ to make solutions containing 20.0 $\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) and $5.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high concentration test solution and low concentration test solution, respectively. Separately, dissolve approximately $50\,\mathrm{~mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin lactobionate RS in $50\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of methanol, add $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathsf{p H}\ 8.0$ to make exactly 100 mL, and use this solution as the standard stock solution. Store the standard stock solution at below $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and use it within 7 days. Take exactly an appropriate amount of the standard stock solution, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ to make solutions containing 20.0 $\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) and $5.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high concentration standard solution and the low concentration standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test according to (A)(8) under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment  

에리트로마이신락토비온산염·콜리스틴메탄설포네이트나트륨안연고  

Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment contains NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13}$ :733.93) and colistin A $(\mathbf{C}_{53}\mathbf{H}_{100}\mathbf{N}_{16}\mathbf{O}_{13}$ : 1169.47).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Ophthalmic Ointments, with Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate. Identification (1) Erythromycin lactobionate —Put about $1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment in a stoppered flask, and turn it into liquid by warming. Add 3 mL of warmed acetone, shake vigorously to mix, cool, and take the acetone layer. Add $2\ \mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid to the solution; the resulting solution turns from orange to red, and finally to reddish purple. Add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform again and shake; the chloroform layer exhibits a purple color.  

(2) Colistin sodium methanesulfonate —Put about 1 $\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment in a stoppered flask, and turn it into liquid by warming. Add $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, shake vigorously to mix, cool, and take the water layer. Add $10\%$ sodium hydroxide solution to this solution, and shake well. Add 5 drops of $1\%$ copper sulfate solution, and shake well to mix; the resulting solution exhibits a reddish purple color.  

Sterility Meets the requirements. Foreign metallic matter Meets the requirements. Water NMT $1.0\%$ $\mathrm{~\textit~{~1.0~g~}~}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

Assay (1) Erythromycin lactobionate— Cylinder plate method (i) Medium: Agar media for seed and base layer Microbial Assays for Antibiotics  Use the medium in (i) (ii) Test organism: Use Bacillus subtilis ATCC 6633 as the test organism.  

(iii) Weigh accurately Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment, equivalent to about $25~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin, according to the labeled potency, place it in a separatory funnel, add $50\,\textrm{m L}$ of ether, shake until the mixture becomes homogeneous, and then add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $\ensuremath{\left(\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0\right)}$ . Extract three times, combine all extracts, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ , and use these solutions as the high concentration test solution and the low concentration test solution, respectively. Separately, weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin lactobionate RS, dissolve in $25\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of methanol, add 0.1 $\mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\,8.0)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and shake well to mix. Use this solution as the standard stock solution. Store the standard stock solution at a temperature NMT $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , and use it within 7 days. Pipet an appropriate amount of the standard stock solution, dilute with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\;8.0)$ to contain $2.0~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and $0.5~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high concentration standard solution and the low concentration standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test according to (i) (8) under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics. (2) Colistin sodium methanesulfonate— Cylinder plate method (i) Medium: Agar media for seed and base layer  Microbial Assays for Antibiotics  Use the medium in (ii) (2) (a) $\textcircled{1}\textcircled{a}$ .  

(ii) Test organism: Use Escherichia coli NIHJ as the test organism.  

(iii) Weigh accurately about 600000 units (potency) of Erythromycin Lactobionate and Colistin Sodium Methanesulfonate Ophthalmic Ointment according to the labeled potency of colistin to place in a separatory funnel, add $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of ether, and shake until the mixture becomes homogeneous. Extract 3 times with $10~\mathrm{mL}$ each of water, combine all extracts, and add $1\%$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\,6.0)$ to make exactly $60\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet an appropriate amount of this solution, dilute with $1\%$ phosphate buffer solution $\ensuremath{\left(\mathrm{pH}\ 6.0\right)}$ , and use these solutions as the high concentration test solution and the low concentration test solution, respectivley. Separately, weigh accurately an appropriate amount of colistin sodium methanesulfonate RS and dissolve in water. Weigh accurately an appropriate amount of the erythromycin RS in this solution, add a small amount of methanol, and add water to make a solution containing 30000 units (potency) of colistin and 1 mg (potency) of erythromycin per mL. Pipet an appropriate amount of this solution, dilute with $1\%$ phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\,6.0)$ to contain 10000 and 2500 units (potency) per mL, and use these solutions as the high concentration standard solution and the low concentration standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test according (A) (8) under the Microbial Assays for Antibiotics.

$\mathrm{C}_{55}\mathrm{H}_{103}\mathrm{NO}_{15}$ : 1018.40  

3,5,7,9,11,13-hexamethyl-oxacyclo-tetradecane-2,10- dione octadecanoate [ 643-22-1 ]  

Erythromycin Stearate is the stearate of erythromyErythromycin Stearate contains NLT $600~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ and NMT $720\,\mathrm{\;\mug}$ (potency) of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13})$ per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Erythromycin Stearate occurs as a white powder. It is freely soluble in ethanol(95) or acetone, soluble in methanol and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Dissolve $3~\mathrm{mg}$ of Erythromycin Stearate in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, and add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the resulting solution exhibits an orange color and immediately turns red to dark violet.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Erythromycin Stearate and erythromycin stearate RS, previously dried in a desiccator (in vacuum, silica gel) for 24 hours, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Stearate in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 6.0 and 11.0.  

Purity Related substances— Weigh accurately $0.165\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Stearate, transfer into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ Erlenmeyer flask, dissolve in $15~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and add 15 mL of buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}~\textrm{8.0}$ . After mixing, filter through a $0.2\ \upmu\mathrm{m}$ filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $6~\mathrm{mg}$ each of erythromycin RS, erythromycin B, erythromycin C and Ndemethylerythromycin, and dissolve them in $15\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of methanol, and add $15~\mathrm{mL}$ of buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\;8.0$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test and standard solutions as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the amount of individual related substances other than erythromycin A, erythromycin B, erythromycin C, erythromycin A enol ether and pseudoerythromycin A enol ether, and the amount of erythromycin A enol ether and pseudoerythromycin A enol ether by the following formula; NMT $3.0\%$ However, the relative retention time of pseudoerythromycin A enol ether to erythromycin A is about 1.5, and the peak areas of ethyl erythromycin A enol ether and pseudoerythromycin A enol ether are calculated by multiplying the area obtained according to the automatic integration method by the correction factors for erythromycin A of 0.09 and 0.15, respectively.  

$$
=\;30\times{\frac{C\times P}{W}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}
$$  

C: Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ of erythromycin in the standard solution  

# W: Weight (mg) of sample taken  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak areas of individual related substances other than erythromycin A, erythromycin B, erythromycin C, erythromycin A enol ether, pseudoerythromycin A enol ether, and erythromycin A enol ether and pseudoerythromycin A enol ether obtained from the test solution  

$A_{S}$ : Peak area of erythromycin A obtained from standard solution  

$p H\,\delta.O$ buffer solution —A solution prepared by dissolving $2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of dibasic potassium phosphate in water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ and adjusting $\mathrm{pH}$ to 8.0 with phosphoric acid.  

# Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $215\;\mathrm{nm})$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with spherical styrene  

divinylbenzene copolymer for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $70\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $3.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of dibasic potassium phosphate in water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and adjust $\mathrm{pH}$ to 9.0 with dilute phosphoric acid (1 in 10). To $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $400\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, $175\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $t$ -butyl alcohol, $30\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile, and add water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Flow rate: $2\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; Ndemethylerythromycin, erythromycin C, erythromycin A and erythromycin B are eluted in this order with the resolution between N-demethylerythromycin and erythromycin C being NLT 0.8, and the resolution between Ndemethylerythromycin and erythromycin A being NLT 5.5. Separately, weigh accurately $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of erythromycin RS, dissolve in $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of $\mathrm{pH}\;3.5$ buffer solution, and allow to stand for 30 minutes, and use this solution as the system suitability solution (1). Proceed with $100\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; the relative retention time of erythromycin A enol ether to that of erythromycin A is between 4.3 and 4.7.  

$p H\,3.5$ buffer solution —A solution prepared by adjusting the pH of $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of $\mathrm{pH}\ 8.0$ buffer solution to $\mathrm{pH}$ 3.5 with phosphoric acid.  

System repeatability: Weigh accurately about 40 mg of erythromycin stearate RS, transfer into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ Erlenmeyer flask, dissolve in $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add 5 mL of $\mathrm{pH}\,8.0$ buffer solution, and use this solution as the system suitability solution (2). Repeat the test 5 times with $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of this solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of Erythromycin is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Water NMT $5.0\%$ $\left.\mathrm{0.5~\mathrm{~g~}}\right$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $2.0\%$ ($\,[\,{\bf\rho}_{1}\,{\bf g})$

Apply iodine vapor or spray $10\%$ sulfuric acid on the plate to examine the spots; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Water NMT $5.0\%$ $_{\parallel.2{\mathrm{~g~}}}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).

# Erythromycin Stinoprate 에리트로마이신스티노프레이트  

![](images/5995c503bb08945c7010369d3ee4a68c64b862e01f550a48307b6cf25b29f974.jpg)  

Erythromycin Stinoprate  

$C_{40}\mathrm{H}_{71}\mathrm{NO}_{14}.\mathrm{C}_{5}\mathrm{H}_{9}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\mathrm{S}:953.18$ 2'-Propanoate erythromycin $N_{}$ -acetyl-L-cysteine (1:1), [84252-03-9 ]  

Erythromycin Stinoprate contains NLT $704~\mathrm{~\mug~}$ ( potency) of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93) per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis, and contains NLT $16.3\%$ and NMT $18.0\%$ of acetylcysteine and NLT $78.7\%$ and NMT $87.0\%$ of erythromycin propionate per mg, calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Erythromycin Stinoprate occurs as a white, crystalline powder and has a characteristic odor. It is soluble in methanol, acetone or chloroform and slightly soluble in water.  

Identification (1) Dissolve $3~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Stinoprate in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, and add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid; the resulting solution exhibits an orange color and immediately turns red to dark purple.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Erythromycin Stinoprate and erythromycin stinoprate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Midinfrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ : Between $-51^{\circ}$ and $-58^{\circ}$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~\textcent~}~}^{\mathrm{~\textcent~}}1.0\mathrm{~\textg~}$ ,calculated on the anhydrous basis, ethanol anhydrous, 50 mL, after $30\;\mathrm{min}$ ,$100\;\mathrm{mm}$ ).  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve Erythromycin Stinoprate in water to make 1 mg (potency)/mL; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of the solution is between 4.0 and 5.0.  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Perform the test with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Stinoprate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 20 ppm).  

(2) Related substances —(i) $N,N.$ -diacetylcystine: Weigh accurately about $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Stinoprate, dissolve in methanol to make $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of $N,N\!\cdot$ -diacetylcystine RS, and add methanol to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ and 6 mL of this solution, add methanol to make exactly 100 mL, and use these solutions as the detection limit solution and the standard solution. Within 30 minutes, perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test and standard solutions as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ of $N,N\!.$ -diacetylcystine from each solution (NMT $0.3\%$ ).  

$$
=\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times
$$  

𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴𝐴 (𝑚𝑚𝑚𝑚) 𝑜𝑜𝑜𝑜 𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠𝑠, 𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐𝑐 𝑜𝑜𝑜𝑜 𝑡𝑡ℎ𝑒𝑒 𝑎𝑎𝑎𝑎ℎ𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦𝑦 𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏𝑏  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $205\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of water and acetonitrile $(99:5)$ , adjusted $\mathrm{pH}$ to 2.5 with phosphoric acid. Flow rate: $2.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

(ii) Erythromycin propionate enol ether and other related substances: Weigh accurately about $0.5\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Erythromycin Stinoprate, dissolve in ethanol to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of erythromycin propionate enol ether RS, add methanol to make exactly $200~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add methanol to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the detection limit solution. Perform the test with exactly $20\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, determine the peak areas $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , of erythromycin propionate enol ether from each solution, and calculate total peak area after the erythromycin propionate peak other than the erythromycin propionate enol ether peak, $S_{\mathrm{T}}$ (NMT $0.5\%$ for each of erythromycin propionate enol ether and other related substances).  

$$
\times\,\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times25
$$  

# Content $(\%)$ of other related substances  

$$
\times\,\frac{S_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times25
$$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $205\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\ \upmu\mathrm{m}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of water and acetonitrile $(65:35)$ , adjusted $\mathrm{pH}$ to 2.5 with phosphoric acid.  

Flow rate: $2.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

(iii) Free erythromycin: Weigh $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Stinoprate, calculated on the anhydrous basis, dissolve in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $10.0~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin RS, dissolve in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with these solutions as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution to the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography (with fluorescence agent), and develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform, ethanol and $15\%$ ammonium acetate $(85:15:1)$ to a distance of about 10 cm. Spray evenly a mixture of methanol acetic anhydride sulfuric acid and anisaldehyde $(92:5:2:1)$ on the plate, and dry at $105\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for about 5 minutes. The spots of erythromycin obtained from the test solution are not more intense than the spots obtained from the standard solution $(\mathrm{NMT}\,5.0\%)$ .  

(iv) Acetylcysteine: Weigh accurately about $0.6~\mathrm{g}$ of Erythromycin Stinoprate, calculated on the anhydrous basis, and dissolve in methanol to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ .Pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add methanol to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of acetylcysteine RS, add methanol to make exactly $500~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Within 30 minutes, perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following operating conditions, and determine the peak areas $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and A S, of acetylcysteine from each solution.

# Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets 에리트로마이신스티노프레이트정  

Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $120.0\%$ of the labeled amount of erythromycin $(\mathbf{C}_{37}\mathbf{H}_{67}\mathbf{NO}_{13}$ : 733.93). Also, Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets contain NLT $16.3\%$ and NMT $18.0\%$ of acetylcysteine and NLT $78.7\%$ and NMT $87.0\%$ of erythromycin propionate, calculated on the anhydrous basis. Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Erythromycin Stinoprate.  

Identification Dissolve $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ (potency) each of Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets and erythromycin stinoprate RS in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography, and develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform, ethanol and $15\%$ ammonium acetate solution $(85:15:1)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10~\mathrm{cm}$ . Spray evenly a mixture of methanol, acetic acid(100), sulfuric acid and anisaldehyde $(92:5:2:1)$ on the plate, and heat at $105\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 5 minutes; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Purity (1) Related substances —$\circleddash$ N,N -diacetylcystine: Perform the test as directed under the Purity (2) $\textcircled{1}$ under Erythromycin Stinoprate. However, weigh accurately about $0.25\mathrm{~g~}$ (potency) of Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets according to the labeled potency, dissolve in methanol to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and then filter. Pipet $3.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add methanol to make exactly $10.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution (NMT $0.7\%$ for erythromycin stinoprate).

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets at 100 revolutions per minute for 45 minutes according to Method 1 under the Dissolution, using $900\;\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution, $\mathrm{pH}\,6.9$ , as the dissolution medium. Take $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of the dissolved solution 45 minutes after starting the dissolution test, and filter. Discard the first $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, and use the subsequent filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $55~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of erythromycin propionate RS, dissolve in acetonitrile to make exactly 100 mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $100\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Assay (4) under Erythromycin Stinoprate It meets the requirements when the dissolution rate of Erythromycin Stinoprate Tablets for 45 minutes is NLT $75\%$ of the labeled potency.
