# Disintegration Meets the requirements.  

Uniformity of dosage units It meets the requirements when the procedure for content uniformity is performed according to the following procedure.  

Transfer 1 tablet of Ethinylestradiol Tablets into a separatory funnel, add $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of Solution 2 from the Disintegration, and shake to mix until disintegration. Add 10 mL of dilute sulfuric acid and $20~\mathrm{~mL}$ of chloroform, shake vigorously for 5 minutes to mix, and filter the chloroform layer through a filter paper containing $5~\mathrm{g}$ of anhydrous sodium sulfate into an Erlenmeyer flask. Extract the water layer twice with $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ each of chloroform, proceed in the same manner, and combine with the previous filtrate. Evaporate gently on a steam bath while passing through nitrogen, add exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol to the residue, dissolve, and centrifuge, if necessary. Pipet $\upchi$ mL of the supernatant clear liquid, add methanol to obtain exactly $\mathrm{V}\,\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution containing about $0.04~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ of ethinylestradiol $\left(\mathbf{C}_{20}\mathbf{H}_{24}\mathbf{O}_{2}\right)$ per mL, and use this solu  

$$
\times\,\frac{\dot{F_{\mathrm{T}}}-\dot{F_{\mathrm{B}}}}{F_{\mathrm{S}}-F_{\mathrm{B}}}\times\frac{\dot{V}}{2500}\times\frac{1}{x}
$$  

Assay Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 tablets of Ethinylestradiol Tablets, and powder. Weigh accurately an amount equivalent to about $0.5~\mathrm{mg}$ of ethinylestradiol $(\mathbf{C}_{20}\mathbf{H}_{24}\mathbf{O}_{2})$ , transfer into a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ beaker, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and shake well to mix. Then add $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform and shake well to mix. Add $4\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of diatomaceous earth for chromatography, mix well until the contents do not adhere to the wall, and use this as the sample. Add $5\textrm{g}$ of diatomaceous earth for chromatography, previously weighed, to a $200{\-}{\mathrm{mL}}$ beaker, put $4\ \mathrm{mL}$ of 1 mol/L hydrochloric acid TS to mix thoroughly. Prepare a column for chromatography about $25~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $30\;\mathrm{cm}$ in length with a glass wool at the bottom and $5\textrm{g}$ of anhydrous sodium sulfate on top. Put the well-mixed solution to the column by pressing appropriately with a glass rod to fill the column homogeneously until the layer reaches 60 to $80\ \mathrm{mm}$ . Use this as the chromatographic column. Add the sample, using a funnel, and pack appropriately and tightly. Add $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of diatomaceous earth for chromatography to the sample sticking to the beaker, mix well, and transfer to the column. Again, wash the sample sticking to the beaker and the glass rod with glass wool, transfer to the column along with the glass wool, and press gently with a glass rod to make the height of the column to $110\textrm{-}130\textrm{m m}$ . Next, take $70~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform, and wash the inner wall of the column for chromatography. Collect the eluate at a rate of NMT 0.8 mL per minute for 1 minute. After the elution is complete, wash the bottom of the column with a small amount of chloroform, combine the washings with the eluate, add chloroform to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $10~\mathrm{\mg}$ of ethinylestradiol RS, previously dried in a desiccator (in vacuum, phosphorus pentoxide) for 4 hours, and dissolve in chloroform to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add chloroform to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Pipet $6~\mathrm{mL}$ each of the test solution, the standard solution and chloroform, transfer into a separatory funnel, and add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of isooctane. Then, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of sulfuric acid and methanol $(7:3)$ , shake vigorously for 5 minutes, allow to stand in the dark for 15 minutes, and centrifuge. Perform the test with the obtained coloring solution as directed under the Ultravioletvisible Spectroscopy using a solution, proceeded with 6 mL of chloroform in the same manner, as the control solution. Determine the absorbances of each solution, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , obtained from the test solution and the standard solution, at a wavelength of $540\;\mathrm{nm}$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers. 2-Ethylpyridine-4-carbothioamide [ 536-33-4 ]Ethionamide, when dried, contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ethionamide $\left(\mathbf{C}_{8}\mathbf{H}_{10}\mathbf{N}_{2}\mathbf{S}\right)$ .  

![](images/dd95dc9eb7a8407b5ce3b21157f851abbbc215e26feffa4d02168a4816659a00.jpg)  

Description Ethionamide occurs as yellow crystals or a crystalline powder and has a characteristic odor and taste. It is soluble in methanol and in acetic acid(100), sparingly soluble in ethanol(95), slightly soluble in ether, and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of Ethionamide and ethionamide RS in methanol (3 in 160000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Ethionamide and ethionamide RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Melting point Between $161\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and $165\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Purity (1) Acidity —Dissolve $3.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethionamide in 30 mL of methanol by warming, add $90~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, allow to stand in iced water for 1 hour, and filter. To $80~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add $0.8~\mathrm{mL}$ of cresol red TS and $0.20~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide VS; the resulting solution exhibits a red color.  

(2) Heavy metals— Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethionamide according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution $(\mathrm{NMT}\ 20\ \mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(3) Arsenic —Proceed with $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethionamide according to Method 3 and perform the test. Add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution of magnesium nitrate hexahydrate in ethanol(95) (1 in 50), then add $1.5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of hydrogen peroxide(30), and fire to burn (NMT 2 ppm).  

(4) Selenium —Weigh about $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Ethionamide and combust as directed under the Oxygen Flask Combustion with $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 30) as an absorbent. Use a combustion flask with a volume of 1000 mL, combust, wash the stopper and the inner wall of the flask with $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, and use $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water to move the solution in the combustion flask into a $150{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ beaker. Heat lightly until it boils, boil for 10 minutes, allow it to cool down to room temperature, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, pipet $6.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of standard selenium stock solution, add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 30) and $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and use this solution as the standard solution. Add diluted ammonia water(28) (1 in 2) to each of the test and standard solutions, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 2.0, add water to dilute to $60~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water to move to a separatory funnel. Then, wash the separatory funnel with $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water. Add $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride, dissolve by mixing, add $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of 2,3-diaminonaphthalene TS, and close the stopper. Mix by stirring and allow to stand at room temperature for 100 minutes. Add $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of cyclohexane, shake well, and allow to stand. If the layer is separated, remove the water layer, centrifuge cyclohexane extract, remove water, and take the cyclohexane layer. With these solutions and a control solution prepared with water added to $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 30) in the same way, perform the test as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy. Determine the absorption at the absorption maximum wavelength around 380 nm; the absorption of the solution from the test solution is not greater than the absorption from the standard solution $(\mathrm{NMT}\,30\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(5) Related substances— Perform the test without exposure to daylight using light-resistant vessels. Dissolve $0.20~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethionamide in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $0.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add acetone to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (1). Pipet $0.2~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, add acetone to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the standard solution (2). With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution, the standard solution (1) and (2) on a plate of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Develop the plate with a mixture of ethyl acetate, hexane, and methanol $(6:2:1)$ to a distance of about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254~\mathrm{nm}$ ); the spots other than the principal spot from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution (1). The number of the spots other than the principal spot from the test solution which is more intense than the spot from the standard solution (2) is NMT one. Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ (1 g, $105\;^{\circ}\!C$ , 3 hours).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.3\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethionamide, previously dried, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and titrate with $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (indicator: 2 mL of p-naphtholbenzein TS). The endpoint of titration is when the color of the solution changes from orange-red to dark orange-brown. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=16.624\;\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C}_{8}\mathrm{H}_{10}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathrm{O}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, wellclosed containers.  

# Ethosuximid 에토숙시미드  

![](images/19991d006c01e0578685f5e23283069bcb2ba3ccdb4c253874e238c3d180e64c.jpg)  

$\mathrm{C}_{7}\mathrm{H}_{11}\mathrm{NO}_{2}$ : 141.17  

3-Ethyl-3-methylpyrrolidine-2,5-dione [ 77-67-8 ]Ethosuximid contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of Ethosuximid $(\mathbf{C}_{7}\mathbf{H}_{11}\mathbf{NO}_{2})$ , calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Ethosuximid occurs as a white, paraffin-like solid or a powder. It is odorless or has a slight, characteristic odor.  

It is very soluble in methanol, ethanol(95), ether and $N{,}N.$ -dimethylformamide, and freely soluble in water.  

Melting point —About $48\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Identification (1) Add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium hydroxide TS to about $0.2\;\mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximid, and boil; the gas produced turns a moistened red litmus paper blue  

(2) Dissolve $50~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of Ethosuximide in $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of ethanol(95), add 3 drops of a solution of cupric acetate (1 in 100), warm slightly, and add 1 to 2 drops of sodium hydroxide TS; the resulting solution exhibits a purple color.  

(3) Determine the absorption spectra of ethanol(95) solutions of Ethosuximide and ethosuximide RS (1 in 2000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution —Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximide in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the solution is clear and colorless.  

(2) Chloride —Perform the test with about $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximide. Prepare the control solution with $0.30~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid (NMT $0.011\%$ ).  

(3) Heavy metals— Proceed with about $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethosuximide according to Method 1 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $20\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

(4) Arsenic —Prepare the test solution with about $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximide according to Method 1 and perform the test (NMT 2 ppm).  

(5) Acid anhydride —Dissolve about $0.50\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethosuximide in $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethanol(95), add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride-iron(III) chloride TS, and allow to stand for 5 minutes. Add $3\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water and mix. Allow to stand for 5 minutes; the red to reddish purple color of this solution is not more intense than that of the following control solution.  

Control solution —Dissolve $70~\mathrm{mg}$ of succinic anhydride in ethanol(95) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To 1.0 mL of this solution, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride-iron(III) chloride TS and proceed in the same manner.  

(6) Cyanide —Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximide in 10 mL of ethanol(95), and add 3 drops of iron(II) sulfate TS, $1\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of sodium hydroxide TS and 2 to 3 drops of iron(III) chloride TS. Warm gently, and acidify with dilute sulfuric acid; no blue precipitates are formed and a blue color is not exhibited within 15 minutes.  

(7) Related substances —Weigh accurately $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethosuximide, dissolve in the mobile phase to make 10 mL, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $10.0~\mathrm{mg}$ each of ethosuximide RS and 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid, add the mobile phase to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions; the amount of 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid by equation (1) is NMT $0.1\%$ . Calculate the amount of each related substance by equation (2): NMT $0.1\%$ , and the total amount of related substances is NMT $0.5\%$ .  

$$
=\frac{c}{w}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\left(1\right)
$$  

C:Concentration $(\mathrm{{mg/mL})}$ of 2-ethyl-2- methylsuccinic acid in the standard solution  

W: Amount of Ethosuximide taken (g) $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid obtained from the test solution  

$A_{S}$ : Peak area of 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid obtained from the standard solution  

$C$ : Concentration of Ethosuximide in the standard   
solution $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$   
$W$ : Amount of Ethosuximide taken (g)   
$A_{\mathrm{i}}$ : Peak area of each related substance obtained   
from the test solution   
A S: Peak area of Ethosuximide obtained from the   
standard solution  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $220\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $3.9\ \mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $30~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography. Mobile phase: A mixture of $\mathrm{pH}\,3.0$ phosphate buffer solution and acetonitrile $(9:1)$ .  

Flow rate: $1\ \mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Weigh accurately a suitable amount each of 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid and ethosuximide RS, dissolve in the mobile phase to obtain a solution containing $2~\mathrm{~mg}$ of 2-ethyl-2-methylsuccinic acid and $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of ethosuximide per mL, and use this solution as the system suitability solution. Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution under the above operating conditions; the resolution between the peaks of 2-ethyl-2- methylsuccinic acid and ethosuximide is NLT 6.6, the number of theoretical plates is NLT 2900, and the symmetry factor of the peak of ethosuximide is NMT 2.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the system suitability solution under the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak areas of ethosuximide and 2-ethyl-2- methylsuccinic acid is NMT $0.4\%$ , respectively.  

Phosphate buffer solution, pH 3.0 —To $4.1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of phosphoric acid add water to make $1000~\mathrm{mL}$ . To this solution, add sodium hydroxide TS to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 3.0. Water NMT $0.5\%$ ($\,2\ \mathrm{g}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Ethosuximide, previously dried, dissolve in $20\quad\mathrm{~mL~}$ of N,NDimethylformamide, and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ tetramethylammonium hydroxide VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ tetramethylammonium hydroxide Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ethyl Aminobenzoate 아미노벤조산에틸  

![](images/220b37cae4869c28810ec2a658537319f0de1868e4660308d9da35b1ff53901c.jpg)  

Benzocaine  

Ethyl 4-aminobenzoate [ 94-09-7 ]Ethyl Aminobenzoate, when dried, contains NLT $99.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ethyl aminobenzoate $\left(\boldsymbol{\mathbf{C}}\boldsymbol{\mathbf{{H}}}_{11}\boldsymbol{\mathbf{N}}\boldsymbol{\mathbf{O}}_{2}\right)$ ).  

Description Ethyl Aminobenzoate occurs as white crystals or a crystalline powder. It is odorless and has a slightly bitter taste, numbing the tongue.   
It is freely soluble in ethanol(95) or in ether and very slightly soluble in water.   
It dissolves in dilute hydrochloric acid.  

Identification (1) Dissolve $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate in $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid and $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the resulting solution responds to the Qualitative Analysis for primary aromatic amines.  

(2) Dissolve $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate in $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water with the aid of dilute hydrochloric acid added dropwise and add iodine TS dropwise; a brown precipitate is formed.  

(3) Warm $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate with 2 drops of acetic acid(31) and 5 drops of sulfuric acid; the characteristic odor of ethyl acetate comes out.  

Melting point Between 89 and $91\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Purity (1) Acid —Dissolve about $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of neutralized ethanol and add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, 2 drops of phenolphthalein TS and $0.50~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide solution; the resulting solution exhibits a red color.  

(2) Chloride —Dissolve $0.20~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate in ethanol(95) and add 2 to 3 drops each of dilute nitric acid and silver nitrate TS; there is no immediate change in the solution.  

(3) Heavy metals —Dissolve $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethanol(95) and add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute acetic acid and ethanol(95) to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Perform the test using this solution as the test solution. Prepare the control solution as follows: to $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute acetic acid and ethanol(95) to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(4) Readily carbonizable substances —Perform the test with $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate. The color of this solution is not more intense than that of the matching fluid A.  

Loss on drying NMT $1.0\%$ ($1\;\mathrm{g}$ , silica gel, 3 hours). Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$ Assay Weight accurately about $0.25\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethyl Aminobenzoate, previously dried, dissolved in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid and $70~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution of potassium bromide (3 in 10), and cool down to a temperature below $15~^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ . Then, titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium nitrite VS. (potentiometric titration or amperometric titration under the Titrimetry).  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

![](images/ad2ab520aa1be18923cb48cdb6f077a5ae481ed725c5d924ee9c758be3daecbc.jpg)  

Ethyl Linoleate  

$$
{\bf C}_{20}{\bf H}_{36}{\bf O}_{2}
$$  

308.50   
Ethyl (9 Z,12 Z)-9,12-octadecadienoic acid ester, [ 544-35- 4 ]  
Ethyl Linoleate contains NLT $88.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ethyl linoleate $(\mathrm{C}_{20}\mathrm{H}_{36}\mathrm{O}_{2}:308.50)$ ).  

Description Ethyl Linoleate occurs as a colorless to pale yellow and clear liquid. It has a slightly characteristic odor.  

It is soluble in methanol, ethanol, ether, chloroform or petroleum ether.  

Identification To about $4\textrm{g}$ of Ethyl Linoleate, add 20 mL of potassium hydroxide-ethanol TS, and heat on a steam bath with a reflux condenser attached for 30 minutes. After cooling, add dilute hydrochloric acid to make the solution acidic. Transfer it to a separatory funnel, take the separated oil layer, wash with $2\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of ligroin for mixing. To this solution, add $3\mathrm{\g}$ of anhydrous sodium sulfate, allow the solution to stand for 10 minutes, and filter. Well shake and maintain the filtrate at between 10 and $15\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , add $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of bromine, and allow it to stand for 30 minutes with occasional shaking. Take the produced precipitate, wash with $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of ligroin 3 times for recrystallization, dry in a desiccator, and determine the melting point of the dried material. The melting point is between 113 and $117\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Specific gravity $\mathrm{d}_{20}^{20}$ : Between 0.875 and 0.885. Refractive index $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ :Between 1.455 and 1.465. Saponification value Between 180 and 185.  

Acid value NMT 15.  

Iodine value Between 150 and 163 (when the test is performed with $0.15\;\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Linoleate).  

Purity (1) Chloride ―To $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Linoleate, add Ethanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of silver nitrateethanol solution (1 in 50). The turbidity of the solution is not greater than the following control solution. Control solution: To $0.40~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ Hydrochloric Acid, add Ethanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ and add $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of silver nitrate-ethanol solution (1 in 50).  

(2) Heavy metals ―Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Linoleate in ethanol, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute acetic acid and ethanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution and perform the test with this solution. Prepare the control solution by adding $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute acetic acid and $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution as well as ethanol to make 50 mL (NMT $20\,\mathrm{ppm}]$ ).  

(3) Arsenic ―To $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethyl Linoleate, add 10 mL of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2) and $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of ether, shake vigorously for 3 minutes to mix, allow to stand, and perform the test with this solution (NMT 2 ppm).  

(4) Peroxide ―Put $10.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform in a 250 mL stoppered flask and replace the air in the flask with dry carbon dioxide. Weigh accurately $1\textrm{g}$ of Ethyl Linoleate and put it in a glass cup. Put the glass cup in the flask and slowly shake to mix and dissolve. To this, add $15.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100) and $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of saturated potassium iodide solution, stopper the flask, shake well for 1 minute to mix, and allow to stand in the dark for 5 minutes. Add $75~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, stopper the flask, shake vigorously to mix, and allow to stand in the dark for 5 minutes. Then, add $75\,\textrm{m L}$ of water, stopper the flask, shake vigorously to mix, and titrate with $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate VS (indicator: starch TS). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

$$
{\mathrm{Peroxide~value}}\,={\frac{\mathrm{(A-B)}}{{\mathrm{Amount}}\,({\mathrm{g}})\;{\mathrm{of}}\;{\mathrm{sample}}}}\times\,10
$$  

A: Consumed amount (mL) of $0.01\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate VS used for the sample  

B: Consumed amount (mL) of $0.01\;\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate VS used for the blank test  

Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g). Put $1{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Ethyl Linoleate in a crucible, previously weighed accurately its mass, and weigh accurately the mass. Heat with weak flame to boil, stop heating once boiling starts, and directly fire to burn. After cooling, wet the residue with 1 or 2 drops of sulfuric acid, carefully ignite to a constant mass, and weigh the mass of the residue.  

Assay Weigh accurately about $60~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ethyl Linoleate and put it in a glass cup. Heat potassium hydroxideglycerin solution at $100~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and put $10\ \mathrm{mL}$ each of this solution to 3 stoppered test tubes (A, B and C). Place a thermometer in the stoppered test tube C. Put the 3 stoppered test tubes in a $180\pm3~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ oil bath and heat until the thermometer in the stoppered test tube C indicates $180\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . Then, blow nitrogen gas into the stoppered test tubes A and B. Take the stoppered test tubes from the oil bath. Place the glass cup containing the sample in the stoppered tube A, place an empty glass cup in the stoppered test tube B, shake vigorously the 3 stoppered test tubes for 2 minutes, and place the 3 stoppered test tubes in the oil bath. When the temperature of the stoppered test tube reaches $175\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , heat for exactly 45 minutes. For at least 30 minutes of this period, take care to maintain $180~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . Take out the stoppered test tubes A and B from the oil bath and cool them down to $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . Wash them with hot methanol, place each in a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, cool, and add methanol to make $100.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ each. To $10.0\,\textrm{m L}$ each of the solutions, add methanol to make $100.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ each, and use each of the resulting solutions as the solution A and solution B, respectively. Perform the test with the solution A, using the solution B for comparison, as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy and determine the absorbance at the wavelength 268 nm, $A_{268}$ . Additionally, to $10.0~\mathrm{mL}$ each of the solutions A and B, add methanol to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ each, and use these solutions as the solution $\mathrm{{A}}'$ and solution $\mathbf{B}^{\bullet}$ , respectively. Perform the test with the solution $\mathbf{A}^{\bullet}$ , using the solution $\mathbf{B}^{\bullet}$ for comparison, as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy and determine the absorbance at the wavelength $233\;\mathrm{nm}$ ,$A_{233}$ .  

$$
=\frac{\mathrm{A}}{93.7}\times\,100
$$  

$$
\mathrm{A}=A_{233}\times{\frac{10}{\mathrm{W}}}-1206\times A_{268}\times{\frac{1}{\mathrm{W}}}
$$  

Potassium hydroxide-glycerin TS —Add glycerin to $17.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of potassium hydroxide and warm to dissolve to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight  

# Ethyl Loflazepate 에틸로플라제페이트  

![](images/7e4ac47c8a4f856774330ad0cfe8fa0e5855f87efc0537af865f69fd840bd8d9.jpg)  

Ethyl Loflazepate $\mathrm{C_{18}H_{14}C l F N_{2}O_{3}}$ : 360.77 Ethyl 7-chloro-5-(2-fluorophenyl)-2,3 -dihydro-2-oxo1 H-1,4-benzodiazepine-3-carboxylic acid ester, [ 29177- 84-2 ]  

Ethyl Loflazepate contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $102.0\%$ of ethyl loflazepate ( $\mathrm{\bf\{C}_{18}H_{14}C l F N_{2}O_{3}}$ : 360.77).  

Description Ethyl Loflazepate is white to pale yellow powder.  

It is freely soluble in chloroform, soluble in acetonitrile, slightly soluble in ethanol(95) and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Weigh $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ethyl Loflazepate, dissolve in dichloromethane to make $4~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Weigh $20~\mathrm{~mg~}$ of ethyl loflazepate RS, dissolve in dichloromethane to make 4 mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform, diisopropyl ether and ethanol(95) $(14:5:1)$ as the developing solvent, and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254~\mathrm{nm}$ ); the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ value and the color of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Ethyl Loflazepate and ethyl loflazepate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) Determine the absorption spectra with a solution of Ethyl Loflazepate in ethanol(95) (1 in 100000); it exhibits maxima at wavelengths of about $231\ \mathrm{nm}$ and 318 nm.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution —Dissolve $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Ethyl Loflazepate in chloroform to make $10~\mathrm{mL}$ ; the solution is clear.  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $4.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethyl Loflazepate as directed under Method 4 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $4.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 40 ppm).  

(3) Related substances —Dissolve $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ethyl Loflazepate in dichloromethane to make exactly $4~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of ethyl loflazepate RS, dissolve in dichloromethane to make exactly $4~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution I. Pipet $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of the standard solution I, add dichloromethane to make exactly $200~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution II. Pipet $2\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution II, dilute with the same solvent to make exactly $5~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution III. Pipet $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution III, dilute with the same solvent to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution IV. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solutions on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform, diisopropyl ether and ethanol(95) $(14:5:1)$ as the developing solvent, air-dry the plate, and examine it under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\;\;\mathrm{nm}\rangle$ ); The spots other than the principal spot obtained from the test solution are not more intense nor greater than the spots obtained from the standard solution II.  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.2\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.2\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethyl Loflazepate, dissolve in $40\,\textrm{m L}$ of a mixture of acetic anhydride and acetic acid(100) $(3:1)$ , and titrate with 0.1 $\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=36.08~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C_{18}H_{14}C l F N_{2}O_{3}}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ethyl Loplazepate Tablets 에틸로플라제페이트정  

Ethyl Loplazepate Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount of ethyl loflazepate $\mathrm{(C_{18}H_{14}C l F N_{2}O_{3}}$ : 360.77).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Ethyl Loflazepate.  

Identification Weigh an amount of Ethyl Loplazepate Tablets, equivalent to about $4~\mathrm{mg}$ of ethyl loflazepate. Add $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile, shake to mix, then filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, dissolve 20 mg of ethyl loflazepate RS in $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile, and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $.0\ \upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform, diisopropyl ether and ethanol(95) $(14:5:1)$ ) as the developing solvent to a distance of about $12\ \mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\,\mathrm{\nm}$ ); the colors and $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Disintegration Meets the requirements.  

# Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements.  

Assay Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 tablets of Ethyl Loplazepate Tablets, and powder. Weigh accurately an amount, equivalent to about $8~\mathrm{mg}$ of ethyl loflazepate $(\mathrm{C}_{18}\mathrm{H}_{14}\mathrm{ClFN}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{3})$ , and add ethanol(95) to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Filter this solution, discard the first $20\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the subsequent filtrate, add ethanol(95) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about 20 mg of ethyl loflazepate RS, and dissolve in ethanol(95) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add ethanol(95) to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy using ethanol(95) as a control solution, and determine the absorbances, $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and A S, at a wavelength of $231\ \mathrm{nm}$ .  

Amount (mg) of ethyl loflazepate $\left({\bf C}_{18}\mathrm{H}_{14}\mathrm{ClFN}_{2}{\bf O}_{3}\right)$ $=$ Amount $(\mathrm{mg})$ of ethyl loflazepate $\mathrm{RS}\times(A_{\mathrm{T}}/A_{\mathrm{S}})\times0.4$ Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

![](images/9069e9e7a8fd353c968aca199b09390fb8b455a8f4ac6ea546079f0a0fc5ecb1.jpg)  

Ethylene Oxide $C_{2}\mathrm{H}_{4}\mathrm{O}:44.05$ Ethylene Oxide, [ 75-21-8 ]  
Ethylene Oxide contains NLT $99.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ethylene oxide $\left({\bf C}_{2}{\bf H}_{4}{\bf O}\right)$ .Description Ethylene Oxide occurs as a colorless and clear liquid at 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  
It has a weak ether odor when vaporized.   
It is very soluble in water, ethanol(95), acetone or ether at 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Identification To $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of Ethylene Oxide, previously cooled to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, 2 drops of phenolphthalein TS and $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium chloride solution (1 in 5), and allow to stand for 5 minutes; the solution exhibits a reddish purple color.  

Purity (1) Aldehyde ―In a $250{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ Erlenmeyer flask, add about $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and cool to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ in iced water. To this, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.2\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium bisulfite and allow to stand for 30 minutes in iced water. Titrate with $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ iodine VS, previously cooled to 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (indicator: $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of starch TS). However, the endpoint of titration is when the blue color persists for 1 minute. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction (NMT $0.03\%$ of acetaldehyde).  

$$
={\frac{(B-A)\times0.0022}{10\times G}}\times100
$$  

A : Consumed amount (mL) of $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ iodine VS $B$ : Amount (mL) of $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ iodine VS consumed for the blank test  

$G$ : Specific gravity of ethylene oxide at 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (2) Chloride ―Perform the test with $4.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of Ethylene Oxide, previously cooled to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , as directed under the Chloride. Prepare the control solution with 1.0 mL of $0.01\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid VS (NMT $0.01\%$ ). Water NMT $0.05\%$ $20.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of Ethylene Oxide previously cooled to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

The above test should be performed at 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Acidity Evaporate $68.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of Ethylene Oxide, previously cooled to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , to the volume of about $50~\mathrm{mL}$ in a fume chamber to eliminate carbon dioxide. Titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide VS (indicator: 3 to 4 drops of phenolphthalein TS) (NMT $0.005\%$ as acetic acid).  

Residue on evaporation Evaporate $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of Ethylene Oxide, previously cooled to 0 to $5~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , in a crucible, previously measured in the mass, in a fume chamber and dry at $105\pm2~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour. Place in a desiccator, allow to stand for 30 minutes, cool to the room temperature, and measure the mass (NMT $0.03\%$ ).  

$$
=\cfrac{A-B-C}{20\times G}\times100
$$  

A : Mass (g) of the crucible measured after placing the sample in it and heating  

$B$ : Mass $(\mathrm{g})$ of the crucible $C$ : Mean mass (g) of the blank test mass difference $G$ : Specific gravity of ethylene oxide at 0 to $5\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Assay Connect and fix Ethylene Oxide to a connector, attach the needle valve for flow rate control, and allow to stand for NLT 30 minutes. Slowly open the needle valve for flow rate control, exhaust the Ethylene Oxide into a container containing water, and control bubbles so that 3 to 4 bubbles appear per second. Introduce the gas to the gas collector for 2 minutes, inject the conversion valve for 2 seconds, and perform the test as directed under the Gas Chromatography according to the following conditions.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: A thermal conductivity detector (TCD) Column: A column about $4\;\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $3\,\textrm{m}$ in length, packed with 80- to 100-mesh divinylbenzene-ethylene glycol-dimethylacrylate copolymer for gas chromatography.  

Column temperature: $120\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$   
Detector temperature: $225\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$   
Carrier gas: Helium   
Flow rate: Between 40 mL/min and 50 mL/min.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate 에틸모르핀염산염수화물  

![](images/5abdad76569951e880f6ac5aa1b06f25532ee22e9911f058d7b3946e4239a336.jpg)  

Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride  

$\mathrm{C}_{19}\mathrm{H}_{23}\mathrm{NO}_{3}$ ·HCl· $2\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{O}$ : 385.88 $(4R,4\mathrm{a}R,7S,7\mathrm{a}R,12\mathrm{b}S)$ -9-Ethoxy-3-methyl-2,4,4a,7,7a,13- hexahydro$1H$ -4,12-methanobenzofuro[3,2-  

Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ethylmorphine hydrochloride ( $\mathrm{{C}_{19}H_{23}N O_{3}}$ ·HCl: 349.85), calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate occurs as white to pale yellow crystals or a crystalline powder.  

It is very soluble in methanol or acetic acid(100), freely soluble in water, soluble in ethanol(95), sparingly soluble in acetic anhydride and practically insoluble in ether. It is affected by light.  

Melting point —About $123\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition). Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of aqueous solutions of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate and ethylmorphine hydrochloride RS (1 in 10000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelength.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate and ethylmorphine hydrochloride RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) An aqueous solution of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate (1 in 50) responds to the Qualitative Analysis (2) for chloride.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ : Between $-103^{\circ}$ and $-106^{\circ}$ $\left.\mathrm{0.4~g}\right.$ calculated on the anhydrous basis, water, $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , 100 mm).  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $0.10\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 4.0 and 6.0.  

Purity Related substances —Dissolve $0.20\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate in $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of diluted ethanol (1 in 2) and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $0.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add diluted ethanol (1 in 2) to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of ethanol(99.5), toluene, acetone and ammonia water(28) $(14:14:7:1)$ as a developing solvent to a distance of about $10\;\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ); the spots other than the principal spot from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution.  

Water Between $8.0\%$ and $10.0\%$ ($\mathbf{0.25\,\mathrm{~g~}}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (0.5 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ethylmorphine Hydrochloride Hydrate, dissolve in $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of acetic anhydride and acetic acid(100) $(7:3)$ , and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=34.985~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C}_{19}\mathrm{H}_{23}\mathrm{NO}_{3}$ ·HCl  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Etizolam 에티졸람  

![](images/d0dee0d808603c65e4895cf381853adc8a7e23ae417e808df2db0d8117d85970.jpg)  

Etizolam $\mathrm{C_{17}H_{15}C l N_{4}S:342.85}$ 7-(2-Chlorophenyl)-4-ethyl-13-methyl-3-thia-1,8,11,12- tetraazatricyclo[8.3.0.02,6}]trideca-2(6),4,7,10,12- pentaene [ 40054-69-1 ]Etizolam contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of etizolam $(\mathbf{C}_{17}\mathbf{H}_{15}\mathbf{C}\mathrm{lN}_{4}\mathbf{S})$ ). Description Etizolam occurs as a white to pale yellowish white crystalline powder.  

It is soluble in ethanol(99.5), sparingly soluble in acetonitrile or acetic anhydride, and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of the solutions of Etizolam and etizolam RS in ethanol(99.5) (1 in 100000) as directed under the Ultravioletvisible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Etizolam and etizolam RS as directed in potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Absorption Spectrophotometry; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Melting point Between 146 and $149\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Purity (1) Heavy metals Proceed with $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Etizolam according to Method 2 and perform the test Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 10 ppm).  

(2) Related substances Dissolve $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Etizolam in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile, and use this solution as the test solution. Take exactly $1.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution and add acetonitrile to make exactly $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . Pipet $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add acetonitrile to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Determine the peak area of each solution as directed in the automatic integration method; each peak area other than that of etizolam from the test solution is not greater than the peak area of etizolam from the standard solution.  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $240\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $35\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $1.36\mathrm{~g~}$ of potassium dihydrogen phosphate in water to make $1000\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and add diluted phosphoric acid (1 in 10) to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 3.5. To $550\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $450\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile. Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of etizolam is about 6 minutes.  

# System suitability  

Test for required detectability: Pipet $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution and add acetonitrile to make exactly 20 mL. Confirm that the peak area of etizolam obtained from $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution is equivalent to 8 to $12\%$ of the peak area of etizolam from the standard solution.  

System performance: Dissolve $0.02\,\mathrm{~g~}$ each of Epizolam and ethylparaben in the mobile phase to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add the mobile phase to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; ethylparaben and etizolam are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 3.0. System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of etizolam is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Time span of measurement: About 5 times the retention time of etizolam after the solvent peak.  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ ($1~\mathrm{g}$ ,$105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 3 hours).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.3~\mathrm{g}$ of Etizolam, previously dried, dissolve in $70~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of acetic anhydride and acetic acid(100) $(7:3)$ , and titrate with 0.1 $\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). The endpoint of the titration is the second inflection point. Perform a blank test in the same way and make a necessary correction.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Etodolac 에토돌락  

![](images/a5b6b48da098262128c69213582c551f25501e24676c2658d10d9fbca7e0cc63.jpg)  
$\mathrm{C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}$ : 287.35  

2-(1,8-Diethyl-4,9-dihydro-3H-pyrano[3,4-b]indol-1- yl)acetic acid [ 41340-25-4 ]  

Etodolac contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $102.0\%$ of etodolac $\left(\mathbf{C}_{17}\mathbf{H}_{21}\mathbf{N}\mathbf{O}_{3}\right)$ , calculated on the anhydrous basis. Description Etodolac occurs as white to pale yellow crystals or a crystalline powder.  

It is freely soluble in methanol or ethanol(99.5) and practically insoluble in water.  

A solution of Etodolac in methanol (1 in 50) shows no optical rotation.  

Melting point —About $147\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition). Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of solutions of Etodolac and etodolac RS in ethanol(99.5) (1 in 200000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Etodolac and etodolac RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Purity (1) Chloride —Dissolve about $0.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of Etodolac in $30\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add water to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Prepare the control solution by adding $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol and water to $0.42~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ (NMT $0.03\%$ ).  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Etodolac according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 10 ppm).  

(3) Methanol and ethanol —Dissolve about $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Etodolac, weighed accurately, in $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ each of methanol and ethanol(95), add $N{,}N$ -dimethylformamide to make exactly $200~\mathrm{~mL~}$ . Pipet $5.0\ \mathrm{\mL}$ of this solution, add $N,N\!-$ dimethylformamide to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard stock solution. Pipet $10.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard stock solution, add $5.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of the internal standard, dilute with $N,N_{\!}$ -dimethylformamide to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $1\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Gas Chromatography according to the following conditions, and calculate the ratios, $Q_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $Q\mathrm{s}$ , of the peak areas of methanol and ethanol in Etodolac to that of the internal standard for the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. The contents of methanol and ethanol is NMT $0.1\%$ , respectively.  

$$
=500\times{\frac{C}{W}}\times{\frac{Q_{\mathrm{T}}}{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}}
$$  

C: Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ ) of ethanol or methanol in the standard solution  

W: Weight (mg) of Etodolac in the test solution Internal standard solution —Dissolve a suitable quantity of 2-propanol in $N,N_{\!}$ -dimethylformamide to make a solution with a concentration of $2.5\ \upmu\mathrm{L}/\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and dilute this solution with $N,N\!\cdot$ -dimethylformamide to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Operating conditions  

Detector: A hydrogen flame ionization detector Column: A fused silica capillary column $0.32\;\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25\textrm{m}$ in length, coated with a $5~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ film of $1\%$ vinyl– ${}_{-5\%}$ phenylmethylpolysiloxane for gas chromatography.  

Carrier gas: Helium Flow rate: $50\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ Sample injection port temperature: $200\,^{\circ}\!C$ Detector temperature: $300\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Column temperature: Maintain the temperature of $45\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 5 minutes, then raise to $280~^{\circ}\!C$ at the rate of 30 $^\circ C$ per minute, and maintain at $280\,^{\circ}\!C$ for 27 minutes.  

System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $1~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution under the above operating conditions; methanol, ethanol, and 2-propanol are eluted in this order with the resolution between their peaks being NLT 1.0. (4) Related substances —Dissolve $25~\mathrm{~mg~}$ of Etodolac, weighted accurately, in acetonitrile to make exactly $250~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the test solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Each peak area of any peak other than the major peak from the test solution is NMT $0.5\%$ to the total area of all peaks, and the total area is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

$$
=\,100\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}
$$  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Each peak area of the peaks other than the principle peak  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $214\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4\,\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (3 to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: Control the mixing ratio of mobile phase A and mobile phase B in stages or gradient elution as follows. For the first 5 minutes, use mixture of $60\%$ solution A and $40\%$ solution B as the mobile phase. For the next 30 minutes, change the mixture ratio as linear gradient to finally make mixture of $20\%$ solution A and $80\%$ solution B. Adjust mobile phase to $40\%$ of solution B before injection of the test solution and the standard solution, and keep re-equilibrium.  

Mobile phase A: Mix $0.6\ \mathrm{mL}$ of phosphoric acid with $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water.  

Mobile phase B: Mix $0.6~\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphoric acid with $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile.  

Flow rate: $1\ \mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Dissolve suitable amount each of etodolac related substance I RS and etodolac RS in acetonitrile to make solutions containing $10~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ of etodolac related substance I RS and $0.2~\mathrm{mg}$ of etodolac RS per mL, respectively. Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution as directed under the above operating conditions; etodolac related substance I and etodolac are eluted in this order with the resolution between their peaks being NLT 3.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the ratio of the peak area is NMT $3\%$ .  

Water NMT $0.5\%$ ($\mathbf{\nabla}^{2}\,\mathbf{g}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.23\mathrm{~g~}$ of Etodolac, dissolve in $60~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ tetrabutylammonium hydroxide VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ tetrabutylammonium hydroxide VS $=28.735~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers. Etodolac Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount of etodolac $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\right.$ :287.36).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Etodolac.  

Identification The retention time of the major peak of the test solution corresponds to that of the standard solution, as obtained in the Assay.  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Etodolac Tablets at 100 revolutions per minute according to Method 1 under the Dissolution, using $1000\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of $\mathsf{p H}\,\,6.8$ phosphate buffer solution as the dissolution medium. Take $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of the dissolved solution 30 minutes after starting the test, and filter through a membrane filter with a pore size of NMT $0.8\ \upmu\mathrm{m}$ . Discard the first $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate and use the subsequent filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{~mg~}$ of etodolac RS, dissolve in the dissolution medium to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and add the dissolution medium to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy at the absorbance maximum wavelength of about $274~\mathrm{nm}$ , using the dissolution medium as a control solution.  

The acceptable dissolution criterion is NLT $80\%$ of Etodolac Tablets dissolved in 30 minutes.  

Dissolution rate $(\%)$ of the labeled amount of etodolac  

$$
\begin{array}{c}{\mathrm{{(C_{17}H_{21}N O_{3})}}}\\ {=W_{\mathrm{{S}}}\times\displaystyle\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\displaystyle\frac{100}{\mathrm{C}}}\end{array}
$$  

$W_{S}$ : Amount $(\mathrm{mg})$ of etodolac RS $C$ : Labeled amount $\left(\mathrm{mg}\right)$ of etodolac $\left(\mathbf{C}_{17}\mathbf{H}_{21}\mathbf{N}\mathbf{O}_{3}\right)$ ) in 1 tablet  

Uniformity of dosage units It meets the requirements when the Content uniformity test is performed according to the following procedure. Take 1 tablet of Etodolac Tablets, add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution, and shake to mix until disintegration. Then, add phosphate buffer solution to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and centrifuge. Take $\chi\,\textrm{m L}$ of the clear supernatant, add phosphate buffer solution to obtain $V\,\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution having known concentration of about $25~\mathrm{~\mug~}$ of etodolac $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\right)$ per mL, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{mg}$ of the etodolac RS, and dissolve in phosphate buffer solution to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add phosphate buffer solution to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy at the absorbance maximum wavelength at about $274\;\mathrm{nm}$ .  

Assay Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 tablets of Etodolac Tablets, and powder. Weigh accurately an amount, equivalent to about $0.1\ \ \mathrm{~g~}$ of etodolac $\left(\mathsf{C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\right)$ , add $30\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of the mobile phase, shake to mix for 15 minutes, and sonicate for 5 minutes to mix. After cooling, add $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Allow to stand for 10 minutes, then take $10.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and filter. Use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $20~\mathrm{~mg~}$ of etodolac RS, dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of etodolac in each solution.  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $274\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $3~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of acetonitrile, water, and phosphoric acid $(500:500:0.25)$ .  

Flow rate: $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

System performance: Dissolve an appropriate amount of etodolac related substance I RS and etodolac RS in acetonitrile to make a solution containing $10~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ of etodolac related substance I RS and $0.2~\mathrm{mg}$ of etodolac RS per mL. Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution as directed under the above conditions; etodolac related substance I and etodolac are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 3.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area is NMT $3\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Etodolac Micronized 미분화에토돌락  

![](images/fff1be6a7d2a0c8b3d449c351336270576eb6c7759ec69f88a9088b597498008.jpg)  

Etodolac Micronized $\mathrm{C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}$ : 287.36 (1 S)-1,8-Diethyl-1,3,4,9-tetrahydropyrano[3,4-b]indole1-acetic acid, [ 87249-11-4 ]  

Etodolac Micronized contains NLT $97.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of etodolac $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\right)$ ), calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Etodolac Micronized occurs as a white fine crystalline powder.  

It is very soluble in polyethylene glycol 400, freely soluble in ethanol, methanol or chloroform and practically insoluble in water.  

Melting point —Between 145 and $148\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Identification (1) Perform the test with Etodolac Micronized as directed in article (2) of the Purity; the spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution show the same $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ value and color.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Etodolac Micronized and etodolac RS as directed in the paste method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) The retention time of the major peak of the test solution corresponds to that of the standard solution, as obtained in the Assay.  

Purity (1) Heavy metals— Proceed with $1.0\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Etodolac Micronized as directed under Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 10 ppm).  

(2) Related substances —Weigh accurately about $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of Etodolac Micronized, add acetone to make 100 mL, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $0.10~\mathrm{g}$ of etodolac RS, dissolve in acetone to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. To $25.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of the standard solution, add acetone to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the diluted standard solution. Perform the test with the test solution, the standard solution and the diluted standard solution as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Immerse a plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography (with florescent agent) in a solution prepared by dissolving $0.5\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of ascorbic acid in a mixture of water and ethanol (1 in 5) to make $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and air-dry the plate. Apply $25\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution and $2~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the diluted standard solution on the plate. Develop the plate with a mixture of toluene, acetic acid and ethanol $(70:50:30)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of $16\;\mathrm{cm}$ to $18~\mathrm{cm}$ , and airdry the plate for 30 minutes. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254\,\mathrm{\nm}$ ); the spots other than the principal spot from the test solution are not greater or more intense than the spot from the diluted standard solution.  

Particle size Place a small amount of Etodolac Micronized on a microscope slide, add 1 to 2 drops of mineral oil, mix well, and disperse. Then, cover it with a coverslip and measure the particle size with a microscope with a magnification of 40 to 400 times. Measure the size of all particles in the micrometer range of particle size measurement, and repeat the test more than three times; the average particle size should be NMT $8~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ , and the percentage of the number of particles NMT $20\ \upmu\mathrm{m}$ should be NLT $95\%$ .  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Etodolac Micronized and dissolve in methanol to make $100.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ .Pipet $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution and add methanol to make $50.0~\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of etodolac RS and proceed in the same manner as in the preparation of the test solution. Use the resulting solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution according to the following conditions as directed under the Liquid Chromatography, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of etodolac in each solution.  

Operating conditions   
Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).   
Column: A stainless steel column about $4\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $30~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).   
Mobile phase: A mixture of buffer solution, methanol and acetonitrile $(68:19:13)$ .  
Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

Buffer solution —To 0.5 mol/L potassium dihydrogen phosphate, add $200~\mathrm{mL}$ of water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

# Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Etodolac Micronized Capsules 미분화에토돌락캡슐  

Etodolac Micronized Capsules contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ the labeled amount of etodolac $(\mathrm{C_{10}H_{21}N O_{3}:287.36})$ .  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Capsules, with Etodolac Micronized.  

Identification The retention times of the major peaks from the test solution and standard solution obtained under the Assay are the same.  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 capsule of Etodolac Micronized Capsules at 100 revolutions per minute according to Method 1, using $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphate buffer solution $({\mathrm{pH}}\ 7.5)$ as the dissolution medium. Take the dissolved solution 45 minutes after the start of the dissolution, filter, take $4.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, and add phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\,7.5)$ to make $25.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of etodolac RS, dissolve in phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\,7.5)$ , make the same concentration as the test solution, and use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances, $\mathrm{A_{T}}$ and $\mathrm{A}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , of the test solution and the standard solution, at $278~\mathrm{nm}$ as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy, using phosphate buffer solution $(\mathrm{pH}\ 7.5)$ as the control solution. It meets the requirements if the dissolution rate in 45 minutes is NLT $75\%$ .  

# Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements.  

Assay Weigh accurately the contents of NLT 20 capsules of Etodolac Micronized Capsules and powder. Weigh an amount equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of etodolac $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{3}\right)$ , add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide to make $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , sonicate for 30 minutes, and centrifuge. Take $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the clear supernatant, add the mobile phase to make $50.0~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of etodolac RS, add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide to make $100.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Take an appropriate amount of this solution to obtain a solution having known concentration of $10~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ per mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak area of etodolac, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , respectively.  

Operating conditions   
Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4\,\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $30~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of phosphate buffer (pH 4.75) and acetonitrile buffer $(55:45)$ .  
Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$

Take $1.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the clear supernatant, add the mobile phase to make $50.0~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about 50 mg of etodolac RS, and dissolve in $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid to make $100.0~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take an appropriate amount of this solution, prepare a solution containing $10~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ per mL, and use this solution as the standard solution. Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $225\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).

Mobile phase: A mixture of phosphate buffer solu  

tion, $\mathrm{pH}\,4.75$ , and acetonitrile $(55:45)$ .Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers. Loss on drying $0.5\%$ ($\mathrm{~1~g,~}105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C,}$ 2 hours).

# Etofylline Nicotinate 에토필린니코티네이트  

# Etofylline Nicotinate Injection 에토필린니코티네이트주사액  

![](images/d1719d340a8d9ffcd33ba7219b7a552d6362ae3aaafec9434fc5d93ea52c92f7.jpg)  

Etofylline Nicotinate $\mathrm{C_{15}H_{15}N_{5}O_{4}}$ : 329.31 2-(1,2,3,6-Tetrahydro-1,3-dimethyl-2,6-dioxo$.7H$ -purin7-yl)ethyl 3-pyridinecarboxylic acid ester, [ 13425-39-3 ]Etofylline Nicotinate, when dried, contains NLT $99.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of etofylline nicotinate $\left({\bf C}_{15}\mathrm{H}_{15}\mathrm{N}_{5}\mathrm{O}_{4}\right)$ .  

Description Etofylline Nicotinate occurs as a white crystalline powder, is odorless and has a bitter taste.  

Identification (1) Add 10 drops of $3\%$ hydrogen peroxide and 3 drops of hydrochloric acid to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of Etofylline Nicotinate, mix well, and evaporate to dryness. Add a few drops of $10\%$ ammonia water to the residue on evaporation; it exhibits dark red color.  

(2) Determine the absorption spectrum as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy with a solution of Etofylline Nicotinate in hydrochloric acid (1 in 10000); it exhibits a maximum at about $268\;\mathrm{nm}$ .  

Melting point Between 151 and $152\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution— Weigh $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Etofylline Nicotinate in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform; the resulting solution is clear and colorless.  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Etofylline Nicotinate as directed under Method 1 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

Etofylline Nicotinate Injection is an aqueous injection and contains NLT $95.0\%$ and NMT $105.0\%$ of etofylline nicotinate $\mathrm{(C_{15}H_{15}N_{5}O_{4}\,;\,329.31}$ ).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Injections, with Etofylline Nicotinate.  

Identification (1) To an amount of Etofylline Nicotinate Injection equivalent to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of etofylline nicotinate, add 10 drops of $3\%$ hydrogen peroxide and 3 drops of hydrochloric acid, shake to mix, evaporate in an evaporating dish until a reddish brown residue forms, and add a few drops of $10\%$ ammonia water; the solution exhibits a dark red color.  

(2) Take an amount of Etofylline Nicotinate Injection equivalent to $25~\mathrm{mg}$ of etofylline nicotinate according to the labeled amount, extract in $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform, and add chloroform to $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the extract to make $100.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of etofylline nicotinate RS in $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on a thinlayer chromatographic plate made of silica gel with fluorescent indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Develop the plate with a mixture of chloroform and methanol $\left(9:\right.$ 1) as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10\;\mathrm{cm}$ ,and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly a phosphomolybdic acid ethanol solution on the plate, dry at $120~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ and apply iodine vapor to the plate; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values and colors of spots obtained from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

(3) Take an amount of Etofylline Nicotinate Injection, equivalent to $10\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of etofylline nicotinate, add $0.05~\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid to make exactly $100\ \mathrm{mL}$ ,and filter. Take $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid to make $100.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ , and measure the absorbance spectrum as directed under Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; it exhibits a maximum around $268~\mathrm{nm}$ .  

Sterility Meets the requirements. Bacterial endotoxins Less than 3 EU per mg of etofylline nicotinate.  

Particulate contamination: Visible particles Meets the requirements.  

Insoluble particulate matter in injections Meets the requirements.  

Extractable volume of injections Meets the requirements.  

Assay Take an amount of Etofylline Nicotinate Injection equivalent to $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of etofylline nicotinate $\left({\bf C}_{15}\mathrm{H}_{15}\mathrm{N}_{5}\mathrm{O}_{4}\right)$ according to the labeled amount, place in a $125~\mathrm{mL}$ separatory funnel, then extract 3 times with $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform each time. Combine the chloroform extract and filter with cotton wool to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution and evaporate the chloroform to dryness completely on a steam bath. Add $0.05\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid to the residue and shake to dissolve to make exactly $500~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of etofylline nicotinate RS, previously dried at $105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 2 hours, and dissolve in $0.05~\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $3\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS to make exactly $500~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of the test solution and the standard solution at the wavelength of $268\ \mathrm{nm}$ as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy, using $0.05\;\mathrm{\mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid as a control solution.  

Amount (mg) of etofylline nicotinate $\left({\bf C}_{15}{\bf H}_{15}{\bf N}_{5}{\bf O}_{4}\right)$ $=$ Amount $(\mathrm{mg})$ ) of etofylline nicotinate $\mathrm{RS}\times(A_{\mathrm{T}}\,/\,A_{\mathrm{S}})$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in hermetic containers.

Etoposide $\mathrm{C}_{29}\mathrm{H}_{32}\mathrm{O}_{13}$ : 588.56   
(5 S,5a R,8a R,9 R)-5-[[ $(2R,4{\mathrm{a}}R,6R,7R,8R,8{\mathrm{a}}S)–7,8-$   
Dihydroxy-2-methyl-4,4a,6,7,8,8a-hexahydropyrano[3,2- d][1,3]dioxin-6-yl]oxy]-9-(4-hydroxy-3,5-
