[2]benzofuro[6,5-f][1,3]benzodioxol-8-one [ 33419-42-0 ]Etoposide contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $102.0\%$ of etoposide $(\mathbf{C}_{29}\mathbf{H}_{32}\mathbf{O}_{13})$ , calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Etoposide occurs as white crystals or a crystalline powder.  

It is sparingly soluble in methanol, slightly soluble in ethanol(99.5), and very slightly in water.   
Melting point —About $260\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of Etoposide and etoposide RS in methanol (1 in 10000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Etoposide and etoposide RS as directed in the paste method under Infrared Spectrophotometry: both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ : Between $-100^{\circ}$ and $-105^{\circ}\:(0.1\mathrm{~g~}$ ,calculated on the anhydrous basis, methanol, $20~\mathrm{mL}$ , 100 mm).  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Proceed about $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Etoposide according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 10 ppm).  

(2) Related substances —Dissolve $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of Etoposide in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add the mobile phase to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet 2 mL of this solution, add the mobile phase to it make exactly $200~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Determine each peak area by the automatic integration method: the area of any peak other than etoposide obtained with the test solution is not greater than 1/5 times the peak area of etoposide obtained with the standard solution. The total area of all peaks other than the peak of etoposide obtained with the test solution is not greater than $1/2$ times the peak area of etoposide obtained with the standard solution.  

Operating conditions  

For the detector, column, column temperature, mobile phase and flow rate, proceed as directed in the operating conditions under the Assay.  

System suitability  

System performance: Proceed as directed under the system suitability under the Assay.  

Test for required detectability: Weigh accurately 1 mL of the standard solution and add the mobile phase to make exactly $10\;\mathrm{\mL}$ . Confirm that the peak area of Etoposide obtained from $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution is within the range between $7\%$ and $13\%$ of the peak area of Etoposide in the standard solution.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $50\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area for Etoposide is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Time span of measurement: About 3 times the retention time of etoposide after the solvent peak.  

Water NMT $4.0\%$ $\left[0.5\,\mathrm{~g~}\right]$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\,[\,{\bf\rho}_{1}\,{\bf g})$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Etoposide and etoposide RS (previously determined the water), dissolve separately in and dilute with methanol to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ each. Pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ each of these solutions, add exactly $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution and the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ and use these solutions as the test solution and standard solution, respectively. Perform the test with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and measure the ratio of the peak area of etoposide to that of the internal standard, $Q_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $Q_{S}$ .  

Amount (mg) of Etoposide $(\mathbf{C}_{29}\mathbf{H}_{32}\mathbf{O}_{13})$ $=$ Amount (mg) of etoposide RS, as calculated on the anhydrous basis $\times\,\frac{Q_{\mathrm{T}}}{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}$ Internal standard solution —A solution of 2,6- dichlorophenol in methanol (3 in 2500).  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $290\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $3.9\ \mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $30~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with phenylsilyl silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $10~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $35\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $6.44\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of sodium sulfate decahydrate in diluted acetic acid(100) (1 in 100) to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ , and add $250\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetonitrile.  

Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of etoposide is about 20 minutes.  

# System suitability  

System performance: Dissolve $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of Etoposide in $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, add $8\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the mobile phase, and mix well. Add $0.1~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted acetic acid(100) (1 in 25) and $0.1\;\mathrm{mL}$ of phenolphthalein TS, and add sodium hydroxide TS until the color of the solution changes to faintly red. After allowing to stand for 15 minutes, add $0.1~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted acetic acid(100)(1 in 25). Proceed with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution under the above operating conditions; the resolution between the peak having the relative retention time of about 1.3 with respect to etoposide is NLT 3.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area for Etoposide is NMT $1.0\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Famotidine 파모티딘  

![](images/ddc340a8a649a9a5ef058b7c339158a1d6f0fede5b83de6055d2255bce424ff1.jpg)  

Famotidine $\mathrm{C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3}:337.45}$ 3-[({2-[(Diaminomethylidene)amino]-1,3-thiazol-4- yl}methyl)sulfanyl]- $.N^{\prime}$ -sulfamoylpropanimidamide [76824-35-6 ]Famotidine, when dried, contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ ).  

Description Famotidine occurs as white to yellowish white crystals.  

It is freely soluble in acetic acid(100), slightly soluble in ethanol(95), very slightly soluble in water.   
It dissolves in $0.5\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS.   
It is gradually colored by light.   
Melting point —About $164\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ (with decomposition).  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of solutions of Famotidine and famotidine RS in $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate TS (1 in 50000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Famotidine and famotidine RS, previously dried, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution— Dissolve $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Famotidine in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.5~\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS; the solution is clear and colorless to pale yellow.  

(2) Heavy metals— Proceed with $2.0\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Famotidine according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

(3) Related substances— Dissolve $0.20\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Famotidine in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and add acetic acid(100) to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . Pipet 1 mL, $2~\mathrm{mL}$ and $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and add acetic acid(100) to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ each, and use these solutions as the standard solutions (1), (2) and (3). With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution, the standard solution (1), the standard solution (2), the standard solution (3) on the plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\ \upmu\mathrm{m}\right.\right.}$ to $7~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter, with fluorescent indicator). Then, dry with the aid of a current of nitrogen. Next, develop the plate using a mixture of ethyl acetate, methanol, toluene and ammonia water(28) $(40:25:20:2)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $8~\mathrm{{cm}}$ , and air-dry the plate. Examine the plate under ultraviolet light (main wavelength: $254~\mathrm{nm})$ ); the spots other than the principal spot and the spot of the starting point obtained from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution (3). The total intensity of the spots other than the principal spot and the spot of the starting point obtained from the test solution are NMT $0.5\%$ , as compared to intensities of the spots obtained from the standard solutions (1) and (2).  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ ($1\;\mathrm{g}.$ , in vacuum, phosphorus pentoxide, $80\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 4 hours).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.3~\mathrm{g}$ of Famotidine, previously dried, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of perchloric acid VS $=16.873~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3}}$ Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Famotidine for Injection 주사용파모티딘  

Famotidine for injection is a preparation for injection, which is dissolved before use. Famotidine for injection contains NLT $94.0\%$ and NLT $106.0\%$ of the labeled amount of famotidine $(\mathrm{C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3}:337.45})$ .  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Injections, with Famotidine.  

Description Famotidine for injection occurs as a porous mass or a powder.  

Identification Weigh an amount of Famotidine for injection, equivalent to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of famotidine according to the labeled amount, dissolve in $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate TS, then to $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the resulting solution, add 0.05 mol/L potassium dihydrogen phosphate TS to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Determine the absorption spectra of this solution as directed under Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; it exhibits a maximum absorption between $263~\mathrm{nm}$ and $267\;\mathrm{nm}$ .  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve an amount of Famotidine for injection equivalent to $20~\mathrm{mg}$ (potency) of famotidine, and dissolve in $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 4.9 and 5.5.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution ―Weigh an amount of Famotidine for injection equivalent to about 20 mg of famotidine according to the labeled amount, and dissolved in $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the solution is clear and colorless.  

(2) Related substances― Take a number of Famotidine for injection, equivalent to about $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of famotidine (C8H15N7O2S3), dissolve each content in water, wash the inside of the container with water, combine the solutions of the contents with the washings, add water to the combined solution to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Determine each peak area of these solutions by the automatic integration method: the total area of the peaks other than the major peak from the test solution is not larger than the major peak from the standard solution.  

# Operating conditions  

For the detector, column, column temperature, mobile phase, flow rate and system performance, proceed as directed in the operating conditions under the Assay.  

Detection sensitivity: Adjust the detection sensitivity so that the peak height of famotidine obtained from 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution is between $5\;\mathrm{mm}$ and $10\;\mathrm{mm}$ .System suitability   
System performance: Proceed as directed under the system suitability under the Assay.   
Test for required detectability: Pipet $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution, and add water to make exactly $20~\mathrm{mL}$ .Confirm that the peak area of famotidine obtained from 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution is $8\%$ to $12\%$ of the peak area of famotidine obtained from the standard solution.   
System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above operating conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of famotidine is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Time span of measurement: About 2 times the retention time of famotidine after the solvent peak.  

Water NMT $1.5\%$ $\mathrm{[0.1~g}$ , coulometric titration). Sterility Meets the requirements. Bacterial endotoxins Less than 15 EU per mg of Famotidine for Injection.  

Particulate contamination: Visible particles Meets the requirements.  

Insoluble particulate matter in injections Meets the requirements.  

Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements. Assay Take a number of Famotidine for injection equivalent to about $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of famotidine $\left(\mathrm{C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3}}\right)$ , dissolve the contents in water, wash each container with water, add the washings to the initial fluid, and add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of famotidine RS (previously dried at $80\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 4 hours in a phosphorus pentoxide desiccator) and dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $50\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . Pipet $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and calculate the peak area ratios, $\mathrm{Q_{T}}$ and $\mathrm{Q}_{\mathrm{S}}$ , of famotidine to the internal standard, respectively.  

Amount (mg) of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ )$=$ Amount (mg) of famotidine $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{Q_{\mathrm{T}}}{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}\times2$ Internal standard solution —To $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution of methyl $p$ -hydroxybenzoate in methanol (1 in 500), add water to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $25\ ^{\circ}\mathbf{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $2\,\mathrm{~\textit~{~g~}~}$ of sodium 1- heptanesulfonate in $900~\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, add acetic acid(100) to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 3.0, and add water to make $1000\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . To this solution, add $240\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of acetonitrile and $40\,\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol.  

Flow rate: Adjust the flow rate so that the retention time of famotidine is about 6 minutes.   
System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $5\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; famotidine and the internal standard are eluted in this order with the resolution being NLT 11.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of ratios of the peak area of famotidine to that of the internal standard is NMT $1.0\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in hermetic containers.  

# Famotidine Tablets 파모티딘정  

Famotidine Tablets contain NLT $94.0\%$ and NMT $106.0\%$ of the labeled amount of famotidine $(\mathrm{C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3}:337.45})$ ).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Famotidine.  

Identification Weigh an amount of Famotidine Tablets, previously powdered, equivalent to $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of famotidine according to the labeled amount, add $50\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of 0.05 $\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate TS, shake well to mix, and then centrifuge. To $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the clear supernatant, add $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate TS to make $50\,\mathrm{mL}$ , and determine the absorption spectrum of the solution as directed under Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; it exhibits a maximum absorption between 263 nm and $267\;\mathrm{nm}$ .  

Purity Related substances —Take NLT 10 Famotidine Tablets, add $200~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluent, and disintegrate by shaking well to mix. To this solution, add $200~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, mix at 300 revolutions per minute for 1 hour, add diluent to make exactly $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and then filter. Pipet an amount of this solution equivalent to $10~\mathrm{~mg}$ of famotidine, add diluent to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately 10 mg of famotidine RS, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, sonicate for 5 minutes, and then add diluent to make exactly 100 mL. Use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $50\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Determine the peak area of each solution by the automatic integration method, and calculate the amount of each related substance in the test solution; the famotidine related substance I {3-[2-(diaminomethyleneamino)-1,3-thiazol4-yl methylsulfonyl]phenyl}- $\cdot N\cdot$ -sulfamoyl-propanamide} is NMT $1.0\%$ , and famotidine related substance II {3-[2- (diaminomethyleneamino)-1,3-thiazol-4-yl methylthio]propanoic acid}, famotidine related substance III {3- [2-(diaminomethyleneamino)-1,3-thiazol-4-yl methylthio]- ${\mathcal{N}}.$ -sulfamoyl-propanamide}, and famotidine related substances IV {3-[2-(diaminomethyleneamino)-1,3- thiazol-4-yl methylthio]-propanamide} are NMT $0.5\%$ and the total amount of related substances is NMT $1.5\%$ However, the peak area of famotidine related substance IV is obtained by dividing the area determined with the automatic integration method by the correction factor 1.3. stance III and famotidine, and between famotidine and famotidine related substance IV, are NLT 1.3, respectively, and the mass distribution ratio of the famotidine peak is NLT 2.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $50\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

$$
=\mathrm{\nabla{100}}\times{\frac{C_{S}}{C\times N}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{i}}}{A_{S}}}
$$  

$C_{\mathrm{{S}}}$ : Concentration $(\mathrm{mg/mL})$ of famotidine in the standard solution  

$C:$ : Labeled amount (g) of famotidine in 1 tablet $N!$ : Number of tablets used in the preparation of the test solution  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of each related substance in the test solution  

$A_{S}$ : Peak area of famotidine in the standard solution Diluent —Dissolve $6.8\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of potassium dihydrogen phosphate in $750\;\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, adjust $\mathrm{pH}$ with 1 mol/L potassium hydroxide to 6.0, and add water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $275\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of buffer solution and acetonitrile $(93:7)$ .  

Flow rate: About 1.4 mL/min System suitability  

Test for required detectability: To $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of famotidine, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid, heat at $80~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 30 minutes, and then cool to room temperature. Then, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide TS, heat at $80\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 30 minutes, then cool to room temperature, and then neutralize with $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid. Add diluent to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, transfer into a solution of $5~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of famotidine dissolved in $8\;\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, then add diluent to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add diluent to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the system suitability stock solution. Take 1 to $1.5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add 1 drop of hydrogen peroxide TS, and use this solution as the system suitability solution. Proceed with 50 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; the relative retention time of famotidine related substances I, II, III, and IV to the retention time of the famotidine peak are 0.4, 0.7, 0.8, and 1.2, respectively.  

System performance: Proceed with $50~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the system suitability solution according to the above conditions; the resolutions between famotidine related subBuffer solution —Dissolve 13.6 gof sodium acetate trihydrate in $750~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of triethylamine, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 6.0 with acetic acid(100), and then add water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Famotidine Tablets at 50 revolutions per minute according to Method 2, using $900\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of $\mathrm{pH}\ 4.5\ 0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphate buffer solution as the dissolution medium. Take $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of the dissolved solution 30 minutes after starting the test, and filter through a membrane filter with a pore size of NMT $0.8~{\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ . Discard the first $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate and use the subsequent filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of Famotidine RS, add buffer solution to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add the buffer solution to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances, AT and AS, of the test solution and the standard solution at the absorbance maximum wavelength near $265~\mathrm{nm}$ as directed under Ultraviolet-visible Spectrophotometry.  

It meets the requirements if the dissolution rate of Famotidine Tablets in 30 minutes is NLT $75\%$ .  

Dissolution rate $(\%)$ of the labeled amount of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$  

$C$ :Labeled amount (mg) of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ in 1 tablet  

Uniformity of dosage units It meets the requirements when the procedure for content uniformity is performed according to the following method.  

Take 1 tablet of Famotidine Tablets, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, shake to disintegrate. Add methanol, shake well to mix, then add methanol to make exactly $V\;\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution containing about $0.2~\mathrm{mg}$ of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ per mL, and centrifuge. Pipet $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the clear supernatant, add $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $20~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of famotidine RS, previously dried in a phosphorus pentoxide desiccator in vacuum at $50~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 4 hours, and dissolve in methanol to make exactly $100~\mathrm{{mL}}$ . Pipet 10 mL of this solution, add $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $20~\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the standard solution. Internal standard solution —To $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution of methyl $p$ -hydroxybenzoate in methanol (1 in 500), add water to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Assay Take a certain number of Famotidine Tablets equivalent to $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ , add 50 mL of water, and disintegrate by shaking well to mix. Next, add $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, shake well to mix, then add methanol to make exactly $200~\mathrm{mL}$ , and centrifuge. Pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the clear supernatant, add exactly $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the internal standard solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of famotidine RS, previously dried in a phosphorus pentoxide desiccator in vacuum at $80\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 4 hours, and dissolve in methanol to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . # Amount (mg) of famotidine $\mathrm{(C_{8}H_{15}N_{7}O_{2}S_{3})}$ )$=$ Amount (mg) of famotidine $\mathrm{RS}\!\times\!\frac{Q_{\mathrm{T}}}{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}\times2$

# Operating conditions

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $25\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: Dissolve $2\,\mathrm{~\textit~{~g~}~}$ of sodium 1- heptanesulfonate in $900~\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, add acetic acid(100) to adjust the pH to 3.0, and add water to make $1000\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . To this solution, add $240\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of acetonitrile and $40\,\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol.

![](images/83870b79175041fd544151aebee223ff3c864296f6722a70e7ef4adf29981d37.jpg)  

Felodipine contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of felodipine ( $\mathrm{\bf\{C}_{18}H_{19}C l_{2}N O_{4})}$ , calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Felodipine occurs as a pale yellow to yellow crystalline powder. It is freely soluble in acetone or ethanol(95), slightly soluble in heptane, and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Determine the infrared spectra of Felodipine and felodipine RS, previously dried, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Midinfrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(2) The retention time of the major peak of the test solution corresponds to that of the standard solution, as obtained in the Assay.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution —Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Felodipine in methanol to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , perform the test with this solution as directed under the Ultravioletvisible Spectroscopy using methanol as a control solution, and determine the absorbance at the wavelength of $440\;\mathrm{nm}$ with a layer length of $5\;\mathrm{{cm}}$ ; it is NMT 0.2.  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Felodipine according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT 20 ppm).  

(3) Related substances —With $40\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ of the test solution prepared according to the Assay, perform the test as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak area from the test solution; each peak area other than the major peak from the test solution is NMT $1.0\%$ , and the sum of peak areas of these peaks is NMT $1.5\%$ relative to the major peak area.  

$$
=\,100\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{i}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}
$$  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Each peak area other than the major peak $A_{S}$ : Total area of all peaks  

Operating conditions  

Proceed as directed under the operating conditions under the Assay.  

Time span of measurement: NLT 2 times the retention time of felodipine.

Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$ Assay Weigh accurately about $30~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Felodipine and felodipine RS, dissolve each in the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. Perform the test with $40~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of felodipine in each solution.  

Amount (mg) of felodipine $\mathrm{(C_{18}H_{19}C l N O_{4})}$ )$=$ Amount (mg) of felodipine $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}$ Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $254\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $15~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).

Flow rate: 1 mL/min System suitability  

System performance: Dissolve $0.15\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of felodipine in a mixture of $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of t-butyl alcohol and $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of $1~\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium ferric sulfate TS, allow to stand for 15 minutes, and add $3.5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $10\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide TS. Neutralize with $2\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide TS. Transfer this mixture into a separatory funnel, add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of dichloromethane, shake, and take the lower layer. Evaporate the lower layer to dryness on a steam bath with the aid of a current of nitrogen. Dissolve $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of the residue (felodipine oxide) and $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of felodipine RS in the mobile phase to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and add the mobile phase to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; felodipine oxide and felodipine are eluted in this order with the resolution not being less than 2.5. Proceed with $40~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the symmetry factor of the felodipine peak is NMT 1.5. Detection sensitivity: Adjust the detection sensitivity so that the height of the two peaks obtained from the solution in the system performance is NLT $20\%$ of the full scale.  

Phosphate buffer solution —Dissolve $6.9~\mathrm{g}$ of sodium dihydrogen phosphate dihydrate in $400~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $8~\mathrm{mL}$ of $1~\mathrm{mol/L}$ phosphoric acid, and add water to make $1000\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

![](images/90f1d684f380e02a384d63abcf98906e42b89334800d2a42b2934b64964e3222.jpg)  

Fenofibrate $\mathrm{C}_{20}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{ClO}_{4}:360.83$ Propan-2-yl 2-{4-[(4-chlorophenyl)carbonyl] phenoxy}- 2-methylpropanoate [ 49562-28-9 ]  

Fenofibrate contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of fenofibrate $\left({\bf C}_{20}{\bf H}_{21}{\bf C}{\bf l O}_{4}\right)$ , calculated on the dried basis. Description Fenofibrate occurs as a white crystalline powder. It is very soluble in dichloromethane, slightly soluble in ethanol(95), and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification Determine the infrared spectra of Fenofibrate and fenofibrate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

Melting point Between 79 and $82\,^{\circ}\!C$ Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution— Dissolve 0.50 g of Fenofibrate in acetone to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ ; the resulting solution is clear.  

(2) Acid— Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenofibrate in $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ethanol previously neutralized with $0.2\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of phenolphthalein TS. To this solution, add dropwise $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide solution until the resulting solution exhibits a pink color; the consumed amount is NMT 0.2 mL.  

(3) Chloride— To $5.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenofibrate, add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, heat at $50\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes, cool, and filter. To $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add $6~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute nitric acid and water to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and perform the test. Prepare the control solution by adding $6\;\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute nitric acid, 0.30 mL of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid, and water to make $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ (NMT $0.01\%$ ).  

(4) Sulfate— To $5.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenofibrate, add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, heat at $50\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes, cool, and filter. To 10 mL of the filtrate, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid and water to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Prepare the control solution by adding $1\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid, $0.42\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of $0.005\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sulfuric acid, and water to make $50\;\mathrm{\mL}$ (NMT $0.01\%$ ).  

(5) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Fenofibrate and perform the test as directed under Method 2. Prepare the control solution with $2.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of the lead standard solution (NMT 20 ppm).  

(6) Related substances— Dissolve about $100~\mathrm{mg}$ of Fenofibrate in the mobile phase to make exactly $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ ,and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, and add the mobile phase to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . Pipet $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of this solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20\;\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Determine each peak area of each solution according to the automatic integration method and determine the amount of each related substance; fenofibrate related substance I with the relative retention time of 0.3 for fenofibrate obtained from the test solution and fenofibrate related substance II with the relative retention time of 0.4 are NMT $0.1\%$ , and fenofibrate related substance III with the relative retention time of 1.3 is NMT $0.1\%$ .Any other individual unidentified related substances are NMT $0.1\%$ , and the total related substances are NMT $0.5\%$ . However, exclude any peaks smaller than $0.05\%$ .  

$$
{}=\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times{}r f\times{\frac{1}{10}}
$$  

$A_{\mathrm{T}}$ : Peak area of each related substance obtained from the test solution   
A S: Peak area of fenofibrate obtained from the standard solution   
$r f\!\!\!/$ : The correction factor for each related substance for fenofibrate peak  

Fenofibrate related substance I: 0.78   
Fenofibrate related substance II: 1.02   
Fenofibrate related substance III: 1.27   
Other related substances: 1.00  

# Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer  

(wavelength: $286\;\mathrm{nm}^{\phantom{\dagger}}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.0\ \mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of acetonitrile and water $(7:3)$ (adjust the pH with phosphoric acid).  

Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability  

Test for required detectability: Pipet $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution, and add the mobile phase to make exactly $10~\mathrm{mL}$ . Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; confirm that the signal-tonoise ratio of the torsemide peak is NLT 10.  

System performance: Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the symmetry factor of the fenofibrate peak is between 0.8 and 2.0.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $20\,\textrm{\textmu L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of fenofibrate is NMT $10.0\%$ .  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ $(0.5\mathrm{~g},\,60\,\,^{\circ}\!C$ , in vacuum, constant mass).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ $\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~}~}\mathrm{g})$  

Assay Weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{{mg}}$ each of Fenofibrate and fenofibrate RS, dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution (1), respectively. Also, weigh $10.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenofibrate RS, $10.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenofibrate related substance I RS, $10.0\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of fenofibrate related substance II RS, and $20.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenofibrate related substance III RS, and dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (2). Perform the test with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution (1) as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the operating conditions for testing related substances, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of fenofibrate in each solution.  

# Amount (mg) of fenofibrate $(\mathbf{C}_{20}\mathbf{H}_{21}\mathbf{C}\mathrm{lO}_{4})$ )$=$ Amount (mg) of fenofibrate $\begin{array}{r}{\mathrm{RS}\!\times\!\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\end{array}$  

# System suitability  

Detection sensitivity: Adjust the sensitivity so that the peak heights obtained by performing the test with 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of standard solution (2) according to the above conditions are NLT $50\%$ of the full scale of the data collection device.  

System repeatability: Repeat the test 6 times with $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution (1) according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area of fenofibrate is NMT $1.0\%$ .  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, wellclosed containers.  

# Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate 페노프로펜칼슘수화물

Fenoprofen Calcium $\mathrm{C_{30}H_{26}C a O_{6}\mathrm{\cdot2H_{2}O_{3}}}$ 558.63 Calcium 2-(3-phenoxyphenyl)propanoate dihydrate [152864-45-4 ]  

Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate contains NLT $97.0\%$ and NMT $103.0\%$ of fenoprofen calcium $\mathrm{(C_{30}H_{26}C a O_{6}\colon522.60)}$ , calculated on the anhydrous basis. Description Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate occurs as a white crystalline powder.  

It is slightly soluble in n-hexanol, methanol, or water, and practically insoluble in chloroform.  

Identification (1) Mix $1{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate with $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(31), heat, filter, and add $2\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonium oxalate TS to the filtrate; a white precipitate develops, and dissolve the precipitate in 3 mol/L hydrochloric acid TS.  

(2) Heavy metals —Proceed with $2.0\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with 2.0 mL of lead standard solution (NMT 10 ppm).  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate and fenoprofen calcium dihydrate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) Related substances —Weigh accurately about $0.2\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate, dissolve in a mixture of water and acetonitrile $(1:1)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenoprofen calcium dihydrate RS and dissolve in a mixture of water and acetonitrile $(1:1)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add a mixture of water and acetonitrile $(1:$ 1) to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, determine each peak area from each solution by the automatic integration method, and calculate the amount of each related substance; the amount of each related substance is NMT amount $0.5\%$ , and the total amount of related substances is NMT $2.0\%$ .  

Purity (1) Calcium —Weigh accurately about $0.75\mathrm{~g~}$ of Fenoprofen Calcium Dihydrate, add ethanol(95), and dissolve by heating if necessary. Add ethanol(95) to make exactly $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Put $70~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium hydroxide solution (1 in 10) and $0.3~\mathrm{g}$ of hydroxynaphthol in a 150- mL beaker to mix, add about $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, and titrate with $0.05\;\mathrm{\mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS until the resulting solution exhibits a blue color. To this solution, add $10.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, and titrate with $0.05~\mathrm{mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS until the resulting solution exhibits a blue color (between $7.3\%$ and $8.0\%$ , calculated on the anhydrous basis).  

Each mL of $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS $=2.004~\mathrm{mg}$ of Ca

# Fenoterol Hydrobromide 페노테롤브롬화수소산염

C17 H21 NO 4 ·HBr : 384.27  

5-[1-Hydroxy-2-[1-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propan-2- ylamino]ethyl]benzene-1,3-diolhydrobromide [ 1944-12- 3 ]  

Fenoterol Hydrobromide contains NLT $99.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of fenoterol hydrobromide $\mathrm{(C_{17}H_{21}N O_{4}{\cdot}H B r)}$ ), calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Fenoterol Hydrobromide occurs as a white crystalline powder.  

It is soluble in water or ethanol(95). Identification (1) Determine the infrared spectra of Fenoterol Hydrobromide and fenoterol hydrobromide RS, previously dried, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(2) An aqueous solution of Fenoterol Hydrobromide (1 in 100) responds to the Qualitative Analysis (1) for bromide.  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenoterol Hydrobromide in water to make exactly $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ ; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 4.2 and 5.2.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution —Dissolve $2.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenoterol Hydrobromide in water to make exactly 50 mL; the resulting solution is clear and colorless.  

(2) Iron —Proceed with $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Fenoterol Hydrobromide according to Method 3 and perform the test as directed under Method A. Prepare the control solution with $0.5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of iron standard solution $(\mathrm{NMT}\,5\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ). (3) Phenone —Dissolve $2.0{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Fenoterol Hydrobromide in water to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ . Determine the absorbance of this solution at the wavelength of $330\ \mathrm{nm}$ as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; it is NMT 0.42 (NMT $0.2\%$ ).  

(4) Isomer —Dissolve $25.0\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ each of Fenoterol Hydrobromide and fenoterol hydrobromide RS in water to make exactly $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. Prepare the test solution and the standard solution before use. Perform the test with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions. Calculate the amount of isomer by determining the heights, $(H_{\mathrm{T}})$ and $(H_{\mathrm{S}})$ , of the peak eluting immediately after the major peak obtained from the test solution; it is NMT $4.0\%$ .  

Content $(\%)$ of isomer $=$ Content $(\%)$ of isomer indicated on the reference standards ×$\frac{H_{\mathrm{T}}}{H_{\mathrm{S}}}$ Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $280\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ to $10\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: To $10~\mathrm{\mL}$ of $0.9~\mathrm{\,w/v\%}$ potassium dihydrogen phosphate, add $690~\mathrm{mL}$ of $2.4~\mathrm{w}/\mathrm{v}\%$ dibasic sodium phosphate 12-hydrate solution, mix, and add phosphoric acid to adjust the pH to 8.5. Add $300~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and mix.  

Flow rate: 1.0 mL/minute. Adjust the retention time of the major peak to be NMT 20 minutes.  

# System suitability  

System performance: Proceed with $20~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution under the above conditions; adjust the sensitivity so that the peak height of the isomer eluting immediately after the major peak is NLT $10\%$ of the full scale. The height of the valley between the major peak and the isomer peak obtained from the standard solution is NMT $4\%$ of the full scale.  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ $\mathrm{~\,~1~g,~}105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , constant mass). Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ ($\mathrm{~\textit~{~1~g~}~}$ ). Assay Weigh accurately about $0.6~\mathrm{g}$ of Fenoterol Hydrobromide, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of dilute nitric acid and $25.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ silver nitrate solution, and titrate with $0.1\mod/\mathrm{L}$ ammonium thiocyanate VS while shaking to mix until the resulting solution exhibits an orange color (indicator: $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonium iron(III) sulfate TS). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, wellclosed containers.  

# Fenoterol Hydrobromide Tablets 페노테롤브롬화수소산염정  

Fenoterol Hydrobromide Tablets contain NLT $95.0\%$ and NMT $105.0\%$ of the labeled amount of fenoterol hydrobromide $(\mathrm{C_{17}H_{21}N O_{4}}{\cdot}\mathrm{HBr}{\cdot}\,384.27)$ ).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Fenoterol Hydrobromide.  

Identification Weigh an amount of Fenoterol Hydrobromide Tablets, equivalent to about $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide according to the labeled amount, extract with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, then filter, and use this solution as the test solution. Weigh $50~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide RS, add water to make $5~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of 2-butanol, formic acid and water $(75~:~15~:~10)$ , and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly a diazobenzenesulfonic acid TS on the plate, and heat at $105\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes; the $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values and colors of the spots from the test solution and the standard solution are the same.  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Fenoterol Hydrobromide Tablets at 50 revolutions per minute according to Method 2, using $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of water as the dissolution medium. Take the medium 15 minutes after starting the test, and filter. Discard the first $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, pipet $V\,\mathrm{mL}$ of the subsequent filtrate, add water to make $V^{\prime}\,\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution containing about $2~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide $\mathrm{(C_{17}H_{21}N O_{4}{\cdot}H B r)}$ per mL according to the labeled amount, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $20\,\mathrm{~mg~}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide RS, and dissolve in water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $100~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of fenoterol hydrobromide in each solution. The dissolution rate in 15 minutes is NLT $80\%$ .  

Dissolution rate $(\%)$ of the labeled amount of fenoterol hydrobromide $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{4}\right)$ )  

$$
=W_{S}\times{\frac{V^{\prime}}{V}}\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}\times{\frac{1}{\mathrm{C}}}\times9
$$  

$W_{S}$ : Amount (mg) of fenoterol hydrobromide RS  

$C$ : Labeled amount (mg) of fenoterol hydrobromide $\left({\bf C}_{17}\mathrm{H}_{21}\mathrm{NO}_{4}\right)$ in 1 tablet  

# Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $276\,\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( $\ensuremath{\left\langle5\;\ensuremath{\upmu\mathrm{m}}\right.\right.}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Mobile phase: A mixture of $\mathrm{pH}\,3.2$ buffer solution and acetonitrile $(100:27)$ .  

Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

# Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements.  

Assay Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 Fenoterol Hydrobromide Tablets, and powder. Weigh accurately an amount equivalent to about $2.5~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide $\mathrm{(C_{17}H_{21}N O_{4}{\cdot}H B r)}$ ), add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , then filter, and use the filtrate as the test solution. Separately, weigh accurately about $25~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of fenoterol hydrobromide RS, and add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography, and determine the peak areas, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , of fenoterol hydrobromide in each solution.  

Amount (mg) of fenoterol hydrobromide $\mathrm{(C_{17}H_{21}N O_{4}{\cdot}H B r)}$ $=$ Amount (mg) of fenoterol hydrobromide $\mathrm{RS}\times\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}\times\frac{1}{10}$  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $276\,\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\upmu\mathrm{m}$ in particle diameter).  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $40\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .
