Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

# Fentanyl Citrate 펜타닐시트르산염  

![](images/2d77274a0036e1278b446b0197c40afb01ba4f0211413b6bb1cc951e5b3b4efe.jpg)  
$\mathrm{C_{22}H_{28}N_{2}O{\cdot}C_{6}H_{8}O_{7}}$ : 528.59  

2-Hydroxypropane-1,2,3-tricarboxylic acid ; $N$ -phenyl$.N.$ -[1-(2-phenylethyl)piperidin-4-yl]propanamide [ 990-73-8 ]Fentanyl Citrate contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of fentanyl citrate $\left({\bf C}_{22}\mathrm{H}_{28}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathrm{O}\cdot{\bf C}_{6}\mathrm{H}_{8}\mathrm{O}_{7}\right)$ , calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Fentanyl Citrate occurs as white crystals or a crystalline powder.  

It is freely soluble in methanol or acetic acid(100), sparingly soluble in water or ethanol(95), and very slightly soluble in ether.  

Identification (1) Dissolve $50~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Fentanyl Citrate and fentanyl citrate RS in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid TS and ethanol(95) to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Determine the absorption spectra of these solutions as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths.  

(2) Determine the infrared spectra of Fentanyl Citrate and fentanyl citrate RS, previously dried, as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Midinfrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) An aqueous solution of Fentanyl Citrate (1 in 100) responds to the Qualitative Analysis (1) for citrate.  

# Melting point Between 150 and $154\,^{\circ}\!C$  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Dissolve $0.10~\mathrm{g}$ of Fentanyl Citrate in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of this solution is between 3.0 and 5.0.  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Proceed with $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Fentanyl Citrate according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $20\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ).  

(2) Related substances —Dissolve $0.10\mathrm{~g~}$ of Fentanyl Citrate in $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of methanol, and use this solution as the test solution. Pipet $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add methanol to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot 5 $\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on the thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of 1-butanol, water and acetic acid(31) $(3:$ $1:1\rangle$ ) as the developing solvent to a distance of about 10 cm, and air-dry the plate. Spray evenly Dragendorff's TS for spraying on the plate; the spots other than the principal spot obtained from the test solution are not more intense than the spots from the standard solution.  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ ($\mathbf{0.2\thetag}$ , in vacuum, silica gel, $60\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 2 hours).  

Residue on ignition NMT $0.2\%$ (0.5 g). Assay Weigh accurately about $75~\mathrm{mg}$ of Fentanyl Citrate, dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and titrate with $0.02\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.02\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS $=10.572\;\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C_{22}H_{28}N_{2}O{\cdot}C_{6}H_{8}O_{7}}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, tight containers.  

# Fenticonazole Nitrate 펜티코나졸질산염  

![](images/a0c8f59ae5de7fb324978cba379bb91f4bd6ce364d087d8651c97e5fc73f9258.jpg)  
and enantiomer  

$\mathrm{C_{24}H_{20}C l_{2}N_{2}O S{\cdot}H N O_{3}:518.41}$ 1-{2-(2,4-Dichlorophenyl)-2-[4-(phenylthio) benzyloxy]ethyl}- $1H$ -imidazole nitrate [ 73151-29-8 ]  

Fenticonazole Nitrate contains NLT $99.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of fenticonazole nitrate $(\mathrm{C_{24}H_{20}C l_{2}N_{2}O S{\cdot}H N O_{3})}$ ), calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Fenticonazole Nitrate occurs as a white crystalline powder.  

It is freely soluble in methanol or N,N -dimethylformamide, sparingly soluble in ethanol(95), and practically insoluble in water.  

Identification (1) Determine the absorption spectra of solutions of Fenticonazole Nitrate and fenticonazole nitrate RS in ethanol(95) (1 in 50000) as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavelengths. (2) Determine the infrared spectra of Fenticonazole Nitrate and fenticonazole nitrate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(3) Weigh an amount of Fenticonazole Nitrate, equivalent to $1~\mathrm{mg}$ of nitrate ions, add a mixture of 0.1 mL of nitrobenzene and $0.2~\mathrm{mL}$ of sulfuric acid, allow to stand for 5 minutes, and cool with iced water. Add gently $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water while stirring, add $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of $10\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium hydroxide TS and $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetone, shake to mix, and allow to stand; the upper layer exhibits an intense purple color.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{\mathrm{D}}^{20}$ : Between $-0.10^{\circ}$ and $+\:0.10^{\circ}$ (0.1 g, methanol, $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ ,$100\;\mathrm{mm}$ ).  

Melting point Between 134 and $137\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Purity (1) Toluene —Weigh exactly $0.2{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Fenticonazole Nitrate, transfer into a $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ vial, disperse with exactly $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, mix $4.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of toluene with water to make $1000~\mathrm{{mL}}$ . Transfer $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution into a 10 mL vial, and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Gas Chromatography according to the following conditions. Use a headspace sample injection apparatus. Determine the amount of toluene according to the standard addition method; it is NMT $100\,\mathrm{{ppm}}$ .  

Operating conditions Detector: A flame ionization detector Column: A tube about $0.32\;\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and about 25 min length, coated with poly(cyanopropyl)(7)phenyl(7)methyl(86)siloxane for ga s chromatography with a thickness of $1.2\;\upmu\mathrm{m}$ .  

Headspace conditions: Equilibrium temperature of $90\;^{\circ}\!C$ , equilibrium time of 1 hour.  

Column temperature: $80\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Injection port temperature: $180\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Detector temperature: $220\,^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Carrier gas: Helium Split ratio: About $1:25$ .Column head pressure: $40\,\mathrm{kPa}$  

Injection volume: Maintain each liquid at $90~^{\circ}\!C$ for 1 hour, and inject $1~\mathrm{mL}$ in the form of vapor into the column.  

(2) Related substances —Weigh accurately $25.0~\mathrm{mg}$ of Fenticonazole Nitrate, add the mobile phase to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. To $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, add the mobile phase to make exactly $200~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (1). To $10.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution (1), add the mobile phase to make exactly $25~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (2). Pipet $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution (1), add the mobile phase to make exactly $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (3). To $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution, add $5~\mathrm{mg}$ of fenticonazolerelatedsubstanceIRS{(RS)-1-[2-(2,4-dichlorophenyl)-2-hydroxyethyl]-3-[4-  

(phenylsulfanyl)benzyl]imidazolium nitrate}, and dissolve in the mobile phase to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of the mobile phase to make exactly $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution (4). Perform the test with $10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution (1) as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following operating conditions, and determine the areas of each peak according to the automatic integration method; the peak area other than the major peak and nitric acid ion peak (corresponding to the void volume of column) obtained from test solution is NMT the major peak area obtained from the standard solution (2) $(0.2\%)$ , and the total area of these peaks is NMT the major peak area obtained from standard solution (1) $(0.5\%)$ . However, exclude any peak having an area smaller than the major peak area obtained from the standard solution (3).  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $229\;\mathrm{nm}$ ).  

Column: A stainless steel column, about $4\textrm{m m}$ in internal diameter and about $25~\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography (5 $\cdot\ensuremath{\mathrm{\;10\;\mum}}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of acetonitrile and phosphate buffer solution $(70:30)$ .  

Flow rate: $1.0\,\mathrm{mL/min}$  

# System suitability  

Inject $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the standard solution (2), and adjust the sensitivity so that the peak height of fenticonazole is at least $10\%$ of the full scale of the data collection device. Inject $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution (3) and the standard solution (4) separately. In the chromatogram obtained from the standard solution (4), the resolution between fenticonazole related substance I and fenticonazole is NLT 2, and in the chromatogram obtained from the standard solution (3), a signal-to-noise ratio is NLT 5. Phosphate buffer solution —Dissolve $3.4~\mathrm{g}$ of potassium dihydrogen phosphate in $900\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, adjust $\mathrm{pH}$ with phosphoric acid to 3.0, and add water to make $1000\,\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Loss on drying NMT $0.5\%$ ($1\;\mathrm{g}_{}$ , in vacuum, $60\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , constant mass).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.45\mathrm{~g~}$ of Fenticonazole Nitrate, dissolve with $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of a mixture of 2-butanone and acetic acid(100) $(1:1)$ , and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ perchloric acid VS (potentiometric titration under the Titrimetry). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction. Packaging and storage Preserve in light-resistant, wellclosed containers.  

# Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex 폴리말토오스수산화제이철착염  

Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex contains NLT $24.0\%$ and NMT $32.0\%$ of iron (Fe: 55.85).  

Description Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex occurs as a brown amorphous powder and is odorless. It is soluble in water and insoluble in organic solvents.  

Identification (1) Ionized iron —Weigh an amount of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex, equivalent to $5\;\mathrm{g}$ of iron according to the labeled amount, add $80~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, dissolve at $70\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour while shaking, add water to make $100~\mathrm{{mL}}$ , and filter the solution. Use the filtrate as the test solution. To the solution of $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution in $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of $2~\mathrm{mol/L}$ ammonia TS, and mix; a brown precipitate does not form. (2) Iron —Mix with $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution of (1), $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, and heat on a steam bath for 5 minutes. After cooling, neutralize with excess $25\%$ ammonia water, and filter. Wash the produced ferric hydroxide precipitate with water, dissolve the precipitate in a small amount of $2\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid, and add water to make $20~\mathrm{mL}$ . To this solution, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride TS, allow to stand for 30 minutes, and add $o$ -phenanthroline ethanol solution (1 in 50); the resulting solution exhibits an dark red color. (3) Polymaltose —To $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of the test solution of (1), add $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $0.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, heat on a steam bath for 5 minutes, cool rapidly, add 2 mL of $25\%$ ammonia water and $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of freshly prepared hydrogen sulfide TS, and mix. Remove excess hydrogen sulfide by boiling, cool, and filter. To $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, heat on a steam bath for 15 minutes, and cool immediately. Add $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of $20\%$ sodium hydroxide solution and $5\,\textrm{m L}$ of Fehling's TS, mix, boil for 1 minute, and cool immediately; a red $\mathrm{Cu2O}$ precipitate forms.  

$\mathbf{pH}$ Weigh an amount of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex, equivalent to $5\textrm{g}$ of iron according to the labeled amount, add $80~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, dissolve at $70~^{\circ}\!C$ for 1 hour while shaking, and add water to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ ; the $\mathrm{pH}$ of the filtrate is between 5.5 and 7.5.  

Purity (1) Polymaltose —Between $25.0\%$ and $50.0\%$ Weigh an amount of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex, equivalent to $5\textrm{g}$ of iron, add $80~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, dissolve at $70~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 1 hour while shaking, add water at $20~^{\circ}\!C$ to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ , and filter. To $2.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, transfer $0.10~\mathrm{g}$ of the anhydrous glucose into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, and add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Take $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use it as the standard solution. Prepare 6 stoppered test tubes, separately add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of water for 2 test tubes, $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of the test solution for 2 test tubes, and $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of the standard solution for 2 test tubes. Add $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of anthrone solution to each tube, mix well, and close the stopper. After warming on a steam bath for exactly 10 minutes, take it out, and cool. Next, shake for 5 minutes to mix, perform the test as directed under the Ultraviolet-visible Spectroscopy using water as the control solution, and determine the absorbances, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{\mathrm{{S}}}$ , at the absorbance maximum wavelength of between $600~\mathrm{nm}$ and $605~\mathrm{nm}$ from the test solution and the standard solution.  

# Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex Solution  

# 폴리말토오스수산화제이철착염액  

Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex Solution contains NLT $95.0\%$ and NMT $105.0\%$ of the labeled amount of iron (Fe: 55.85) in the ferric hydroxide polymaltose complex.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Liquids, with Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex.  

Identification Take $0.25~\mathrm{mL}$ of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex Solution, add $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of $4~\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid, and heat until it becomes transparent yellow. Add $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium ferrocyanide TS; the resulting solution exhibits a blue color.  

pH Between 5.0 and 7.0.  

$$
=\frac{A_{\mathrm{T}}\times1\bar{0}0\,(m\dot{g})\stackrel{.}{\times}162}{A_{\mathrm{S}}\times180}
$$  

(2) Sodium chloride —NMT $6.0\%$ . Transfer 10.0 mL of the test solution of (1) into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ beaker, add $60\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $0.2\;\mathrm{mL}$ of nitric acid, shake well, and titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ silver nitrate VS using the potentiometric titration. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ silver nitrate VS $=5.850\;\mathrm{mg}$ of NaC1  

Loss on drying NMT $5.0\%$ ($^{\mathrm{~1~g~}}$ , in vacuum, $20\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ phosphorus pentoxide, 2 hours).  

Assay After mixing $10~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex well, weigh accurately $0.3\mathrm{~g~}$ of the mixed drug, transfer into a $200{\-}{\mathrm{mL}}$ beaker, add $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, and heat on a steam bath for 1 to 2 minutes while shaking to mix. After the solution is completely dissolved, take it out, and allow to stand for 5 minutes. Add $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to between 2.2 and 2.5 with $30\%$ sodium hydroxide solution. Add $2.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of $2\%$ pyrocatechol sodium salt solution as the indicator, titrate with freshly prepared $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS at between 40 and $50~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ until the green color of the solution turns yellow. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS $=5.585~\mathrm{mg}$ of Fe  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers. Purity To $0.25\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex Solution, add $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $1\,\textrm{m L}$ of 2 mol/L ammonia TS, and shake to mix; a brown precipitate $\left(\mathrm{Fe}(\mathrm{OH})_{3}\right)$ ) does not form.  

Assay Take $5.0\,\textrm{m L}$ of Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex Solution, add $10~\mathrm{\mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, shake well to mix, and heat until the solution becomes yellow. Add $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of acetic acid(100), and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to between 2.2 and 2.5 with $30\%$ sodium hydroxide solution. Add $0.2\ \mathrm{mL}$ of hydrogen peroxide, immediately add $2.5~\mathrm{mL}$ of $2\%$ pyrocatechol sodium salt solution, and titrate with $0.05\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS while maintaining the temperature at 40 to $50~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . The endpoint of the titration is when the color of this solution changes from green to yellow. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.05\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt VS $=2.7925\ \mathrm{mg}$ of Fe  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets 폴리말토오스수산화제이철착염·폴산정  

Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets contain NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount of iron (Fe: 55.85) and NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $150.0\%$ of folic acid $\mathrm{(C_{19}H_{19}N_{7}O_{6}}$ : 441.40).  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Tablets, with Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid.  

Identification (1) Ferric hydroxide polymaltose complex —Perform the test with Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets as directed under the Analysis for Minerals.  

(2) Folic acid —Perform the test with Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets as directed under the Analysis for Vitamins.  

Disintegration Meets the requirements. Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements. Assay (1) Ferric hydroxide polymaltose complex —Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets, then powder, and perform the test as directed under the Analysis for Minerals.  

(2) Folic acid —Weigh accurately the mass of NLT 20 Ferric Hydroxide Polymaltose Complex and Folic Acid Tablets, and perform the test as directed under the Analysis for Vitamins.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers. Ferrous fumarate $\mathrm{C_{4}H_{2}F e O_{4}:169.90}$ Iron(II) $(E)$ -but-2-enedioate [ 141-01-5 ]Ferrous fumarate, when dried, contains NLT $97.0\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of ferrous fumarate $\left({\bf C}_{4}\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{FeO}_{4}\right)$ .  

![](images/0c4688960f797af6f671c72af684b12dec28d68c96500b504084c92df4da6478.jpg)  

Description Ferrous fumarate occurs as an orange to reddish brown powder and is odorless.   
It is slightly soluble in water and very slightly soluble in ethanol(95).  

The solubility of Ferrous Fumarate in dilute hydrochloric acid is decreased by separation of fumarate.  

Identification (1) Add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2) to $1.5\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous fumarate, add water to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ , and heat until the solution completely dissolves. After cooling, filter using a glass filter, wash the precipitate with diluted hydrochloric acid (3 in 100), and dry at $105\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ . Determine the infrared spectra of this precipitate and fumarate RS as directed in the potassium bromide disk method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wave numbers.  

(2) The filtrate obtained in (1) responds to the Qualitative Analysis for ferrous salt.  

Purity (1) Sulfate —Put $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Fumarate in a $250{\-}{\bmod{L}}$ beaker, add $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, and heat on a steam bath while adding hydrochloric acid dropwise until the solution completely dissolves (about $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid is consumed). Filter, if necessary, and add water to the filtrate to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ . Heat this solution to boiling, add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of barium chloride TS, heat for 2 hours on a steam bath, put a lid, and allow to stand for 16 hours. If crystals of ferrous fumarate form, dissolve by heating the solution on a steam bath. Filter the solution with filter paper for assay, add ammonium sulfide TS to the filtrate, and wash with warm water until the black precipitate is no longer produced. Transfer the residue into a crucible, previously weighed along with the filter paper, carbonize the filter paper without burning, and ignite the crucible and its contents at $600\;^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ to a constant mass. $1~\mathrm{mg}$ of the residue corresponds to $0.412\,\mathrm{~mg}$ of sulfate $\mathrm{(SO_{4})}$ (NMT $0.2\%$ ).  

(2) Arsenic —Put $2.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Fumarate in a beaker and add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water and $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of sulfuric acid. Heat the fumaric acid and precipitate completely, cool, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and filter in a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask. Wash the precipitate with water, combine the washings in a volumetric flask, and add water to the gauge line to mix. Use $25.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution as the test solution and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $3.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of arsenic standard solution (NMT $3\;\mathrm{ppm}$ ). (3) Ferric ion —Weigh accurately about $2.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Fumarate, put in a $250{\-}{\bmod{L}}$ Erlenmeyer flask with a stopper, add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $4~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, and heat on a hot plate until it completely dissolves. Stopper and cool to room temperature. Add $3{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of potassium iodide, stopper, shake to mix, and allow to stand for 5 minutes in the dark. Remove the stopper, add $75~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, then titrate with $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate solution (indicator $:\,3\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of starch TS). NMT 7.16 of 0.1 mol/L sodium thiosulfate is consumed (NMT $2.0\%$ ).  

(4) Mercury— Proceed with the following procedure using a light-resistant container. Weigh accurately about $1{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Ferrous Fumarate, add $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 10), and dissolve while heating on a steam bath. Cool quickly in an ice bath and filter using a filter washed with pre-diluted nitric acid (1 in 10) and water. To the filtrate, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4) and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride TS, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, prepare the control solution with $3.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of mercury standard solution, $30\;\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 4), $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4) and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride. Add ammonia TS to the control solution to adjust the pH to 1.8, and adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ of the test solution to 1.8 with sulfuric acid, and transfer each to a separatory funnel. Perform the test with the test solution and the control solution as directed below. Extract 2 times using $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of dithizone solution for extraction and then $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform, and transfer the chloroform extract to another separatory funnel. To the extract, add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2), shake to mix, allow to stand, and then discard the chloroform layer. Wash the acid-extract with $3\,\textrm{m L}$ of chloroform and discard the washings. Add $0.1~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt solution (1 in 50) and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of $6\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ acetic acid, mix, and slowly add $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia TS. Close the lid of the separatory funnel, cool it under running cold water, open the lid, and transfer the contents into a beaker. Adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ of the test solution and the control solution to 1.8 in the same way as the above, and transfer them to separatory funnels again. Add $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted dithizone solution for extraction, shake vigorously to mix, and allow to stand. Compare the color of the chloroform layers of the test solution and the control solution using a diluted dithizone solution for extraction as a control solution; the color obtained from the test solution is not more intense than that from the control solution (NMT 3 ppm).  

Mercury standard stock solution —Transfer 135.4 mg of mercury(II) chloride to a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, dissolve in $0.5\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill to the gauge line, and mix. This solution contains $0.1\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of mercury $\mathrm{(Hg)}$ in $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Mercury standard solution —Take $1.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of the mercury standard stock solution immediately before use, put in a $1000{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, add $0.5\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill up to the gauge line, and mix. $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution contains $1\ \upmu\mathrm{g}$ of mercury $\mathrm{(Hg)}$ .  

Diluted dithizone solution for extraction —Dilute 5 mL of dithizone solution for extraction with $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform before use.  

(5) Lead —Put $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Fumarate in a 50- mL beaker, add $6~\mathrm{mL}$ of nitric acid and $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of perchloric acid, cover with a watch glass, and heat to evaporate until completely dry. Cool, then dissolve the residue by adding $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of $9~\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid, and then use about $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water to transfer to a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask. Add $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of ascorbic acid-sodium iodide TS and $5.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of trioctylphosphine oxide solution, shake for 30 seconds to mix, and allow to stand to separate. Then, add water so that the organic solvent layer reaches the neck portion of the flask, shake to mix again, and allow to stand to separate. Use the organic solvent layer as the test solution. Separately, take $5\mathrm{mL}$ of lead standard solution, and add water to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . Pipet $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution and put in a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ beaker. To this beaker and a beaker for blank test, add $6\;\mathrm{mL}$ of nitric acid and 10 mL of perchloric acid, and heat to evaporate to dryness. Cool, dissolve the residue in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of $9~\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid, and use about $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water to transfer to $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ flasks, respectively. To each flask, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of ascorbic acid-sodium iodide TS and 5.0 mL of trioctylphosphine oxide solution, shake for 30 seconds to mix, and allow to stand to separate. Then add water so that the organic solvent layer reaches the neck portion of the flask, shake to mix again, allow to stand to separate. Use the organic solvent layers as the standard solution $(2.0\ \upmu\mathrm{g/mL)}$ and the blank test solution, respectively. Perform the test with the test solution and the standard solution as directed under Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy according to the following conditions; the absorbance of the test solution is not greater than that of the standard solution (NMT $0.001\%$ ). Use 4-methyl-2- pentanone to adjust absorbance to 0; the absorbance of the blank test solution is NMT $20\%$ of the difference between the absorbance of the standard solution and the absorbance of the blank test solution.  

Gas: Air–acetylene   
Lamp: Lead hollow-cathode lamp   
Wavelength: $283.3\;\mathrm{nm}$  

Trioctylphosphine oxdie solution —Dissolve $5.0~\mathrm{g}$ of trioctylphosphine oxide in 4-methyl-2-pentanone to make $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

(6) Cadmium —Weigh $2.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Fumarate and dissolve in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid and $80\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and heat gently as needed. After cooling, filter as needed, add water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, pipet $2.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of cadmium standard solution, add hydrochloric acid to make exactly $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with the test solution and the standard solutions as directed under Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy according to the following conditions; the absorbance of the test solution is NMT that of the standard solution (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

Gas: Air–acetylene   
Lamp: Cadmium hollow-cathode lamp   
Wavelength: $228.8\;\mathrm{nm}$  

# Loss on drying NMT $1.5\%$ ($\mathrm{~l~g,~}105~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ , 16 hours).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.15\ \mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Fumarate, previously dried, add $7.5\ \ \mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid, dissolve by heating and cool, then add $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and immediately titrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS (indicator $:0.1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of ferroin TS). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS $=16.990\;\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C}_{4}\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{FeO}_{4}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

# Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate 글루콘산제일철수화물  

![](images/0d6ccfccf8832c3a32520cbbdc5afa626bd8fabfa95f55aeea75e8190e6a3c9d.jpg)  

Ferrous Gluconate $\mathrm{C_{12}H_{22}F e O_{14}{\cdot}2H_{2}O:482.17}$ $\mathrm{Iron}(2\!+\!);(2R,3S,\!4R,5R)\!-\!2,\!3,\!4,\!5,\!6-$ pentahydroxyhexanoate; dihydrate [ 6047-12-7 ]  

Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate contains NLT $97.0\%$ and NMT $102.0\%$ of ferrous gluconate $\left({\bf C}_{12}{\bf H}_{22}{\mathrm{FeO}}_{14}\right.$ 446.14), calculated on the dried basis.  

Description Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate occurs as a yellowish gray or light yellowish green fine powder or granule with a faint odor of burning sugar.  

$1.0\;\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate dissolves in $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of warm water and is practically insoluble in ethanol(95). Its aqueous solution (1 in 20) is acidic.  

Identification (1) Weigh $10~\mathrm{{mg}}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate and dissolve in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water to use it as the test solution. If necessary, warm it in a $60~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ water bath. Separately, dissolve $10~\mathrm{mg}$ of ferrous gluconate hydrate RS in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and use this solution as the standard solution. Perform the test with these solutions as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $5~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on a thin-layer chromatographic plate made of silica gel for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of ethanol(95), water. ammonia water(28) and ethyl acetate $(50:30:10:10)$ as a developing solvent to a distance of about $15~\mathrm{cm}$ , dry the plate at $110\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 20 minutes, and cool it. Dissolve $2.5\mathrm{~g~}$ of ammonium heptamolybdate tetrahydrate in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of $1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sulfuric acid, add $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of cerium sulfate, shake to dissolve, and add $1~\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid to make $100\ \mathrm{mL}$ . Spray this solution evenly on the plate and heat at $110\mathrm{~}^{\circ}\mathrm{~C~}$ for 10 minutes; the color and $R_{\mathrm{f}}$ values of the spots obtained from the test and standard solutions are the same.  

(2) Add potassium hexacyanoferrate(III) TS to the aqueous solution of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate (1 in 200); a dark blue precipitate is formed.  

Purity (1) Chloride —Proceed with $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.02\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ hydrochloric acid (NMT $0.07\%$ ).  

(2) Sulfate —Proceed with $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of $0.01\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid (NMT $0.1\%$ ).  

(3) Oxalic acid —Dissolve $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate in $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, extract each with $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ and $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of ether, and combine all the extracts. To the combined extracts, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and evaporate ether on a steam bath. Add 1 drop of $6~\mathrm{mol/L}$ acetic acid and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of calcium acetate hydrate solution (1 in 20); the solution does not become turbid within 5 minutes.  

(4) Lead —Weigh $1.0\textbf{g}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate, put it in $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of 9 mol/L hydrochloric acid, about $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, $20\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ascorbic acid-sodium iodide TS, and $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of 4-methyl-2- pentanone solution of trioctylphosphine oxide (5 in 100), shake for 30 seconds, and allow to stand until the layers separate. Next, add water to the neck of the volumetric flask, shake it again, and allow it to stand. Take the organic solvent layer and use it as the test solution. Separately, put exactly $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of lead nitrate standard stock solution into a volumetric flask, dilute with water to make $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , transfer exactly $2.0\ \mathrm{mL}$ of this solution into a volumetric flask, and then prepare the standard solution in the same way as the test solution. Perform the test with the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy according to the following conditions; the absorbance of the test solution is less than that of the standard solution (NMT $0.001\%$ ).  

Gas: Air–acetylene   
Lamp: Lead hollow-cathode lamp   
Wavelength: $283.8\;\mathrm{nm}$  

(5) Mercury —Proceed with the following procedure using a light-resistant container. Weigh accurately about $1{\mathrm{~g~}}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate, add $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 10), and dissolve while heating on a steam bath. Cool quickly in an ice bath and filter using a filter washed with pre-diluted nitric acid (1 in 10) and water. To the filtrate, add $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4) and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride TS and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, prepare the control solution with $3.0\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of mercury standard solution, $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 4), 5 mL of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4) and $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride. Put the test solution and the control solution each into a separatory funnel, adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 1.8 using sulfuric acid, extract twice with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of dithizone solution for extraction and then with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform, and transfer the chloroform extract to another separatory funnel. To the extract, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2), shake to mix, allow to stand, and then discard the chloroform layer. Wash the acidextract with $3\ \mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform and discard the solution used for washing. Add $0.1\,\mathrm{~mL~}$ of ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt solution (1 in 50) and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of $6\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ acetic acid, mix, and slowly add $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia TS. Close the lid of the separatory funnel, cool it under running cold water, open the lid, and transfer the contents into a beaker. Adjust the pH of the test solution and the control solution to 1.8 in the same way as the above, and transfer them to separatory funnels again. Add 5.0 mL of diluted dithizone solution for extraction, shake vigorously, and allow to stand. Compare the color of the chloroform layers of the test solution and the control solution using a diluted dithizone solution for extraction as a control solution; the color obtained from the test solution is not more intense than that from the control solution (NMT 3 ppm).  

Mercury standard stock solution —Transfer 135.4 mg of mercury(II) chloride into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, dissolve in $0.5\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill up to the gauge line, and mix. This solution contains $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of mercury $\mathrm{(Hg)}$ in $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Mercury standard solution —Before use, take 1.0 mL of the mercury standard stock solution, put it in a $1000{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, add $0.5\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill up to the gauge line, and mix. $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution contains $1~\upmu\mathrm{g}$ of mercury $\mathrm{(Hg)}$ .  

Before using diluted dithizone solution for extraction, dilute $5\;\mathrm{mL}$ of dithizone solution for extraction with $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform.  

(6) Ferric ion —Weigh accurately about $5\textrm{g}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate and dissolve it in a mixture of $100\ \mathrm{mL}$ of water and $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of hydrochloric acid, and add $3.0\mathrm{~g~}$ of potassium iodide. Shake well to mix and allow to stand in the dark place for 5 minutes. Then, titrate any free iodine with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate VS (indicator: $3\;\mathrm{mL}$ of starch TS). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction (NMT $2.0\%$ ).  

exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ . To $5\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution, add $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of Ferring's TS, and boil for 1 minute; a red precipitate is not formed within 1 minute.  

Loss on drying Between $6.5\%$ and $10.0\%$ $(1~\mathrm{g},~105~^{\circ}\mathrm{C},$ ,16 hours).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $1.5\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate, put it in a $300{\mathrm{-mL}}$ Erlenmeyer flask, and dissolve in a mixture of $75~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $15~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid. Add $0.25\mathrm{~g~}$ of zinc powder, stopper the flask with a Bunsen valve, and allow to stand at room temperature for 20 minutes or until the solution becomes colorless. Filter the solution through a filtering crucible (Gooch crucible) containing an asbestos mat coated with a thin layer of zinc dust, and wash the crucible and the contents with $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid and then with $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of water. To the filtrate, add 1,10-phenanthroline monohydrate TS, and immediately titrate the filtrate with $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS in a suction flask. Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ferrous Gluconate Tablets 글루콘산제일철정  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ sodium thiosulfate VS $=5.585~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{Fe}^{+3}$  

Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate solution $=44.61~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C_{12}H_{22}F e O_{14}}$  

(7) Arsenic —Weigh $1.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate, put it in $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ round bottom flask, add $40\;\mathrm{mL}$ of $4.5~\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of potassium bromide solution (3 in 10), and connect it to a distillation device equipped with an ice water cooler. Heat the test sample to dissolve and start distillation. Perform the test using $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of the distillate as the test solution (NMT 3 ppm).  

(8) Reducing sugars —Weigh $0.5~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate, dissolve it in $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, slightly warm it up, and add $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia TS to make it alkaline. Precipitate iron through hydrogen sulfide in this solution, allow to stand for 30 minutes, filter, and wash the precipitate twice with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of water. Then, combine the filtrate and the solution used for washing, make the combined solution acidic with hydrochloric acid, and add another $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute hydrochloric acid. Boil this solution until the steam does not turn the lead acetate paper black, and if necessary, boil further to concentrate to about $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ . After cooling, add $5\ \mathrm{mL}$ of sodium carbonate TS and $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, filter, wash the residue with water, combine the filtrate and the solution used for washing, add water to make the combined solution to Ferrous Gluconate Tablets contains NLT $93.0\%$ and NMT $107.0\%$ of the labeled amount of ferrous gluconate hydrate $(\mathrm{C_{12}H_{22}F e O_{14}}\mathrm{\cdot2H_{2}O}:482.17)$ .  

Method of preparation Prepare Ferrous Gluconate Tablets as directed under Tablets, with Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate.  

Identification Powder Ferrous Gluconate Tablets, weigh an appropriate amount of the powder, equivalent to $1\ \mathrm{g}$ of ferrous gluconate hydrate, according to the labeled amount, dissolve in $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and filter. Take an appropriate amount of the filtrate, add water, dilute it to the corresponding concentration, and perform the test as directed under the Identification for Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate.  

Dissolution Perform the test with 1 tablet of Ferrous Gluconate Tablets at 150 revolutions per minute according to Method 1 under the dissolution using $900~\mathrm{mL}$ of dissolution medium 1. Take the dissolved solution 80 minutes after the start of the dissolution, filter it, and use the filtrate as the test solution. If necessary, dilute the test solution to a suitable concentration using the dissolution medium. Separately, weigh accurately an appropriate amount of ferrous gluconate hydrate RS, dissolve in the dissolution medium, and prepare the standard solution containing the same concentration of iron as the test solution. Determine the absorbances of the test solution and the standard solution according to the following conditions, as directed under the Atomic Absorption Spectroscopy, and calculate the content of iron using the calibration curve obtained from the absorbance of the standard solution.  

Gas: Air–acetylene   
Lamp: Iron hollow-cathode lamp   
Wavelength: 248.3 nm  

It meets the requirements when the dissolution rate of Ferrous Gluconate Tablets in 80 minutes is NLT $80\%$ .  

# Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements.  

Assay Weigh accurately NLT 20 tablet of Ferrous Gluconate Tablets and powder them. Weigh accurately an appropriate amount of the powder equivalent to about 1.5 g of ferrous gluconate hydrate $(\mathrm{C_{12}H_{22}F e O_{14}{\cdot}2H_{2}O)}$ , put in a $300{\mathrm{-mL}}$ Erlenmeyer flask, dissolve in a mixture of $75~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $15~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid, and hereinafter proceed as directed under the Assay of Ferrous Gluconate Hydrate.  

Each mL of $0.1\ \mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS $=48.22~\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{C_{12}H_{22}F e O_{14}{\cdot}2H_{2}O}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate 황산철수화물  

Ferrous Sulfate FeSO 4 ·7H 2 O: 278.02 Iron $(2+)$ sulfate heptahydrate [ 7782-63-0 ]  

Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate contains NLT $98.0\%$ and NMT $104.0\%$ of ferrous sulfate hydrate $\mathrm{(FeSO_{4}{\cdot}7H_{2}O)}$ ). Description Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate occurs as pale green crystals or a crystalline powder. It is odorless and astringent.  

It is freely soluble in water and practically insoluble in ether. It easily effloresces in dry air, and its crystal surface changes to yellowish brown in the humid air.  

Identification An aqueous solution of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate (1 in 10) responds to the Qualitative Analysis for ferrous salt and sulfate.  

Purity (1) Clarity and color of solution ―Dissolve $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate in $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of water and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid; the resulting solution is clear.  

(2) Acid —To $5.0\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of powdered Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate, add $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethanol(95), shake for 2 minutes, and filter. To $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of the filtrate, add $50\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, 3 drops of bromothymol blue TS, and $0.5~\mathrm{~mL}$ of dilute sodium hydroxide TS; the resulting solution exhibits a blue color.  

(3) Mercury —Perform the test using a lightresistant container. Weigh accurately about $1~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate, add $30\,\textrm{m L}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 10), and dissolve while heating on a steam bath. Cool quickly in an ice bath and filter using a filter washed with pre-diluted nitric acid (1 in 10) and water. To the filtrate, add $20\;\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4) and $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride TS, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, prepare the control solution with $3.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of mercury standard solution, $30~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted nitric acid (1 in 4), $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of sodium citrate solution (1 in 4), and $1\ \mathrm{mL}$ of hydroxylamine hydrochloride. To the control solution, add ammonia TS to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 1.8. To the test solution, add sulfuric acid to adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ to 1.8. Transfer each solution into two separation funnels. Perform the test with the test solution and the control solution as follows. Extract 2 times each with $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of extracting dithizone solution and $5\,\textrm{m L}$ of chloroform, transfer chloroform extract into another separation funnel. To the extract, add $10\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of diluted hydrochloric acid (1 in 2), shake to mix, allow to stand, and then discard the chloroform layer. Wash the acid extract with 3 mL of chloroform and discard the solution used for washing. Add $0.1~\mathrm{mL}$ of ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid disodium salt solution (1 in 50) and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of $6~\mathrm{mol/L}$ acetic acid, mix, and slowly add $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of ammonia TS. Close the lid of the separatory funnel, cool it under running cold water, open the lid, and transfer the contents into a beaker. Adjust the $\mathrm{pH}$ of the test solution and the control solution to 1.8 in the same way as the above, and transfer them to separatory funnels again. Add $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of diluted dithizone solution for extraction, shake vigorously, and allow to stand. Compare the color of the chloroform layers of the test solution and the control solution using a diluted dithizone solution for extraction as a control solution; the color obtained from the test solution is not more intense than that from the control solution (NMT 3 ppm). Mercury standard stock solution —Transfer 135.4 mg of mercury(II) chloride into a $100{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, dissolve in $0.5\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill up to the gauge line, and mix. This solution contains $0.1~\mathrm{g}$ of mercury $\mathrm{(Hg)}$ in $100\;\mathrm{mL}$ .  

Mercury standard solution —Before use, take 1.0 mL of the mercury standard stock solution, transfer into a $1000{\mathrm{-mL}}$ volumetric flask, add $0.5\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ sulfuric acid TS, fill up to the gauge line, and mix. $1~\mathrm{mL}$ of this solution contains $1\ \upmu\mathrm{g}$ of mercury $\left(\mathrm{Hg}\right)$ .  

Diluted dithizone solution for extraction —Before use, dilute $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of dithizone solution for extraction with $25~\mathrm{mL}$ of chloroform.  

(4) Lead —Transfer about $1.0\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate into a $50{\-}\mathrm{mL}$ volumetric flask, add $10~\mathrm{mL}$ of 9 mol/L hydrochloric acid, about $10\;\mathrm{mL}$ of water, $20\;\mathrm{mL}$ of ascorbic acid-sodium iodide TS, and $5~\mathrm{mL}$ of a solution of 4-methyl-2-pentanone solution in trioctylphosphine oxide (5 in 100), shake for 30 seconds, and allow to stand until the layers separate. Next, add water to the neck of the volumetric flask, shake it again, and allow to stand. Take the organic solvent layer and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, transfer exactly $5.0~\mathrm{mL}$ of lead nitrate standard stock solution into a volumetric flask, dilute with water to make $100~\mathrm{{mL}}$ , transfer exactly 2.0 mL of this solution into a volumetric flask, and proceed in the same manner as the test solution. Use this solution as the standard solution. Determine the absorbances of the test solution and the standard solution according to the following conditions, as directed under Ultravioletvisible Spectrophotometry; the absorbance of the solution obtained from the test solution is not greater than that from the standard solution.  

Gas: Air–acetylene   
Lamp: Lead hollow-cathode lamp   
Wavelength: 283.8 nm  

(5) Arsenic —Prepare the test solution with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate, according to Method 1, and perform the test (NMT 2 ppm).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $0.7\ \mathrm{g}$ of Ferrous Sulfate Hydrate, add $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of water, $20\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid TS, and $2~\mathrm{mL}$ of phosphoric acid, and titrate immediately with $0.02\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium permanganate VS. Each mL of $0.02\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ potassium permanganate VS $=27.80\ \mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{FeSO}_{4}{\cdot}7\mathrm{H}_{2}\mathrm{O}$  

Packaging and storage Preserve in tight containers.  

# Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules 건조황산제일철·폴산· $\lambda|\mathfrak{o}\mathfrak{h}$ 노코발라민·DL-세린캡슐  

Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules contain ferrous sulfate $\mathrm{(FeSO_{4}}$ :151.90) equivalent to NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $110.0\%$ of the labeled amount, folic acid $\mathrm{(C_{19}H_{19}N_{7}O_{6}}$ : 441.40) and cyanocobalamin $\mathrm{(C_{63}N_{88}C o_{14}O_{14}P}$ : 1355.37) equivalent to NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $150.0\%$ of the labeled amount, and DL-serine $\mathrm{(C_{3}H_{7}N O_{3}}$ : 105.10) NLT $90.0\%$ and NMT $130.0\%$ of the labeled amount.  

Method of preparation Prepare as directed under Capsules, with Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine.  

Identification (1) Ferrous sulfate ―Weigh an amount of the contents of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules, equivalent to $0.25~\mathrm{g}$ of ferrous sulfate according to the labeled amount, add water and hydrochloric acid to acidify, and add water again to make $50~\mathrm{mL}$ ; the solution responds to the Qualitative Analysis for ferrous salt and sulfate.  

(2) Folic acid ―Perform the test with the contents of 5 capsules of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules as directed under the Analysis for Vitamins.  

(3) Cyanocobalamin ―Perform the test with the contents of 5 capsules of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules as directed under the Analysis for Vitamins.  

(4) DL-serine ―Add the contents of 5 capsules of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules to a G4 glass filter, and wash several times with petroleum ether until the fat of the residue is completely removed. Carefully dry the residue at $65\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}_{!}$ ,dissolve in $50~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and use this solution as the test solution. Separately, dissolve $0.13~\mathrm{g}$ of DL-serine RS in $100~\mathrm{mL}$ of water, and use this solution as the standard solution. With these solutions, perform the test as directed under the Thin Layer Chromatography. Spot $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution on a plate made of silica gel with fluorescence indicator for thin-layer chromatography. Next, develop the plate with a mixture of methanol and water $(70:30)$ as the developing solvent to a distance of about $10~\mathrm{cm}$ , and air-dry the plate. Spray ninhydrin-ethanol solution evenly on the plate, and heat at $100~^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ for 10 minutes; the $R_{f}$ values of the spots obtained from the test and standard solutions are the same.  

Disintegration Meets the requirements.  

# Uniformity of dosage units Meets the requirements.  

Assay (1) Ferrous sulfate ―Weigh accurately the mass of the contents of NLT 20 capsules of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules. Weigh accurately about $0.4\,\mathrm{~g~}$ of ferrous sulfate $\mathrm{(FeSO_{4})}$ , dissolve in a mixture of $20\ \mathrm{~mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid and $80~\mathrm{mL}$ of freshly boiled and cooled water, and filter. Wash the beaker and the residue on the filter paper with a small amount of the mixture of $20~\mathrm{mL}$ of dilute sulfuric acid and $80\,\textrm{m L}$ of freshly boiled and cooled water, combine the washings with the filtrate, and immediately titrate with $0.1\,\mathrm{\mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS (indicator: $o$ -Phenanthroline TS). Perform a blank test in the same manner and make any necessary correction.  

# Each mL of $0.1\;\mathrm{mol/L}$ cerium sulfate VS $=15.190\;\mathrm{mg}$ of $\mathrm{FeSO_{4}}$  

(2) Folic acid and cyanocobalamin ―Weigh accurately the mass of the contents of NLT 20 tablets of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DLSerine Capsules and perform the test as directed under the Analysis for Vitamins.  

(3) DL-serine ―Weigh accurately the mass of the contents of NLT 20 tablets of Dried Ferrous Sulfate, Folic Acid, Cyanocobalamin and DL-Serine Capsules and perform the test as directed under the Identification and Assay for Amino Acids.  

Packaging and storage Preserve in well-closed containers.  

Finasteride, dissolve in a mixture of acetonitrile and water $(1:1)$ to make exactly $100~\mathrm{mL}$ , and use this solution as the test solution. Perform the test with $15\ \upmu\mathrm{L}$ of the test solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, determine the peak areas according to the automatic integration method, and calculate the amount of each related substance; it is NMT $0.5\%$ , and total amount of all related substances is NMT $1.0\%$ .

# Finasteride 피나스테리드  

![](images/f230548d7b8c4c8a2b29f7790436b50beb112a921b44f0d36150b9cc36aed60f.jpg)  

Finasteride $\mathrm{C}_{23}\mathrm{H}_{36}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathrm{O}_{2}$ : 372.54 $(1S,3\mathrm{a}S,3\mathrm{b}S,5\mathrm{a}R,9\mathrm{a}R,9\mathrm{b}S,11\mathrm{a}S)$ -N-tert -Butyl-9a, 11adimethyl-7-oxo-1,2,3,3a,3b,4,5,5a,6,9b,10,11- dodecahydroindeno[5,4-f]quinoline-1-carboxamide [98319-26-7 ]  

Finasteride contains NLT $98.5\%$ and NMT $101.0\%$ of finasteride $(\mathbf{C}_{23}\mathrm{H}_{36}\mathrm{N}_{2}\mathbf{O}_{2}$ : 372.55), calculated on the anhydrous basis.  

Description Finasteride occurs as a white or grayish white crystalline solid.  

It is freely soluble in ethanol(95) or chloroform, and very slightly soluble in water.  

Melting point —About $257\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ Identification (1) Determine the infrared spectra of Finasteride and finasteride RS, as directed in the paste method under the Mid-infrared Spectroscopy; both spectra exhibit similar intensities of absorption at the same wavenumbers.  

(2) The retention time of the major peak of the test solution corresponds to that of the standard solution, as obtained in the Assay.  

Optical rotation $[\alpha]_{405\mathrm{nm}}^{25}$ : Between $-56.0^{\circ}$ and $-60.0^{\circ}$ $_{(0.1\mathrm{~g~}}$ calculated on the anhydrous basis, methanol, 10 mL, $100\;\mathrm{mm}$ ).  

Purity (1) Heavy metals —Proceed with $1.0~\mathrm{g}$ of Finasteride according to Method 2 and perform the test. Prepare the control solution with $1.0\,\mathrm{\mL}$ of lead standard solution (NMT $10\,\mathrm{ppm})$ ).  

(2) Related substances— Weigh accurately $0.1\ \mathrm{g}$ of  

$$
=\,100\times{\frac{A_{\mathrm{i}}}{A_{\mathrm{S}}}}
$$  

# $A_{\mathrm{i}}$ : Peak area of each related substance  

$A_{S}$ : Total area of peaks obtained from the test solution  

Operating conditions  

Detector: An ultraviolet absorption photometer (wavelength: $210\;\mathrm{nm})$ .  

Column: A stainless steel column about $4.6~\mathrm{mm}$ in internal diameter and $30\;\mathrm{cm}$ in length, packed with octadecylsilanized silica gel for liquid chromatography ( ${}^{4}\ensuremath{\,\upmu\mathrm{m}}$ in particle diameter).  

Mobile phase: A mixture of water, tetrahydrofuran and acetonitrile $(8:1:1)$ .  

Column temperature: A constant temperature of about $60\ ^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ .  

Flow rate: About $1.5\;\mathrm{mL/min}$ System suitability

Proceed with $15~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ of this solution according to the above conditions; the number of theoretical plates and the symmetry factor of the peak of finasteride are NLT 10000 plates and NMT 1.3, respectively.  

Water NMT $0.3\%$ ($1{\mathrm{~g~}}$ , volumetric titration, direct titration).  

# Residue on ignition NMT $0.1\%$ (1 g).  

Assay Weigh accurately about $20~\mathrm{mg}$ each of Finasteride and finasteride RS, dissolve in a mixture of water and acetonitrile (1 in 1) to make exactly $100\,\mathrm{\mL}$ , and use these solutions as the test solution and the standard solution, respectively. Perform the test with $10~\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the test solution and the standard solution as directed under the Liquid Chromatography according to the following conditions, and determine the peak areas of finasteride, $A_{\mathrm{T}}$ and $A_{S}$ , from each solution.

System repeatability: Repeat the test 5 times with  

$10\,\upmu\mathrm{L}$ each of the standard solution according to the above conditions; the relative standard deviation of the peak area is NMT $1.0\%$ .
